Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Conditional Ila': Penalties and Temporary vs. Permanent Vows
Explains the ruling when the husband attaches conditions like Hajj or divorce to the vow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Ila' when the husband attaches a conditional penalty such as Hajj or divorce, and distinguish between temporary and permanent vows in their effect after remarriage.

Core Idea
A conditional vow with a difficult penalty counts as Ila', but its effect after divorce depends on whether the vow is temporary or permanent.

In this lesson, we examine how the Hanafi school treats Ila' when the husband combines his vow of abstinence with a conditional penalty, such as 'upon me is Hajj' or 'you are divorced'. The key is that such a vow is valid Ila' if the penalty is difficult, and it carries the same four-month waiting period. However, the fate of the oath after divorce differs based on whether it was limited to a specific period or was open-ended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional vow and its penalty
Look at the husband's statement: he attaches a condition like 'upon me is Hajj' or 'you are divorced' to his abstinence. Recognize that this is a conditional Ila'.
The penalty may be an act of worship, charity, or a legal consequence like divorce.
2
Determine if the penalty constitutes difficulty (mashaqqa)
The Hanafi school requires that the penalty be something difficult, like Hajj, fasting, or freeing a slave. Easy acts like two rak'ahs do not qualify. This step is crucial for validity.
The text mentions that one hundred rak'ahs would be difficult, but two rak'ahs are not.
3
Apply the four-month Ila' rule
The conditional vow is treated as a valid Ila': if the husband approaches within four months, the penalty becomes due; if he refrains for four months, one ba'in divorce occurs automatically.
This is the same rule as for standard Ila' without a condition.
4
Distinguish temporary vs. permanent oaths
If the oath was temporary (e.g., 'for four months'), after the ba'in divorce and remarriage, the oath is nullified – no further consequences. If the oath was permanent ('forever'), the oath remains in effect, and another four-month abstinence triggers another divorce.
This distinction is essential for understanding the long-term effect.
5
Conclude the consequence
If he breaks the vow by approaching, the penalty (jaza') is obligatory. If he refrains for four months without breaking, a ba'in divorce occurs. The oath then falls for temporary vows but not for permanent ones.
The penalty is distinct from kaffarah (expiation of an oath) because the vow was not by Allah.

أو إن قربتك فعلي حجّ ، أو صوم، أو صدقة ، أو فأنت طالق ، أو عبدي حرّ، فقد آلى إن قربها في المدة حيث، وتجب الكفارة في الحلف بالله تعالى، وفي غيره الجزاء، وسقط الإيلاء. وإلا بانت بواحدة ، وسقط الحلف المؤقت لا المؤبد. [١] قوله : (أو إن قربتك فعلي حج، أو صوم ، أو صدقة)، أو فأنتِ طالق ، أو عبدي حر، فقد آلى إن قربها في المدَّة حيث، وتجب الكفارة في الحلف بالله تعالى، وفي غيره الجزاء، وسقط الإيلاء. وإلا بانـت بواحدة : أي إن لم يقربها بانت بطلقة واحدة، وسقط الحلف المؤقت لا المؤيد : حتى لو كان الحلف مؤقتاً بأربعة أشهر، ولم يقربها بانت بواحدة، وسقط الحلفُ حتى لو نكحها فلم يقربها بعد ذلك لا تبين ، أما في الحلف المؤبد إن نكحها ولم يقربها أربعة أشهر تبين ثانياً، ثُمَّ إن نكحها حنث تجب الكفارة وينزل الجزاء. [1] قوله : وفي غيره ؛ أي في غير الحلف بالله يجب الجزاء، وهو الحج والصومُ مثلاً، وتطلق هي أو يعتق عبده، وبالجملة : ينزل الجزاء الذي علق بوطئه لتحقق الشرط. [٢] قوله : وسقط الإيلاء ؛ أي بطل، فلو مضت أربعة أشهر لا يقع الطلاق. [٣] قوله : وسقط الحلف ؛ يعني عند وطئها في المدّة يسقط الإيلاء، وعند عدمه ووقوع البائنة بمضي المدة يسقط الإيلاء المؤقت بأربعة أشهر دون المؤبد. [٤] قوله : حتى ... الخ ؛ تفريع على سقوط الحلف، يعني لما لم يطأ في المدة ووقع الطلاق البائن بمضي المدة سقط ذلك الحلف ، فلو نكح تلك المرأة بعد العدة أو فيها فلم يطأها أربعة أشهر أو فصاعداً ، لا يقعُ عليها الطلاق البائن ؛ لأنَّ الحلف السابق لم يبق حتى يبقى أثره. [0] قوله : تبين ثانياً ؛ الوجه في ذلك أنّ اليمين ترتفع بالحنث مؤقتاً كانت أو (أو نحوه مما يشق ، بخلاف فعلي صلاة ركعتين، فليس بمول لعدم مشقتهما، بخلاف فعلي مئة ركعة، وقياسه أن يكون مولياً بمئة ختمة أو اتباع مئة جنازة ولم أره. ينظر : «الدر المختار»(۲ : .(٥٤٨)
Or if he said: 'If I approach you, then upon me is Hajj, or fasting, or charity, or you are divorced, or my slave is free', then he has made Ila' if he approaches her during the period such that expiation becomes obligatory if he swore by Allah, and in other cases the penalty is due, and the Ila' falls. Otherwise she becomes separated by one divorce, and the temporary oath falls but not the permanent one. [1] He said: 'Or if I approach you, then upon me is Hajj, or fasting, or charity, or you are divorced, or my slave is free', then he has made Ila' if he approaches her during the period such that expiation becomes obligatory if he swore by Allah, and in other cases the penalty is due, and the Ila' falls. And 'otherwise she becomes separated by one divorce' i.e., if he does not approach her, she is separated by one divorce, and the temporary oath falls but not the permanent one: even if the oath was temporary for four months and he did not approach her, she is separated by one divorce, and the oath falls such that if he later marries her and does not approach her for another four months, she does not become separated. As for the permanent oath, if he marries her and does not approach her for four months, she becomes separated a second time; then if he marries her and then breaks the oath by approaching, expiation becomes obligatory and the penalty is incurred. [1] He said: 'and in other than it' i.e., in other than swearing by Allah, the penalty is obligatory, which is Hajj, fasting, etc., and she is divorced or his slave is freed; in short, the penalty that was conditioned upon his intercourse is incurred because the condition is fulfilled. [2] He said: 'and the Ila' falls' i.e., it is nullified; so if four months pass, no divorce occurs. [3] He said: 'and the oath falls' meaning that when he approaches her during the period, the Ila' falls; and when he does not and the ba'in divorce occurs by the passage of time, the temporary Ila' (limited to four months) falls but not the permanent one. [4] He said: 'until... etc.'; this is a branch of the falling of the oath, meaning that when he did not approach during the period and the ba'in divorce occurred by the passage of time, that oath falls; so if he marries that woman after the 'idda or during it and does not approach her for four months or more, the ba'in divorce does not occur upon her because the previous oath no longer remains to have effect. [0] He said: 'she becomes separated a second time'; the reasoning is that the oath is lifted by breaking it, whether temporary or... (or something similar that is difficult, unlike 'upon me is two rak'ahs of prayer' which is not Ila' because there is no difficulty; but if it is something difficult like one hundred rak'ahs, by analogy he would be an muli with one hundred khatmas or following one hundred funerals, but I have not seen this. Refer to 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' 2:548.)
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of Ila' by addressing cases where the husband attaches a conditional penalty to his vow, such as 'upon me is Hajj' or 'you are divorced' if he approaches his wife. The ruling: if the husband makes such a conditional vow, it constitutes Ila' (a valid vow of abstinence) with the same consequences as a regular Ila'—if he approaches his wife during the period, the condition is activated (e.g., he must perform Hajj, or his wife becomes divorced) and the Ila' is lifted; if he does not approach her until the four months expire, a single ba'in divorce occurs. However, there is a key distinction between temporary and permanent oaths: if the oath was temporary (e.g., 'I will not approach you for four months'), then after the ba'in divorce occurs and the 'idda ends, if the husband remarries her, the previous oath no longer applies—he can have intercourse without any consequence. If the oath was permanent (e.g., 'forever'), then after remarriage, if he again abstains for four months, another ba'in divorce occurs. The passage then explains that if the husband swore by something other than Allah (e.g., 'upon me is Hajj'), the penalty for breaking the vow is to fulfill that condition, not the expiation of an oath. The commentator clarifies that 'falling of Ila'' means it is nullified, so if four months pass without intercourse after the Ila' is nullified (e.g., because he approached earlier), no divorce occurs. The falling of the oath means: if he approaches during the period, the Ila' is cancelled; if he does not approach and the ba'in divorce happens, the temporary oath (the specific vow limited to four months) falls completely, while a permanent oath continues to have effect even after remarriage. The last part discusses that for a vow to constitute Ila', the promised penalty must be something difficult (like Hajj, three fasts, etc.); easy actions like two rak'ahs of prayer do not count as Ila'.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza'): The penalty or consequence that becomes obligatory when the husband breaks a conditional vow that was not sworn by Allah; e.g., performing Hajj, fasting, freeing a slave, etc.
حلف مؤقت (hilf mu'aqqat): A vow of abstinence that is restricted to a specific period, such as four months.
حلف مؤبد (hilf mu'abbad): A vow of abstinence that is indefinitely or permanently binding, not limited to a period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his wife: 'If I approach you, then upon me is to fast for one month' and then refrains for four months. What happens according to the Hanafi school?
A) No divorce, but he must fast because he broke his conditional vow.
B) One ba'in divorce occurs, and his vow is void.
C) The marriage continues, but he must pay expiation for breaking his oath.
D) The wife can demand immediate divorce.

Key Takeaway
A conditional vow with a difficult penalty constitutes valid Ila'; if the vow is temporary, it is nullified after divorce and remarriage, while a permanent vow persists.

Talaq — Divorce

Basic Ruling of Ila': Approach or Wait
Commentary on the matn of Ila' explaining the core ruling and the two types of oaths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of a valid ila', describe the two possible outcomes (approach or passage of four months), and differentiate between temporary and perpetual oaths.

Core Idea
An ila' oath ends either by approaching (with expiation) or by four months passing (leading to one irrevocable divorce).

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqaya explains the foundational ruling of ila'. The husband swears an oath not to approach his wife. If he breaks the oath by approaching, he must fulfill the attached condition (kaffarah or other). If he does not approach for four months, the wife becomes irrevocably divorced. The nature of the oath—temporary or perpetual—determines whether the divorce recurs upon remarriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Find the basic scenario: the husband swears an oath not to approach his wife. The act is called ila'. Determine its legal effect: if he approaches within four months, the ila' falls and he must expiate; if not, a bain divorce occurs.
The matn says: 'If he approaches within the period, kaffarah is obligatory if swearing by Allah, and fulfillment of the condition is obligatory otherwise, and the ila' falls. Otherwise she becomes bain with one divorce.'
2
Understand the two possible outcomes
The first outcome: the husband approaches before four months. This breaks the oath and nullifies the ila'. He must either pay kaffarah (if swearing by Allah) or fulfill the condition (e.g., Hajj, freeing a slave). The second outcome: he does not approach for four months. This triggers a single irrevocable divorce (bain).
3
Differentiate temporary vs permanent oaths
A temporary oath (mu'aqqat) has a specified time (e.g., four months). If the period passes without intercourse, the divorce occurs and the oath is nullified permanently. A perpetual oath (mu'abbad) has no time limit; it is only nullified by breaking it (intercourse). Therefore, after a divorce, the oath remains, and if the husband remarries and again does not approach, another divorce occurs.
The passage states: 'the temporary oath bound to four months falls, but not the perpetual.'
4
Note the expiation details
If the husband swears by Allah and then approaches, he must pay kaffarah (like in a regular oath). If he swears by something else (e.g., 'upon me is Hajj'), he must fulfill that specific condition. The commentary clarifies: 'fulfillment is obligatory, such as Hajj or fasting, or she is divorced or his slave is freed.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب الإيلاء

أو إن قربتك فعلي حج، أو صوم، أو صدقة، أو فأنت طالق، أو عبدي حر، فقد آلى إن قربها في المدة حيث، وتجب الكفارة في الحلف بالله تعالى، وفي غيره الجزاء، وسقط الإيلاء. وإلا بانت بواحدة، وسقط الحلف المؤقت لا المؤبد

[1] قوله: وفي غيره؛ أي في غير الحلف بالله يجب الجزاء، وهو الحج والصوم مثلاً، وتطلق هي أو يعتق عبده، وبالجملة: ينزل الجزاء الذي علق بوطئه لتحقق الشرط.

[2] قوله: وسقط الإيلاء؛ أي بطل، فلو مضت أربعة أشهر لا يقع الطلاق.

[3] قوله: وسقط الحلف؛ يعني عند وطئها في المدة يسقط الإيلاء، وعند عدمه ووقوع البائنة بمضي المدة يسقط الإيلاء المؤقت بأربعة أشهر دون المؤبد.

[4] قوله: حتى... الخ؛ تفريع على سقوط الحلف، يعني لما لم يطأ في المدة ووقع الطلاق البائن بمضي المدة سقط ذلك الحلف، فلو نكح تلك المرأة بعد العدة أو فيها فلم يطأها أربعة أشهر أو فصاعداً، لا يقع عليها الطلاق البائن؛ لأن الحلف السابق لم يبق حتى يبقى أثره.

(١) أو نحوه مما يشق، بخلاف فعلي صلاة ركعتين، فليس بمول لعدم مشقتهما، بخلاف فعلي مئة ركعة، وقياسه أن يكون مولياً بمئة ختمة أو اتباع مئة جنازة ولم أره. ينظر : «الدر المختار»(۲ : ٥٤٨)

[0] قوله: تبين ثانياً؛ الوجه في ذلك أن اليمين ترتفع بالحنث مؤقتة كانت أو مؤبدة، وتبطل بمضي الوقت الذي وقتت به، فلبطلان المؤقت صورتان: أحدهما: الحنث. وأخرهما مضي الوقت. وأما المؤبد فلا يرتفع إلا بالحنث إذ لا وقت هناك يبطل بمضيه، فإذا قال: والله لا أقربك أو قال: والله لا أقربك أبداً فمضت مدة الإيلاء وقع عليها طلاق بائن، ثم إن نكحها ومضت أربعة أشهر بلا قربان وقع عليها طلاق ثان، ثم إن نكحها ومضت المدة وقع عليها ثالث، وذلك لعدم ارتفاع اليمين.

وأشار بقوله: إن نكحها إلى أنه لا يتكرر الطلاق في الحلف المؤبد بدون التزوج؛ لعدم منع حقها، وقيل: لو بانت بمضي أربعة أشهر بالإيلاء، ثم مضى أربعة أخرى، وهي في العدة وقعت أخرى، فإن مضت أربعة أخرى، وهي في العدة وقعت أخرى، والأول أصح؛ لأن وقوع الطلاق بمضي أربعة أشهر جزاء الظلم، وليس للمبانة حق، فلا يكون ظالماً، كذا حققه الزيلعي في «شرح الكنز»).

وقال في «النهر»: «اختلف في اعتبار ابتداء مدته، ففي «الهداية»، وعليه جرى في «الكافي»: إنها من وقت التزوّج، وقيده في «العناية» و«النهاية» تبعاً للتمرتاشي والمرغيناني بما إذا كان التزوج بعد انقضاء العدّة، فإن كان فيها اعتبر ابتداءه من وقت الطلاق، قال الزيلعي وهذا لا يستقيم إلا على قول من قال بتكرار الطلاق قبل التزوج وقد مر ضعفه».

[1] قوله: بلا فيء؛ أي رجوع وهو إما بالقول كقوله: فئت، وبالفعل كالوطء، فإن وُجد الوطء لم تبن.

(1) تبيين الحقائق (2: 263). (2) انتهى من النهر الفائق (2: 428).
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Ila': 'Or if I approach you, then upon me is Hajj, or fasting, or charity, or you are divorced, or my slave is free, then he has made ila'. If he approaches her within the period, kaffarah is obligatory if swearing by Allah, and fulfillment of the condition is obligatory otherwise, and the ila' falls. Otherwise she becomes bain with one divorce, and the temporary oath falls but not the perpetual.' [1] Comment: 'And in other than swearing by Allah, fulfillment is obligatory, such as Hajj or fasting, or she is divorced or his slave is freed. In short, the condition attached to intercourse is fulfilled because the condition is realized.' [2] Comment: 'The ila' falls; i.e., it is nullified, so if four months pass, no divorce occurs.' [3] Comment: 'The oath falls; meaning when he approaches her within the period the ila' falls, and when he does not and the bain divorce occurs by the passage of time, the temporary ila' bound to four months falls, but not the perpetual.' [4] Comment: 'The phrase 'until... etc.' is a branch on the falling of the oath, meaning since he did not approach within the period and the bain divorce occurred by the passage of time, that oath has fallen. So if he marries that woman after the iddah or during it and does not approach her for four months or more, no bain divorce falls upon her because the previous oath no longer remains to have effect.' (Footnote: Or something similar that is burdensome, unlike an oath to pray two rak'ahs, which is not ila' due to lack of burden; but an oath to pray one hundred rak'ahs is ila' by analogy, and similarly for one hundred recitations or following one hundred funerals, though I have not seen it. See: Al-Durr al-Mukhtar 2:548.) [0] Comment: 'She becomes bain a second time; the reason is that the oath is removed by breaking it, whether temporary or perpetual, and becomes void by the passage of the time specified for it. Thus, for the temporary oath there are two ways of nullification: one is breaking it, the other is the passage of time. As for the perpetual oath, it is only removed by breaking it, since there is no time that voids it. So if he says, 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or 'By Allah, I will never approach you,' and the period of ila' passes, a bain divorce occurs. Then if he marries her and four months pass without intercourse, a second divorce occurs. Then if he marries her and the period passes, a third occurs, due to the lack of removal of the oath.' He indicated by his saying 'if he marries her' that divorce does not repeat in the perpetual oath without remarriage, because his right does not prevent her. It was said: If she becomes bain after four months of ila', then another four months pass while she is in the iddah, another divorce occurs. This is weak; the first is correct because the occurrence of divorce after four months is a penalty for oppression, and the separated woman has no right, so he is not an oppressor. Thus al-Zayla'i verified in Sharh al-Kanz. And in Al-Nahr: 'There is disagreement regarding the beginning of its period. In Al-Hidayah and Al-Kafi: it is from the time of marriage. It is restricted in Al-Inayah and Al-Nihayah following al-Tamartashi and al-Marghinani to when the marriage occurs after the completion of the iddah; if during the iddah, the beginning is from the time of divorce. Al-Zayla'i said: This is only sound according to the one who says divorce repeats without remarriage, and its weakness has passed.' [1] Comment: 'Without fi'; i.e., return, which is either by speech, such as 'I have returned,' or by act, such as intercourse, and if intercourse occurs, she does not become bain.' (Footnotes: 1. Tabiyin al-Haqa'iq 2:263. 2. End from al-Nahr al-Fa'iq 2:428.)
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of Ila' from Al-Wiqaya. It explains the ruling when a husband makes an oath not to approach his wife. The author first states the basic ruling: if the husband swears by Allah or by other expressions (like saying 'upon me is Hajj' etc.), and he does not approach her within four months, then an irrevocable divorce occurs. If he does approach within the period, the ila' falls, and he must either pay kaffarah (if swearing by Allah) or fulfill the condition (e.g., perform Hajj, free a slave). The commentary then clarifies that 'fi ghayrihi' (other than swearing by Allah) refers to fulfilling the attached condition, such as the wife being divorced or his slave freed. It emphasizes that the ila' is nullified if he approaches within the period, so no divorce occurs after four months. The temporary oath (mu'aqqat) is distinguished from the perpetual (mu'abbad): for mu'aqqat, if he does not approach, the divorce occurs and the oath falls; for mu'abbad, the oath remains, so if he remarries and again does not approach for four months, another divorce occurs, and so on. The text then discusses the repetition of divorce in mu'abbad: it only repeats if he remarries; without remarriage, no further divorce occurs while she is in the iddah. There is a disagreement on whether divorce can repeat within the iddah, but the stronger view is that it does not. Finally, the passage addresses the start of the four-month period. According to Al-Hidayah and Al-Kafi, it begins from the time of marriage. However, some scholars (like in Al-Inayah and Al-Nihayah) hold that if the marriage occurs after the iddah, the period is from marriage; if during the iddah, from the time of divorce. Al-Zayla'i criticizes this view, saying it only works if one accepts the weaker position of divorce repeating without remarriage. The commentary on 'bila fi'' explains that 'fi'' means return, either by verbal declaration or by actual intercourse, which prevents the divorce.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā’): An oath taken by a husband not to have intercourse with his wife for a period exceeding four months.
المؤقت (al-mu’aqqat): A temporary oath with a specified time, e.g., 'I will not approach you for four months'.
المؤبد (al-mu’abbad): A perpetual oath without a specified time, e.g., 'I will never approach you'.
البائن (al-bā’in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage without a right to return without a new contract.
الفيء (al-fay’): The husband's return to marital relations, either by words (declaring return) or by actual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following correctly describes the consequence of a temporary ila' oath if the husband does not approach for four months?
A) The oath remains and the wife is divorced irrevocably.
B) The oath falls and the wife is divorced irrevocably.
C) The oath falls and no divorce occurs.
D) The wife is divorced revocably.

Key Takeaway
In ila', a temporary oath is completely nullified after four months without approach, resulting in one bain divorce; a perpetual oath persists and can cause multiple divorces upon remarriage.

Perpetual Oath and the Start of the Ila' Period
Commentary expanding on the ruling for perpetual oaths and the dispute about the starting point of the ila' period.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why divorce recurs in a perpetual ila' oath and evaluate the two Hanafi positions on when the four-month period begins.

Core Idea
In perpetual ila', the oath lives on after divorce, so each new marriage restarts the waiting period.

This part of the commentary addresses the specific rulings for perpetual oaths and a scholarly dispute within the Hanafi school. For a perpetual oath, the oath is only removed by actual intercourse. Therefore, after a divorce, the oath remains, and upon remarriage, if the husband again fails to approach for four months, another divorce occurs. This can lead to up to three divorces. The passage also discusses a disagreement about when the four-month period begins: some say from the marriage, others say from the divorce if the marriage occurs during the iddah. Al-Zayla'i rejects the latter view.

Guided Path
1
Understand why divorce recurs in perpetual oaths
The oath is not time-bound, so it is not nullified by the passage of time. The only way to nullify it is by performing the prohibited act (intercourse). If a divorce occurs, the oath continues. In a new marriage, the husband is still bound by the oath, so a new four-month waiting period begins, and failure to approach triggers another divorce.
The text says: 'the perpetual oath is only removed by breaking it (al-hinth).'
2
Note that divorce does not repeat without remarriage
The author clarifies that the repetition only occurs if the husband remarries. During the iddah, no further divorce happens because she is no longer his wife. A weak opinion that divorce can recur in iddah is rejected.
3
Identify the dispute on the start of the period
Some scholars (e.g., Al-Hidayah) hold that the four-month period begins at the time of marriage. Others (in Al-Inayah and Al-Nihayah) say that if the marriage occurs after the iddah, it begins from marriage; if during the iddah, it begins from the time of divorce. Al-Zayla'i critiques this latter view as only consistent with the weak opinion that divorce repeats without remarriage.
4
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred ruling)
The majority view (mufta bihi) is that the period starts from marriage, and no divorce repeats during iddah. This is considered stronger because the separated wife has no right to demand intercourse.

كتاب الطلاق باب الإيلاء

أو إن قربتك فعلي حج، أو صوم، أو صدقة، أو فأنت طالق، أو عبدي حر، فقد آلى إن قربها في المدة حيث، وتجب الكفارة في الحلف بالله تعالى، وفي غيره الجزاء، وسقط الإيلاء. وإلا بانت بواحدة، وسقط الحلف المؤقت لا المؤبد

[1] قوله: وفي غيره؛ أي في غير الحلف بالله يجب الجزاء، وهو الحج والصوم مثلاً، وتطلق هي أو يعتق عبده، وبالجملة: ينزل الجزاء الذي علق بوطئه لتحقق الشرط.

[2] قوله: وسقط الإيلاء؛ أي بطل، فلو مضت أربعة أشهر لا يقع الطلاق.

[3] قوله: وسقط الحلف؛ يعني عند وطئها في المدة يسقط الإيلاء، وعند عدمه ووقوع البائنة بمضي المدة يسقط الإيلاء المؤقت بأربعة أشهر دون المؤبد.

[4] قوله: حتى... الخ؛ تفريع على سقوط الحلف، يعني لما لم يطأ في المدة ووقع الطلاق البائن بمضي المدة سقط ذلك الحلف، فلو نكح تلك المرأة بعد العدة أو فيها فلم يطأها أربعة أشهر أو فصاعداً، لا يقع عليها الطلاق البائن؛ لأن الحلف السابق لم يبق حتى يبقى أثره.

(١) أو نحوه مما يشق، بخلاف فعلي صلاة ركعتين، فليس بمول لعدم مشقتهما، بخلاف فعلي مئة ركعة، وقياسه أن يكون مولياً بمئة ختمة أو اتباع مئة جنازة ولم أره. ينظر : «الدر المختار»(۲ : ٥٤٨)

[0] قوله: تبين ثانياً؛ الوجه في ذلك أن اليمين ترتفع بالحنث مؤقتة كانت أو مؤبدة، وتبطل بمضي الوقت الذي وقتت به، فلبطلان المؤقت صورتان: أحدهما: الحنث. وأخرهما مضي الوقت. وأما المؤبد فلا يرتفع إلا بالحنث إذ لا وقت هناك يبطل بمضيه، فإذا قال: والله لا أقربك أو قال: والله لا أقربك أبداً فمضت مدة الإيلاء وقع عليها طلاق بائن، ثم إن نكحها ومضت أربعة أشهر بلا قربان وقع عليها طلاق ثان، ثم إن نكحها ومضت المدة وقع عليها ثالث، وذلك لعدم ارتفاع اليمين.

وأشار بقوله: إن نكحها إلى أنه لا يتكرر الطلاق في الحلف المؤبد بدون التزوج؛ لعدم منع حقها، وقيل: لو بانت بمضي أربعة أشهر بالإيلاء، ثم مضى أربعة أخرى، وهي في العدة وقعت أخرى، فإن مضت أربعة أخرى، وهي في العدة وقعت أخرى، والأول أصح؛ لأن وقوع الطلاق بمضي أربعة أشهر جزاء الظلم، وليس للمبانة حق، فلا يكون ظالماً، كذا حققه الزيلعي في «شرح الكنز»).

وقال في «النهر»: «اختلف في اعتبار ابتداء مدته، ففي «الهداية»، وعليه جرى في «الكافي»: إنها من وقت التزوّج، وقيده في «العناية» و«النهاية» تبعاً للتمرتاشي والمرغيناني بما إذا كان التزوج بعد انقضاء العدّة، فإن كان فيها اعتبر ابتداءه من وقت الطلاق، قال الزيلعي وهذا لا يستقيم إلا على قول من قال بتكرار الطلاق قبل التزوج وقد مر ضعفه».

[1] قوله: بلا فيء؛ أي رجوع وهو إما بالقول كقوله: فئت، وبالفعل كالوطء، فإن وُجد الوطء لم تبن.

(1) تبيين الحقائق (2: 263). (2) انتهى من النهر الفائق (2: 428).
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Ila': 'Or if I approach you, then upon me is Hajj, or fasting, or charity, or you are divorced, or my slave is free, then he has made ila'. If he approaches her within the period, kaffarah is obligatory if swearing by Allah, and fulfillment of the condition is obligatory otherwise, and the ila' falls. Otherwise she becomes bain with one divorce, and the temporary oath falls but not the perpetual.' [1] Comment: 'And in other than swearing by Allah, fulfillment is obligatory, such as Hajj or fasting, or she is divorced or his slave is freed. In short, the condition attached to intercourse is fulfilled because the condition is realized.' [2] Comment: 'The ila' falls; i.e., it is nullified, so if four months pass, no divorce occurs.' [3] Comment: 'The oath falls; meaning when he approaches her within the period the ila' falls, and when he does not and the bain divorce occurs by the passage of time, the temporary ila' bound to four months falls, but not the perpetual.' [4] Comment: 'The phrase 'until... etc.' is a branch on the falling of the oath, meaning since he did not approach within the period and the bain divorce occurred by the passage of time, that oath has fallen. So if he marries that woman after the iddah or during it and does not approach her for four months or more, no bain divorce falls upon her because the previous oath no longer remains to have effect.' (Footnote: Or something similar that is burdensome, unlike an oath to pray two rak'ahs, which is not ila' due to lack of burden; but an oath to pray one hundred rak'ahs is ila' by analogy, and similarly for one hundred recitations or following one hundred funerals, though I have not seen it. See: Al-Durr al-Mukhtar 2:548.) [0] Comment: 'She becomes bain a second time; the reason is that the oath is removed by breaking it, whether temporary or perpetual, and becomes void by the passage of the time specified for it. Thus, for the temporary oath there are two ways of nullification: one is breaking it, the other is the passage of time. As for the perpetual oath, it is only removed by breaking it, since there is no time that voids it. So if he says, 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or 'By Allah, I will never approach you,' and the period of ila' passes, a bain divorce occurs. Then if he marries her and four months pass without intercourse, a second divorce occurs. Then if he marries her and the period passes, a third occurs, due to the lack of removal of the oath.' He indicated by his saying 'if he marries her' that divorce does not repeat in the perpetual oath without remarriage, because his right does not prevent her. It was said: If she becomes bain after four months of ila', then another four months pass while she is in the iddah, another divorce occurs. This is weak; the first is correct because the occurrence of divorce after four months is a penalty for oppression, and the separated woman has no right, so he is not an oppressor. Thus al-Zayla'i verified in Sharh al-Kanz. And in Al-Nahr: 'There is disagreement regarding the beginning of its period. In Al-Hidayah and Al-Kafi: it is from the time of marriage. It is restricted in Al-Inayah and Al-Nihayah following al-Tamartashi and al-Marghinani to when the marriage occurs after the completion of the iddah; if during the iddah, the beginning is from the time of divorce. Al-Zayla'i said: This is only sound according to the one who says divorce repeats without remarriage, and its weakness has passed.' [1] Comment: 'Without fi'; i.e., return, which is either by speech, such as 'I have returned,' or by act, such as intercourse, and if intercourse occurs, she does not become bain.' (Footnotes: 1. Tabiyin al-Haqa'iq 2:263. 2. End from al-Nahr al-Fa'iq 2:428.)
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of Ila' from Al-Wiqaya. It explains the ruling when a husband makes an oath not to approach his wife. The author first states the basic ruling: if the husband swears by Allah or by other expressions (like saying 'upon me is Hajj' etc.), and he does not approach her within four months, then an irrevocable divorce occurs. If he does approach within the period, the ila' falls, and he must either pay kaffarah (if swearing by Allah) or fulfill the condition (e.g., perform Hajj, free a slave). The commentary then clarifies that 'fi ghayrihi' (other than swearing by Allah) refers to fulfilling the attached condition, such as the wife being divorced or his slave freed. It emphasizes that the ila' is nullified if he approaches within the period, so no divorce occurs after four months. The temporary oath (mu'aqqat) is distinguished from the perpetual (mu'abbad): for mu'aqqat, if he does not approach, the divorce occurs and the oath falls; for mu'abbad, the oath remains, so if he remarries and again does not approach for four months, another divorce occurs, and so on. The text then discusses the repetition of divorce in mu'abbad: it only repeats if he remarries; without remarriage, no further divorce occurs while she is in the iddah. There is a disagreement on whether divorce can repeat within the iddah, but the stronger view is that it does not. Finally, the passage addresses the start of the four-month period. According to Al-Hidayah and Al-Kafi, it begins from the time of marriage. However, some scholars (like in Al-Inayah and Al-Nihayah) hold that if the marriage occurs after the iddah, the period is from marriage; if during the iddah, from the time of divorce. Al-Zayla'i criticizes this view, saying it only works if one accepts the weaker position of divorce repeating without remarriage. The commentary on 'bila fi'' explains that 'fi'' means return, either by verbal declaration or by actual intercourse, which prevents the divorce.

Key Terms
المؤبد (al-mu’abbad): A perpetual oath without a specified time, e.g., 'I will never approach you'.
الفَاء (al-fay’): The husband's return to marital relations, either by words (declaring return) or by actual intercourse.
الحنث (al-hinth): Breaking an oath by performing the prohibited act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, when does the four-month period begin for a perpetual ila'?
A) From the time of the marriage
B) From the time of the divorce
C) From the time the oath was made
D) From the time the iddah begins

Key Takeaway
In perpetual ila', the oath remains after divorce, so each new marriage restarts the four-month waiting period, leading to repeated bain divorces upon failure to approach.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Repeated Divorce in Perpetual Ila' After Remarriage
Expands rulings for perpetual Ila' causing repeated divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on repeated divorce in perpetual Ila', identify the condition for repetition (remarriage), and explain what happens after three divorces.

Core Idea
In perpetual Ila', divorce repeats with each remarriage but only up to three times; after that, the oath remains but Ila' is void.

Perpetual Ila' (a vow of indefinite abstinence) leads to an irrevocable divorce if the husband does not return within four months. If the couple remarries, the cycle can repeat because the oath was never broken. But this only happens up to three divorces total. After that, the Ila' no longer applies, though the oath still binds the husband. This passage unpacks these rulings and clarifies key disagreements within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish time-bound from perpetual Ila'
Identify that a time-bound Ila' ends with passage of time or violation, while perpetual Ila' only ends by violation (intercourse). This affects whether divorce can repeat.
Perpetual Ila' uses words like 'never' or no time limit.
2
Trace the divorce sequence for perpetual Ila'
Follow the scenario: first divorce after four months → remarriage → second divorce after another four months without intimacy → remarriage → third divorce. This shows repetition requires remarriage.
The passage states: 'if he marries her and four months pass... a second divorce'.
3
Understand why repetition requires remarriage
The divorce is a penalty for injustice (zulm). After divorce, the woman is separated and has no right to intimacy, so no further injustice occurs until they remarry.
Al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz confirms this as the correct view.
4
Examine the disagreement on start of period after remarriage
Some say the new four-month period begins from the new marriage; others say from the original divorce if remarriage is during 'iddah. The stronger view is from the new marriage.
Al-Marghinani and al-Tamartashi restrict this to marriage after 'iddah.
5
Identify what happens after three divorces
After three divorces, the Ila' ends because ownership (milk) is gone, but the oath remains. If the husband later remarries after tahlil and has intercourse, he must expiate for the oath. No new Ila' applies.
The oath remains binding only for expiation, not for Ila'.

فتبين بأخرى إن مضت مدة أُخْرَى بعد نكاح ثان بلا فيء ولم يقربها أربعة أشهر تبين ثالثاً، وهذا معنى قوله : (فتبين بأخرى إن مضت مدة أُخرى بعد نكاح ثان بلا فيء مؤبدة، وتبطل بمضي الوقت الذي وقتت به، فلبطلان المؤقت صورتان : أحدهما : الحنث. وأخرهما مضي الوقت. وأما المؤبد فلا يرتفع إلا بالحنث إذ لا وقت هناك يبطل بمضيه ، فإذا قال : والله لا أقربك أو قال : والله لا أقربك أبداً فمضت مدة الإيلاء وقع عليها طلاق بائن، ثم إن نكحها ومضت أربعة أشهر بلا قربان وقع عليها طلاق ثان، ثم إن نكحها ومضت المدة وقع عليها ثالث، وذلك لعدم ارتفاع اليمين. وأشار بقوله : إن نكحها إلى أنه لا يتكرر الطلاق في الحلف المؤبد بدون التزوج ؛ لعدم منع حقها ، وقيل : لو بانت بمضي أربعة أشهر بالإيلاء، ثم مضى أربعة أخرى ، وهي في العدة وقعت أخرى، فإن مضت أربعة أخرى ، وهي في العدة وقعت أخرى ، والأوّل أصح ؛ لأنَّ وقوع الطلاق بمضي أربعة أشهر جزاء الظلم، وليس للمبانة حق، فلا يكون ظالماً ، كذا حققه الزيلعي في «شرح الكنز»). وقال في «النهر»: «اختلف في اعتبار ابتداء مدته ، ففي «الهداية»، وعليه جرى في «الكافي»: إنّها من وقتِ التزوّج، وقيده في «العناية» و«النهاية» تبعاً للتمرتاشي والمرغيناني بما إذا كان التزوج بعد انقضاء العدّة ، فإن كان فيها اعتبر ابتداءه من وقت الطلاق، قال الزيلعي وهذا لا يستقيم إلا على قول من قال بتكرار الطلاق قبل التزوج وقد مر ضعفه. قوله : بلا فيء ؛ أي رجوع وهو إما بالقول كقوله: فئت، وبالفعل كالوطء، فإن وُجد الوطء لم تبن. ثم أخرى كذلك بعد ثالث ، وبقي الحلف بعد ثالث، لا الإيلاء ، فلو قربها كفر، ولا تبين بالإيلاء ثم أخرى كذلك بعد ثالث) : فقولُه بلا في أي بلا قربان. ( وبقي الحلف بعد ثالث، لا الإيلاء، فلو قربها كفر، ولا تبين بالإيلاء) : أي في الحلف المؤبد إذا وقع ثلاث تطليقات من غير قربان بقي الحلف ؛ لأنه لم يقربها، فلم ينحل اليمين، لكن لم يبق الإيلاء، فلو نكحها بعد الزوج الثاني، وقربها تجبُ الكفّارة ؛ لبقاء اليمين، ولو لم يقربها لا تبينُ بالإيلاء ؛ لأنه لم يبق الإيلاء. قوله : كذلك ؛ أي يقع ثالث إن لم يفئ في المدّة ومضت أربعة أشهر بلا قربان. قوله : وبقي الحلف ؛ يعني إذا وقع الطلاق عليها ثلاث مرات في الحلف المؤبد بمضي المدة ثلاث مرات بغير قربان يبقى الحلف ويبطل الإيلاء، أما بطلان الإيلاء فلانتهاء ملك المولى بوقوع ثلاث تطليقات، وأما بقاء الحلف فلعدم وجود الحنث. قوله : فلو ؛ تفريع على بقاء اليمين وبطلان الإيلاء، وحاصله أنه لو نكحها رابعاً بعد التحليل، فإن وطئها تجب عليه كفارة اليمين ؛ لوجود الحنث حينئذ وعدم وجود حنث قبله، وإن لم يطأ حتى مضت أربعة أشهر لا يقع عليها الطلاق بالإيلاء السابق ؛ لبطلانه بذهاب ذلك الملك الذي آلى فيه وحدوث ملك جديد. قوله : أي في الحلف المؤيد ؛ وأما المؤقت فقد مر أنه لا يتصور فيه وقوع ثلاث تطليقات ؛ لسقوطه بمضي المدة أولاً. قوله : ثلاث تطليقات ؛ بخلاف لو بانت بالإيلاء بما دون ثلاث أو أبانها بتنجيز الطلاق، ثم عادت إليه بثلاث ، فإنّه يقع حينئذ الطلاق بالإيلاء عندهما خلافاً لمحمد ، فعنده لا تقع الثلاث، بل ما بقي من واحدة أو ثنتين، بناءً على قوله : إنّ الزوج الثاني لا يهدم ما دون الثلاث كما مر تفصيله. قوله : بعد الزوج ؛ أي بعد أن نكحها الثاني، وطلقها بعد الوطء، وانقضت عدته فنكحها الأول. قوله : لأنه لم يبق الإيلاء ؛ هذا نظير ما إذا علّق طلاقها بالدخول مثلاً ثمَّ نَجَّزَ
So she is divorced a third time if another period passes after a second marriage without fay', and he does not approach her for four months, and this is the meaning of his statement: 'So she is divorced a third time if another period passes after a second marriage without fay'' [for a perpetual vow]. And it (the vow) becomes void with the passage of the time that was specified. Thus for the voiding of a time-bound vow there are two forms: one is the violation (by intercourse), and the other is the passage of time. As for the perpetual vow, it is only removed by violation, because there is no time that would nullify it by passing. So if he says: 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or says: 'By Allah, I will never approach you,' and the period of Ila' passes, a irrevocable divorce occurs. Then if he marries her and four months pass without intimacy, a second divorce occurs. Then if he marries her and the period passes, a third divorce occurs. This is because the oath is not removed. And he indicated by his statement 'if he marries her' that the divorce is not repeated in a perpetual vow without remarriage, because there is no prevention of her right. And it was said: if she becomes separated by the passage of four months due to Ila', then another four months pass while she is in the 'iddah, another divorce occurs. Then if another four months pass while she is in the 'iddah, another divorce occurs. The first is more correct because the occurrence of divorce by the passage of four months is the penalty for injustice, and the separated woman has no right, so he is not unjust. Thus al-Zayla'i verified it in Sharh al-Kanz. And he said in al-Nahr: 'There is disagreement concerning the consideration of the beginning of its period. In al-Hidayah, and according to what is in al-Kafi, it is from the time of marriage. And it was restricted in al-`Inayah and al-Nihayah, following al-Tamartashi and al-Marghinani, to when the marriage occurs after the completion of the 'iddah. If it is during it, its beginning is considered from the time of divorce. Al-Zayla'i said: This is only consistent with the opinion of those who say the repetition of divorce before remarriage, and its weakness has passed.' His words: 'without fay'; i.e., return, which is either by speech like saying 'I have returned' or by action like intercourse, for if intercourse occurs she is not divorced. Then another similarly after a third, and the oath remains after the third, not the Ila', so if he approaches her he must expiate, and she is not divorced by Ila'. Then another similarly after a third: so his statement 'without fay' means without intimacy. (And the oath remains after the third, not the Ila', so if he approaches her he must expiate, and she is not divorced by Ila') i.e., in the perpetual vow when three divorces occur without intimacy, the oath remains because he did not approach her, so the oath is not dissolved, but the Ila' does not remain. So if he marries her after the second husband and approaches her, expiation is obligatory due to the remaining oath. And if he does not approach her, she is not divorced by Ila' because the Ila' does not remain. His words: 'similarly'; i.e., a third occurs if he does not return to her within the period and four months pass without intimacy. His words: 'and the oath remains'; meaning that when three divorces occur in the perpetual vow by the passage of three periods without intimacy, the oath remains and the Ila' becomes void. As for the voiding of the Ila', it is because the ownership of the one making Ila' ends with the occurrence of three divorces. As for the remaining of the oath, it is because no violation has occurred. His words: 'so if'; a branching on the remaining of the oath and voiding of the Ila', and its summary is that if he marries her a fourth time after tahlil, then if he has intercourse, expiation for the oath is obligatory due to the occurrence of violation at that time and the absence of previous violation. And if he does not have intercourse until four months pass, divorce does not occur upon her by the previous Ila' because it is voided by the removal of that ownership in which he made Ila' and the occurrence of new ownership. His words: 'i.e., in the perpetual vow'; as for the time-bound vow, it has already passed that the occurrence of three divorces is not conceivable because it is terminated by the passage of the first period. His words: 'three divorces'; contrary to if she becomes separated by Ila' with less than three or he divorces her by immediate divorce, then she returns to him with three, then the divorce by Ila' occurs according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad (al-Shaybani) who holds that three do not occur, but rather what remains of one or two, based on his statement that the second husband does not demolish less than three, as detailed earlier. His words: 'after the husband'; i.e., after she married the second, and he divorced her after intercourse, and her 'iddah ended, then the first married her. His words: 'because the Ila' did not remain'; this is analogous to if he suspended her divorce on entry, for example, then he effected it immediately.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a matn statement on Ila' (vow of abstinence from marital relations). The commentator explains the rulings for a perpetual vow (mu'abbad) as opposed to a time-bound vow (muwaqqat). In a perpetual vow, if the husband abstains for four months without returning (fay'), an irrevocable divorce occurs. If they remarry and again he abstains for four months, another divorce occurs, and a third if it happens again. This repetition requires remarriage; without remarriage, divorce does not repeat because the separated woman has no right to claim injustice. The passage also addresses a disagreement about the start of the period for Ila' after remarriage: whether it begins from the new marriage or from the previous divorce if the marriage occurs during the 'iddah. The more authoritative view is that it begins from the new marriage unless the marriage occurs during the 'iddah, in which case it begins from the divorce. The commentator clarifies that after three divorces, the Ila' is void because the husband's ownership (milk) is gone, but the oath remains. If he later marries her again after tahlil (her marriage to another) and has intercourse, expiation is required for breaking the oath. If he does not have intercourse, no divorce by Ila' occurs because the Ila' was attached to the previous ownership. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if less than three divorces occurred by Ila' and then the husband remarries her after tahlil, Divorce by Ila' can occur again, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the second husband does not demolish less than three, so only the remaining divorces occur.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā'): A vow by a husband to abstain from marital relations with his wife for a period of four months or more.
الفيء (al-fay'): Return to marital relations, either by word (saying 'I have returned') or by actual intercourse, ending the Ila'.
المؤبد (al-mu'abbad): A perpetual oath of abstinence without a specified time limit; it can only be removed by violation (intercourse).
الحنث (al-hinth): Violation of the oath by having intercourse, which requires expiation and ends the Ila'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a perpetual Ila' vow, if the husband abstains for four months after remarriage and they have not had intercourse, what occurs?
A) The vow is automatically cancelled
B) A single irrevocable divorce occurs, and the cycle ends
C) A divorce occurs, and this can happen up to three times with remarriage
D) The husband must expiate but no divorce

Key Takeaway
In perpetual Ila', each new marriage restarts the potential for divorce, but only three times total; after that, the Ila' ends but the oath remains.

Perpetual Oath After Triple Divorce: Remaining Hulf but Void Ila'
Ruling on perpetual oath after triple divorce and remaining oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the perpetual oath after three divorces and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf vs. Imam Muhammad on whether the Ila' revives after remarriage.

Core Idea
A perpetual oath outlasts three divorces, but the Ila' dies with the marriage; only kaffarah remains.

In a perpetual Ila' (vow never to approach), if four months pass three times without intercourse, three divorces occur. What happens to the original oath and the Ila'? This passage clarifies that the oath remains because it was never broken, but the Ila' is null because the husband no longer has marital authority. If the couple reunites after a proper tahlil, the oath still binds, but the Ila' does not revive. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the revivability of Ila' when the separation was by less than three divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The husband made a perpetual oath (hulf mu'abbad) not to approach his wife. Four months pass three times without intercourse, resulting in three divorces due to Ila'.
The scenario assumes no violation of the oath during the original marriage.
2
Separate the oath from the Ila'
Understand that the oath (hulf) and the Ila' are distinct legal constructs. Ila' is the specific vow that leads to divorce; the oath is the binding promise that can require kaffarah.
The Ila' is a subset of oaths but with specific rules.
3
Apply the rule: Ila' void, oath remains
After three divorces, the Ila' is null because marital authority (milk) ends. But the oath remains because it was never violated. Thus, if he later approaches her (after remarriage), kaffarah is wajib.
Reason for Ila' nullification: the husband no longer has a wife to abstain from.
4
Analyze the post-remarriage scenario
After a lawful tahlil and remarriage, if he approaches, kaffarah is due. If four months pass without approach, no divorce occurs from the old Ila' because it was voided.
This is the clear ruling in the matn.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
If the separation was by less than three divorces (e.g., one or two via Ila' or immediate divorce), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the original Ila' revives and causes divorce after four months upon remarriage. Imam Muhammad says only the remaining divorces (if any) take effect.
The basis of Muhammad's view: the second husband does not 'demolish' less than three divorces.

[1] His saying 'likewise': i.e., a third occurs if he does not return within the period and four months pass without intercourse. [2] His saying 'and the oath remains': meaning when three divorces occur upon her in the perpetual oath by the passage of three periods without intercourse, the oath remains and the Ila' becomes void. Its summary is that if he marries her a fourth time after the tahlil, and he has intercourse with her, kaffarah of the oath becomes obligatory due to the existence of violation at that time and the absence of violation before. [6] His saying 'after the husband': i.e., after she married the second husband, and he divorced her after intercourse, and her iddah ended, then the first husband married her. [7] His saying 'because the Ila' does not remain': this is analogous to if he suspended her divorce upon entry, for example, then he made it immediate.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in perpetual Ila' (vow of abstinence). The matn states: When a husband makes a perpetual oath not to approach his wife, and three periods of four months pass without intercourse, three divorces occur. After the third, the oath (hulf) remains because he never violated it, but the Ila' itself is null because his marital authority has ended. If he later marries her again (after she marries another and is divorced), and then approaches her, he must perform kaffarah (expiation) because the oath is still binding. However, if he does not approach her during a subsequent four-month period, she is not divorced by the original Ila', because the Ila' was nullified when the divorces occurred. The detailed commentary expands on this, clarifying that the perpetual oath (hulf mu'abbad) remains even after three divorces, but the Ila' ends because the husband no longer has a wife to abstain from. The commentary also notes a dispute: If the wife had separated by Ila' with less than three divorces or by an immediate divorce, and then returns to him after three divorces (from a second marriage), then the original Ila' would cause divorce upon the passage of four months according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but Imam Muhammad disagrees. According to Muhammad, only one or two divorces remain, because the second husband does not dissolve the effect of less than three divorces (a principle discussed elsewhere).

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā’): A vow by a husband not to approach his wife for a period, leading to divorce after four months if he does not return.
حلف مؤبد (ḥalf mu’abbad): A perpetual oath with no time limit, e.g., 'By Allah, I will not approach you.'
حنث (ḥinth): Violation of an oath; in this context, by having intercourse after the oath.
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation for breaking an oath, typically feeding ten poor or freeing a slave.

Key Takeaway
A perpetual oath outlasts three divorces and requires kaffarah upon violation, but the Ila' institution dies with the marriage; however, if less than three divorces occurred, the Ila' may revive upon remarriage—a point of dispute within the Hanafi school.

Perpetual Oaths After Triple Divorce: Classification and the Zufar Dispute
Classification of perpetual oaths and dispute on Ila' after triple divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify perpetual oaths after triple divorce into three types and state the Hanafi position on Ila' after triple divorce, distinguishing it from Zufar's view.

Core Idea
After triple divorce, oaths by Allah or by other acts remain; oaths conditional on the wife's divorce become void; Ila' is nullified entirely.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah delves into a nuanced area: what happens to perpetual oaths—especially Ila'—after a woman has been divorced three times? The author classifies oaths into three categories and then addresses a dispute with Zufar, a Hanafi scholar who held that Ila' retains effect even after triple divorce. The Hanafi consensus, however, rules that such Ila' is void because the marriage is completely severed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of perpetual oaths
The passage distinguishes oaths by Allah (e.g., 'By Allah, I will not approach you'), oaths by other than the wife's divorce (e.g., an oath to perform Hajj or to divorce another wife), and oaths by the wife's own divorce (e.g., 'If I approach you, you are divorced').
This classification determines the effect after triple divorce.
2
Apply the ruling to each type after triple divorce
For oaths by Allah and oaths by other acts, the oath remains; if the condition occurs, kaffarah or penalty is due. For oaths by the wife's divorce, the suspension becomes void because the immediate divorce (tangeez) nullifies the suspension.
The underlying principle: tangeez nullifies ta'leeq.
3
Analyze the Ila' dispute with Zufar
If a man makes Ila' (swearing not to approach for four months) and then divorces his wife three times, the Hanafi position is that the Ila' is void. Zufar held that Ila' remains effective, so if four months pass in iddah, an additional divorce occurs. The text sides with the majority.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Zufar would require an extra divorce; the majority does not.
4
Explain the underlying principle
The key principle is that once the husband pronounces three divorces immediately (tangeez), any prior conditional suspension (ta'leeq) is abrogated. This applies to both Ila' and conditional divorce statements.
This is derived from the broader Hanafi rule that tangeez nullifies ta'leeq.

[٣] قوله : ايلاء ; لتحقق مدة الإيلاء ; لأنه جمع بينهما بحرف الجمع، فصار كقوله : لا أكلم فلاناً يومين ويومين، فإنّه كقوله : لا أكلم أربعة أيام، والأصل في جنس هذه المسائل أنه متى عطف من غير إعادة حرف النفي ولا تكرار اسم الله يكون يميناً واحداً، أو لو أعاد حرف النفي، أو كرّر اسم الله له يكون يمينين، وتتداخل مدته. وتوضيحه أنه لو قال : والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين ولا يومين يكون يمينين ومدتهما واحدة، لو كلّمه في اليوم الأوّل أو الثاني يحنث وتجب عليه كفارتان، وإن كلّمه في (۱) «فتح القدير» (٤ : ٢١٠).
And His (the author's) statement: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months, and two months after these two months' is Ila'. And His (the author's) statement: 'And the oath remains after three; there is a detail: if the oath was by Allah, the oath remains until kaffarah is due; if the oath was by other than her divorce, the oath also remains; and if it was by her divorce, it does not remain because making it immediate nullifies the suspension.' [2] (And his statement: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months' is Ila' — three [divorces], then she marries another, then he brings her back and has intercourse, she is not divorced, contrary to Zufar. Similarly, if he made Ila' and then divorced her three times, the Ila' is void, even if four months pass while she is in her iddah, no divorce occurs, contrary to Zufar. Thus in 'al-Fath'.) [1] His saying: 'if the oath was ... etc.'; its summary: The perpetual oath is either by Allah, as in his saying 'By Allah, I will not approach you', or by other than Allah, which is either the divorce of that wife, as in his saying 'If I approach you, you are divorced', or other than her divorce, whether another act like hajj, fasting, or charity, or the divorce of another wife. If the oath is by Allah, the oath remains after three divorces as well, so kaffarah of the oath becomes obligatory if he violates. If the oath is by other than her divorce, likewise, the penalty happens upon intercourse. But if the oath is by the divorce of that woman, the oath becomes void after three divorces upon her, so even if he marries her after tahlil, no divorce falls upon her by that suspension because of what passed earlier: that making it immediate nullifies the suspension. [2] His saying 'after': this is an accidental restriction; because if he said 'two months and two months', the ruling would be the same, as al-Zayla'i stated. [3] His saying 'ila'': because the period of Ila' is established; because he combined them with the conjunction, so it is like his saying 'I will not speak to so-and-so for two days and two days,' which is like saying 'I will not speak for four days.' The principle in these matters is that whenever he joins without repeating the negation or the name of Allah, it is one oath. If he repeats the negation or the name of Allah, it becomes two oaths, and their periods overlap. An explanation: if he says 'By Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days nor two days', it is two oaths with one period; if he speaks to him on the first or second day, he violates and must give two kaffarahs, and if he speaks to him on (1) 'Fath al-Qadir' (4:210).
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage opens with two matn statements. The first concerns a man who swears a perpetual oath not to approach his wife for two months, then another two months after the first two. This constitutes a valid Ila' because the total period exceeds four months. The second matn statement provides a crucial classification: after three divorces, the effect of the perpetual oath depends on its type. If it is an oath by Allah, the oath remains and kaffarah is due upon violation. If it is an oath by something other than the wife's divorce (e.g., an oath to do an act, or to divorce another wife), the oath also remains. But if the oath is conditional upon the wife's own divorce (e.g., 'if I approach you, you are divorced'), then after three divorces have already occurred, the conditional divorce becomes void because the immediate effect (tangeez) nullifies the suspension (ta'leeq). The passage then records a dispute with Zufar: If a man makes Ila' and then divorces his wife three times, the Ila' is void. If after she marries another and returns, he has intercourse, no divorce occurs from the original Ila'. Also, if four months pass during her iddah after the triple divorce, no divorce occurs — contrary to Zufar's view. This shows that the Ila' is completely nullified by the definitive cessation of marriage. The commentary concludes with a linguistic analysis: if the husband says 'two months and two months after these two months,' the conjunction makes it a period of four months, establishing Ila'. The principle is that without repeating the negation, it is a single oath; with repetition, it is two oaths with overlapping periods.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta‘līq): Suspending a divorce upon a condition, e.g., 'If I approach you, you are divorced.'
تنجيز (tanjīz): Immediate pronouncement of divorce without condition.
تحليل (taḥlīl): The process of a divorced woman marrying another man, consummating the marriage, and being divorced, to become permissible for the first husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only oaths by the wife's divorce.

Key Takeaway
After triple divorce, oaths by Allah or by other acts remain binding; oaths conditional on the wife's divorce become void, and Ila' is completely nullified.

Effect of Three Divorces on Oaths in Ila'
Commentary analysing the survival of oaths after three divorces in Ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify perpetual oaths into three categories, state the Hanafi ruling on each after three divorces, and explain why a conditional divorce oath is nullified using the maxim al-tanjiz yubtil al-ta'liq.

Core Idea
After three divorces, only oaths tied to that wife's divorce are nullified; oaths by Allah or on other actions remain binding.

In the law of Ila', a husband may take a perpetual oath related to his wife. But what happens to such oaths after three divorces? This commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies that the answer depends on the type of oath. Understanding this detail is essential for correctly applying rulings on oaths and divorce in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of perpetual oaths
The text distinguishes oaths by Allah, oaths by other-than-divorce (e.g., Hajj, fasting, or divorce of another wife), and oaths by divorce of that specific wife. List them clearly.
The first two are non-divorce oaths; the third is a divorce conditional.
2
Determine the ruling after three divorces for each type
For oaths by Allah: they remain, and expiation becomes obligatory if violated. For oaths by non-divorce actions: they remain, and the stipulated consequence applies upon violation. For the divorce-linked oath: it is nullified.
The nullification of the third type is the key Hanafi position.
3
Understand the legal maxim behind nullification
The maxim 'al-tanjiz yubtil al-ta'liq' (immediate application invalidates suspension) applies. Since three divorces have already occurred, the conditional divorce cannot be triggered again; the suspension (ta'liq) is broken.
This is a form of istihsan based on usul al-fiqh.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar
Imam Zufar held that the divorce-linked oath remains even after three divorces. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view that it is nullified.
The text cites Fath al-Qadir for support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : والله لا أقربك شهرين، وشهرين بعد هذين الشهرين إيلاء وقوله : وبقي الحلف بعد ثلاث ; فيه تفصيل، إن كان الحلف بالله تعالى يبقى الحلف حتَّى تجب الكفّارة، وإن كان الحلف بغيرِ طلاقها بقي الحلف أيضاً، وإن كان بطلاقها لا يبقى ; لأن التنجيز يُبْطِلُ التعليق. [٢] (وقوله : والله لا أقربك شهرين وشهرين بعد هذين الشهرين إيلاء" الثلاث فتزوّجت بغيره، ثم أعادها فدخلت لا تطلق خلافا لزفر ، وكذا لو آلى منها ثم طلقها ثلاثاً بطل الإيلاء، حتى لو مضت أربعة أشهر وهي في العدة لم يقع الطلاق، خلافاً لزفر . كذا في «الفتح»). And His saying: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months, and two months after these two months' is Ila'. And His saying: 'And the oath remains after three' has details: if the oath is by Allah the Exalted, the oath remains until expiation becomes obligatory; if the oath is by something other than her divorce, the oath also remains; but if it is by her divorce, it does not remain, because immediate application (tunjiz) invalidates suspension (ta'liq). [2] (And His saying: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months is Ila'' and the three... then she married another, then he returned her and she entered, she is not divorced, contrary to Zufar. Similarly, if he made Ila' from her then divorced her thrice, the Ila' is nullified, so even if four months pass while she is in 'iddah, divorce does not occur, contrary to Zufar. As in al-Fath.) [1] His saying: 'If it was...' etc.; its summary: the perpetual oath is either by Allah, as in 'By Allah, I will not approach you', or by other than Allah, and that is either the divorce of that wife, as in 'If I approach you, you are divorced', or other than her divorce, whether it is another action besides divorce, or the divorce of another wife, as in 'If I approach you, upon me is Hajj or fasting or charity', or 'If I approach you, my other wife is divorced'. If the oath is by Allah, the oath remains even after the occurrence of three divorces, so expiation of the oath becomes obligatory if he violates. If the oath is by other than her divorce, likewise, the consequence takes effect when he has intercourse. But if the oath is by the divorce of that woman, the oath is nullified after the occurrence of three divorces upon her, so even if he marries her after tahlil, divorce does not occur by that conditional, as previously mentioned: because immediate application invalidates the suspension.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the statement from the matn regarding Ila' and the effect of three divorces. The author explains that the oath (half) after three divorces requires detail (tafsil). There are three types of perpetual oaths: (1) by Allah, (2) by something other than divorce (like Hajj, fasting, charity, or divorce of another wife), and (3) by divorce of that specific wife. For type 1 and 2, the oath remains even after three divorces; if the husband violates, he must pay expiation (kaffarat yameen) for type 1, or fulfill the consequence for type 2. For type 3, the oath is nullified (batal) because applying the condition immediately (tunjiz) invalidates the suspension (ta'liq). The text cites a disagreement with Zufar, who held that the oath remains. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is nullified, as mentioned in Fath al-Qadir. The reason is the legal maxim: al-tanjiz yubtil al-ta'liq. This ensures that after three divorces, a conditional divorce cannot take effect again, even after remarriage.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā’): A vow of abstinence from intercourse with one's wife, lasting four months or more, which may lead to divorce if not broken.
تنجيز (tanjīz): The immediate application or execution of a condition; here refers to the occurrence of three divorces making the condition operative.
تعليق (ta‘līq): A conditional suspension of a legal consequence; here, the divorce is suspended on a future condition (approach).
كفارة يمين (kaffārat yamīn): Expiation for violating an oath by Allah; it consists of feeding ten poor, clothing them, or freeing a slave, or fasting three days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After a husband has divorced his wife three times, what happens to an oath he took that says 'If I approach you, you are divorced'?
A) The oath remains and divorce occurs if he approaches
B) The oath is nullified and no divorce occurs
C) The oath remains but only expiation is required
D) The oath becomes invalid only if the wife remarries

Key Takeaway
Only a perpetual oath that is a conditional divorce of that specific wife is nullified by three divorces; oaths by Allah or other actions remain binding.

Determining Whether Multiple Oaths Constitute Ila' or Separate Oaths
Commentary on the principle of counting oaths in Ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of conjunction to determine whether an utterance in the form of Ila' counts as one or two oaths, and state the resulting legal effects.

Core Idea
Conjunction without repetition merges durations; repetition of negation or Divine Name creates separate oaths.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a critical rule in Ila': how to count oaths when multiple time periods are mentioned. The key is whether the husband repeats the negation particle ('la') or the name of Allah. This determines if he has made a single Ila' covering four continuous months or multiple oaths that do not satisfy the Ila' requirement. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly ruling on Ila' and expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance structure
Examine whether the husband used conjunction ('wa') without repeating the negation or Allah's name, or if he repeated the negation/name.
2
Apply the Hanafi principle
If conjunction without repetition, treat as one oath with combined duration. If repetition of negation (e.g., 'la') or Allah's name, treat as multiple oaths with overlapping durations.
This principle is based on the underlying intent; the language indicates whether the speaker intends one continuous commitment or multiple separate ones.
3
Determine effect on Ila'
For Ila', there must be a single oath covering a continuous four-month period. Multiple oaths break continuity, so no Ila' is formed.
4
Calculate expiation if violated
If multiple oaths and violation occurs during overlapping periods, multiple expiations are due. If violation occurs after one period expired, only expiation for the remaining oath.
This is illustrated in the passage with the 'day' examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢] قوله : بعد؛ هذا قيد اتفاقي ; لأنه لو قال : شهرين وشهرين كان الحكم كذلك، صرّح به الزيلعي. [٣] قوله : ايلاء ; لتحقق مدة الإيلاء; لأنه جمع بينهما بحرف الجمع، فصار كقوله : لا أكلم فلاناً يومين ويومين، فإنّه كقوله : لا أكلم أربعة أيام، والأصل في جنس هذه المسائل أنه . متی عطف من غير إعادة حرف النفي ولا تكرار اسم الله يكون يميناً واحداً، أو لو أعاد حرف النفي، أو كرّر اسم الله له يكون يمينين، وتتداخل مدته. وتوضيحه أنه لو قال : والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين ولا يومين يكون يمينين ومدتهما واحدة، لو كلّمه في اليوم الأوّل أو الثاني يحنث وتجب عليه كفارتان، وإن كلّمه في بخلاف بعد يوم، والله لا أقربك شهرين بعد الشهرين الأولين") : أي لو قال : والله لا أقربك شهرين ومكث يوماً، ثُمَّ قال : والله لا أقربك الشهرين بعد الشهرين الأولين، لم يكن مولياً ; لأن" في اليوم الأول كان حلفه على شهرين، وفي اليوم الثاني كان حلفه على أربعة أشهر إلا يوماً واحداً. اليوم الثالث لا يحنث ; لانقضاء مدتها ، وكذا لو قال : والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين، والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين. ولو قال : والله لا أكلمه يومين ويومين كان يميناً واحداً، مدته أربعة أيام حتى لو كلمه فيها تجب عليه كفارة واحدة. ولو قال : والله لا أكلمه يوماً ولا يومين أو قال : والله لا أكلمه يوماً والله لا أكلمه يومين، يكون يمينين، فمدة الأولى يوم، ومدة الثانية يومان، حتى لو كلّمه في اليوم الأوّل تجب عليه كفّارتان، وفي اليوم الثاني كفارة واحدة، ولو كلّمه في اليوم الثالث لا يحنث ; لانقضاء مدتها. وعلى هذا لو قال : والله لا أقربك شهرين ولا شهرين، أو قال : والله لا أقربك شهرين والله لا أقربك شهرين، لا يكون مولياً ; لأنهما يمينان، فتتداخل مدتها. كذا ذكره الزيلعي في «التبيين».
[2] His saying: 'after' is an incidental qualifier, because if he said 'two months and two months' the ruling is the same, as stated by al-Zayla'i. [3] His saying: 'Ila' is to verify the period of Ila', because he combined them with the conjunction, so it is like his saying: 'I will not speak to so-and-so for two days and two days', for it is like his saying: 'I will not speak for four days'. The principle in this type of matter is: whenever he joins with the conjunction without repeating the negation particle or repeating the name of Allah, it is one oath; but if he repeats the negation particle or repeats the name of Allah, then they are two oaths, and their durations overlap. Its clarification: if he says: 'By Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days and not for two days', it is two oaths and their duration is one; if he speaks to him on the first or second day, he violates and owes two expiations; and if he speaks to him on... contrary to after a day, and 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months after the first two months' i.e. if he said: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months' and then waited a day, then said: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for the two months after the first two months', he is not a muli' (one who makes Ila'), because on the first day his oath was for two months, and on the second day his oath was for four months less one day. On the third day he does not violate because its period has expired. Similarly, if he said: 'By Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days', and 'By Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days'. And if he said: 'By Allah, I will not speak to him for two days and two days', it is one oath, its period four days, such that if he speaks to him during it, one expiation is due. And if he said: 'By Allah, I will not speak to him for one day nor for two days', or he said: 'By Allah, I will not speak to him for one day' and 'By Allah, I will not speak to him for two days', they are two oaths, the period of the first one day, the period of the second two days, such that if he speaks to him on the first day, two expiations are due, on the second day one expiation, and if he speaks to him on the third day he does not violate because its period has expired. And based on this, if he said: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months nor for two months', or he said: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months' and 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months', he is not a muli' because they are two oaths, so their durations overlap. This is mentioned by al-Zayla'i in al-Tibyan.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage explains the rules for multiple oaths in the context of Ila'. The key principle is: when a person combines two time periods with 'wa' (and) without repeating the negation particle ('la') or the name of Allah, it counts as a single oath with a combined duration. If the negation or the divine name is repeated, they are two separate oaths whose durations overlap. The passage uses examples with speaking to Zayd and applies them to Ila'. For instance, 'I will not speak to you for two days and two days' is one oath for four days; 'I will not speak to you for two days nor two days' is two oaths for two days each overlapping. Applied to Ila', if a man says 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months', it is one Ila' for four months. But if he says 'two months nor two months' or repeats the divine name, it becomes two oaths, the durations overlap, and because the continuous four-month period is not maintained, it does not constitute Ila'. The passage also contrasts with the case where there is a gap between the oaths, which is discussed later.

Key Terms
يمين (yamīn): An oath; in this context, a vow abstaining from intercourse or speech.
عطف (‘aṭf): Conjunction; joining two phrases with 'wa' (and).
تداخل (tadākhul): Overlap of durations; when two oaths have concurrent periods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Invalid due to inconsistency
D) One oath for two months

Key Takeaway
In Ila', when multiple time periods are mentioned, the decisive factor is whether the negation or divine name is repeated: without repetition, it is one oath with continuous period; with repetition, it is multiple oaths that do not create Ila'.

Effect of a Gap Between Oaths on Ila'
Commentary explaining why a gap between two oaths prevents Ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a gap between two oaths and explain why it prevents Ila'.

Core Idea
Any gap, even an hour, breaks Ila'—the four months must be continuous.

In a previous case, the husband swore to abstain for two months, then immediately swore again for two more, making four continuous months and thus Ila'. But what if there is a time gap between the oaths? In this passage, the commentator clarifies that any interval, no matter how short, prevents Ila' because the continuous four-month abstention is broken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two oaths and their durations
The first oath is for two months, the second oath is for two months, and between them is a gap (e.g., a day). Note that the example 'after a day' is illustrative; any gap works.
2
Recognize that the gap breaks continuity
Ila' requires four consecutive months of abstention without any break. The gap between the oaths is a period when the husband is not bound by any oath, so the total abstention is not continuous.
3
Apply the ruling: no Ila' with a gap
Because the four months are not continuous, the husband is not a muli' (one who makes Ila'). The ruling does not change if the gap is a day or an hour—any interval suffices.
4
Contrast with the case of no gap
In the previous case (without a gap), the two oaths together formed a continuous four-month period, so Ila' was established. This contrast highlights the condition of continuity.
5
Derive the underlying principle
The condition of continuity in Ila' is derived from the requirement of a single continuous period of abstention. A gap nullifies the 'period of Ila'.' This principle applies regardless of the length of the gap.
This is a talil (reasoning) type argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١]قوله: بعد يوم؛ هذا على سبيل التمثيل ; وإلا فالساعة أيضاً كذلك، وبالجملة إذا فصل بينهما بفاصل لا يكون مولياً. [٢]قوله : بعد الشهرين الأولين ; هذا أيضاً قيد اتفاقي ; فإنّ الحكم لا يختلفُ إن لم يقل هذه الكلمة. [٣] قوله : لأن ... الخ ; حاصله : أنّ مدّة الامتناع في الحلف الأوّل كان شهرين ، وفي الحلف الثاني شهران بعدهما، وبين الحلفين مدّة لم يلزمه شيء بالقربان فيها، وهو الزمان الفاصل بينهما، كاليوم مثلاً ، فلم توجد مدة الإيلاء، وهي أربعة أشهر، بخلافِ المسألة السابقة فإنّه لا فاصل هناك.
[1] His saying: 'after a day' is by way of example; otherwise, even an hour is also the same. In summary, if there is any interval between them, he is not a muli'. [2] His saying: 'after the first two months' is also an incidental qualifier; the ruling does not differ if he does not say this word. [3] His saying: 'because' etc.; its summary: that the period of abstention in the first oath was two months, and in the second oath two months after them, and between the two oaths there was a period in which nothing was required of him regarding intercourse, and that is the intervening time, like a day for example, so the period of Ila', which is four months, is not fulfilled, contrary to the previous case where there is no interval.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage provides the reasoning behind the ruling that a gap between two oaths prevents Ila'. The commentator explains that the phrase 'after a day' is just an example; any gap, even an hour, has the same effect. The phrase 'after the first two months' is incidental; the ruling holds even without it. The core reason is that with a gap, the total period of continuous abstention does not reach four months. In the first oath, the husband swore to abstain for two months; then there is a gap where he is not bound; then he swears again for two more months. The four-month period required for Ila' must be continuous and uninterrupted. Since the gap breaks the continuity, it is not Ila'. This is contrasted with the previous case where there was no gap, so the four months are continuous and Ila' is established.

Key Terms
فاصل (fāṣil): A time interval or separation between two oaths.
مدة الإيلاء (muddat al-īlā’): The period of the vow of abstinence, which must be four consecutive months to constitute Ila'.

Key Takeaway
A gap between oaths, however short, prevents Ila' because the required four-month continuous abstention is broken.
