Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
The Legal Nature of Khul': Annulment or Divorce?
Proves that khul' is a type of divorce (talaq) based on Quran and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khul' and explain the evidence from Quran and Sunnah that supports it as a form of divorce (talaq) rather than annulment (faskh).

Core Idea
Khul' is a revocable divorce (talaq bain) in Hanafi fiqh, supported by Quranic placement and Prophetic practice.

The debate over whether khul' is an annulment (faskh) or divorce (talaq) has profound practical consequences for the 'iddah period and the count of divorces. The Hanafi school argues from the Quran and Sunnah that khul' is a type of divorce. This passage presents the evidence and refutes the annulment view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Recognize that the core dispute is whether khul' is a form of talaq (divorce) or faskh (annulment). This determines its legal consequences.
2
Follow the Hanafi Proof (Dalil)
Examine the Quranic placement of the khul' verse (2:229) between verses on talaq, the hadith of Ibn 'Umar that the 'iddah of a mukhalla'ah is that of a divorced woman, the hadith 'khul' is a revocable divorce,' and the incident of Thabit ibn Qays where the Prophet instructed him to 'divorce her with a single divorce.'
Note that the Quranic context and explicit hadith indicate khul' is a type of talaq.
3
Analyze the Counter-Argument and Response
Some scholars argue that the khul' verse is an interjection, implying it is a separate institution (faskh). The Hanafi response: making it an interjection would break the textual coherence; rather, it explains a type of talaq with compensation.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
The practical difference: if khul' is talaq, it reduces the number of divorces and the 'iddah is three menstrual cycles; if faskh, it does not reduce the count and the 'iddah is one cycle (according to some). The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ابن عمر : عدّتها - أي المختلعة - عدة المطلقة، أخرجه ابن حزم ومالك وغيرهما.
ويشهد له حديث : «الخلع تطليقة بائنة» ، أخرجه البيهقي والدارقطني بسند ضعيف، ويدل عليه قول النبي الثابت بن قيس له. طلبت امرأته الخلع : اقبل الحديقة وطلقها تطليقه، أخرجه البخاري.
وكان ذلك أول خلع في الإسلام، كما ورد في رواية أحمد والبزار، وكان الحديقة صداقها أعطاها ثابت له، كما ورد في رواية أبي داود. وكون الخلع طلاقاً هو منطوق القرآن، كما فصله الأصوليون، وتفصيله : إن الله ذكر الطلاق المعقب للرجعة بقوله : الطلاق مرتان، وذكر الثالث بقوله : فإن طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتى تنكح زوجا غيره، وأدرج في أثناء ذكر الطلاق بحث الخلع حيث قال : فإن خفتم : أي علمتم أو ظننتم أيها الحكام، ألا يقيما : أي الزوجان، حدود الله : أي حقوق الزوجية، فلا جناح عليهما : أي فلا إثم على الزوجين، فيما افتدت به، فخص فعل المرأة وهو الافتداء، ولم يذكر فعل الزوج مع أنه جمعها في قوله : فلا جناح عليهما. ومن المعلوم أنه لا يحصل التخلص إلا بفعل الزوج، فعلم بطريق الضرورة أن فعل الزوج هو الذي تقرر فيما سبق، وما لحق وهو الطلاق، فكان هذا بياناً لنوع الطلاق بمال وبغير مال، وفي جعل آية الخلع معترضة بين ذكر الطلاق كما ظنه القائلون بالفسخ فساد التركيب وفي المقام أسئلة وأجوبة مذكورة في كشف الأسرار والتلويح وغيرهما. ثم ثمرة الخلاف بين كون الخلع فسخاً، وبين كونه طلاقاً : هو أن الخلع ينقص عدد الطلاق، ويكون عدة المطلقة على الثاني دون الأول، ولقد أعجب بعض علماء عصرنا حيث ظن أن الخلع فسخ لا يتوقف على تراضي الزوج، ففرق بين امرأة وزوجها جهراً وقهراً من غير رضاه، واستند في ذلك بعبارة الشوكاني في رسالته الدرر البهية مع عدم دلالتها على ما فهمه كما لا يخفى على من تأملها بنظر التحقيق.
Ibn 'Umar said: Her 'iddah – i.e., the mukhalla'ah – is the 'iddah of a divorced woman, reported by Ibn Hazm, Malik and others. And it is supported by the hadith: 'Khul' is a revocable divorce,' reported by al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni with a weak chain, and it is indicated by the Prophet's statement to Thabit ibn Qays when his wife requested khul': 'Accept the garden and divorce her with a single divorce,' reported by al-Bukhari. And that was the first khul' in Islam, as narrated by Ahmad and al-Bazzar, and the garden was her mahr that she gave to Thabit, as narrated by Abu Dawud. And that khul' is divorce is the explicit meaning of the Quran, as elaborated by the usuliyyun. Its detail: Allah mentioned the divorce that is followed by revocability in His saying: 'Divorce is twice,' and mentioned the third in His saying: 'And if he divorces her, she is not lawful to him afterward until she marries another husband,' and He inserted the discussion of khul' in the midst of mentioning divorce where He said: 'And if you fear that they will not uphold the limits of Allah – then there is no blame upon them for what she gives in ransom.' So the action of the woman, which is the ransom, is specified, and the action of the husband is not mentioned, even though He gathered them in His saying: 'there is no blame upon them.' And it is known that the deliverance does not occur except by the husband's action, so it is known by necessity that the husband's action is what was established before and what follows, which is divorce. So this was an explanation of the type of divorce with compensation and without. And making the verse of khul' interjected between the mention of divorce, as those who say it is an annulment think, would corrupt the composition. There are questions and answers on this matter mentioned in 'Kashf al-Asrar' and 'al-Talwih' and others. Then the practical consequence of the difference between khul' being an annulment and it being divorce is that khul' reduces the number of divorces, and the 'iddah is that of a divorced woman according to the second view, not the first. And I was amazed by some contemporary scholars who thought that khul' is an annulment that does not require the husband's consent, so they separated a woman from her husband openly and forcibly without his consent, and they relied for that on the statement of al-Shawkani in his treatise 'al-Durar al-Bahiyya,' even though it does not indicate what they understood, as is not hidden from whoever examines it with the eye of verification.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the legal nature of khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation). The author argues that khul' is a form of divorce (talaq) rather than an annulment (faskh). The evidence includes: (1) the hadith of Ibn 'Umar that the 'iddah of a mukhalla'ah is that of a divorced woman, which implies talaq; (2) the hadith that 'khul' is a revocable divorce' (bainunah sughra); (3) the incident of Thabit ibn Qays where the Prophet instructed him to accept the garden (the mahr) and divorce her with a single divorce; (4) the Quranic placement of the khul' verse between the verses on talaq, indicating it is a type of talaq. The author refutes the view that khul' is faskh by noting that treating the verse as an interjection would break the textual coherence. The practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute is that if khul' is talaq, it reduces the count of divorces and the 'iddah is three menstrual cycles or three months; if it is faskh, it does not reduce the count and the 'iddah is one menstrual cycle according to some. The author criticizes contemporary scholars who erroneously believe khul' does not require the husband's consent, citing a misinterpretation of al-Shawkani's work.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): طلاق تطلبه الزوجة ببذل عوض للزوج ليفارقها، وهو نوع من الطلاق البائن في المذهب الحنفي.
الفسخ (al-faskh): إبطال عقد النكاح من غير وقوع طلاق، لا ينقص عدد الطلاق. هذا هو معنى الفسخ في هذه المسألة.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (ثمرة الخلاف) of the dispute over whether khul' is an annulment (faskh) or a divorce (talaq)?
A) If faskh, it reduces the number of divorces; if talaq, it does not.
B) If faskh, the 'iddah is that of a divorced woman; if talaq, it is less.
C) If talaq, it reduces the number of divorces and the 'iddah is three periods; if faskh, it does not reduce and the 'iddah is one period.
D) Both views agree on the 'iddah but differ on the number of divorces.

Key Takeaway
Khul' is a revocable divorce in Hanafi fiqh, reducing the number of divorces and requiring the 'iddah of a divorced woman.

Is Khul' Faskh or Talaq? The Hanafi Position and Its Practical Consequences
Explaining the linguistic and legal nature of khul' and the fruit of the dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school regards khul' as a type of talaq, identify the practical consequences (thamarah) of the dispute, and critique the misapplication that omits the husband's consent.

Core Idea
Khul' is talaq, not faskh: it reduces the divorce count and requires the husband's consent.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental Hanafi position: that khul' (divorce by redemption) is a form of talaq, not an annulment (faskh). The author, Imam al-Laknawi, argues from the Qur'anic structure and highlights the practical consequences of this classification. He also warns against a contemporary error that treats khul' as a faskh independent of the husband's consent — a view that, he asserts, contradicts the clear sources and consensus. Let's work through the proofs and thamarah step by step.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on khul'
Identify what the Hanafi school says: khul' is a type of talaq, not faskh. This means it is a divorce initiated by the wife's payment but executed by the husband's pronouncement.
Hanafi fiqh treats khul' as one of the forms of talaq.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) consider khul' a faskh (annulment). Their argument is that the khul' verse is interpolated between talaq verses, indicating a separate institution.
The author calls this view a corruption of textual structure (فساد التركيب).
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from the Qur'anic structure
The verse (2:229) says 'then there is no blame upon them' — referring to both spouses. Since release (takhallus) requires the husband's action, and the verse does not mention it separately, it must be the talaq already established in the context.
This is an argument from necessity (ḍarūra) and textual coherence.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Two practical differences: (1) if khul' is talaq, it reduces the number of remaining divorces; if faskh, it does not. (2) The 'iddah period: for a divorced woman, 'iddah is three menstrual cycles; for an annulled marriage, it is one cycle (unless consummated).
This distinction matters for subsequent remarriage and divorce counting.
5
Recognize the contemporary misapplication and the Hanafi response
The author criticizes those who claim khul' is a faskh that does not require the husband's consent. He asserts this contradicts the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus. The proper Hanafi view requires the husband's agreement (or a judge's intervention only under limited conditions).
The author promises to provide hadith evidence to further refute this error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
الخلع
فعل المرأة وهو الافتداء، ولم يذكر فعل الزوج مع أنه جمعها في قوله : فَلَا جُنَاحَ عليهما (٢) ومن المعلوم أنه لا يحصلُ التخلّص إلا بفعل الزوج، فعلم بطريق الضرورة أنّ فعل الزوج هو الذي تقرّر فيما سبق، وما لحق وهو الطلاق، فكان هذا بياناً لنوع الطلاق بمال وبغير مال، وفي جعل آية الخلع معترضة بين ذكر الطلاق كما ظنّه القائلون بالفسخ فساد التركيب وفي المقام أسئلة وأجوبة مذكورة في «كشف الأسرار) و«التلويح» وغيرهما. ثم ثمرة الخلاف بين كون الخلع فسخاً، وبين كونه طلاقاً : هو أن الخلع ينقصُ عدد الطلاق، ويكون عدة المطلقة على الثاني دون الأوّل، ولقد أعجب بعض علماء عصرنا حيث ظنّ أنّ الخلع فسخ لا يتوقف على تراضي الزوج، ففرق بين امرأة وزوجها جهراً وقهراً من غير رضاه (٣) ، واستند في ذلك بعبارة الشوكاني في رسالته «الدرر البهية» مع عدم دلالتها على ما فهمه كما لا يخفى على من تأملها بنظر التحقيق. (١) «كشف الأسرار» (١ : ٩٠). (٢)«التلويح»(١ : ٦٥). (3) أقول : هذا العجب الذي ذكره الإمام اللكنوي صار مقرراً في بعض قوانين الدولة الإسلامية، بحيث صارت المرأة تملك طلاقاً أقوى من طلاق الرجل، فإنها إذا أرادت فراق زوجها ما عليها إلا أن تطلب من القاضي الخلع من زوجها، فيجبر القاضي على المخالعة بينها وبينه ولا تقدم له إلا مهرها، ولا تلتزم بأي حقوق مالية أو معنوية، في حين إذا أراد الزوج أن يطلقها عليه أن يدفع لها مهرها المتأخر مع : نفقة العدة والحضانة وغيرها، وبهذا صار الطلاق بيد المرأة على صورة الخلع هذه أقوى بكثير من طلاق الرجل، ولم يقل به أحد يعتد به من الفقهاء لمخالفته لصريح القرآن والسنة. وقد اغتر بعض المعاصرين بظاهر بعض الأحاديث في تأييد هذه القوانين، وقد فصلت ذلك في كتاب في «اشتراط رضا الزوج في الخلع نقلت فيه النصوص القرآنية والحديثية وإجماع كلمة الفقهاء قاطبة على ذلك ، وأقتصر هاهنا بعض الأحاديث النبوية لمـا وقـع فـيـهـا مـن الإشكال، لعل الله أن ينفع بها لرفع هذا البلاء، فأقول :
Book of Divorce. Khul'. The woman's action is the ransoming, and he did not mention the husband's action even though He (Allah) combined them in His saying: 'then there is no blame upon them' (2:229). It is known that release does not occur except by the husband's action, so it is known by necessity that the husband's action is what was established previously, and what follows is divorce. Thus this is an explanation of a type of divorce with wealth and without wealth. And considering the verse of khul' as interpolated between mentions of divorce, as those who say faskh think, corrupts the structure. In this place there are questions and answers mentioned in 'Kashf al-Asrar' and 'al-Talwih' and others. Then the fruit of the dispute between whether khul' is faskh or talaq: that khul' reduces the number of divorces, and the 'iddah of the divorced woman for the second [opinion] is different from the first. And indeed some scholars of our time amazed me, as they thought that khul' is faskh that does not depend on the husband's consent, so they separated a woman from her husband openly and forcefully without his consent, relying on the words of al-Shawkani in his treatise 'al-Durar al-Bahiyyah' despite it not indicating what they understood, as is not hidden from one who examines it with a scrutinizing eye. (1) 'Kashf al-Asrar' (1:90). (2) 'al-Talwih' (1:65). (3) I say: This wonder that Imam al-Laknawi mentioned has become established in some laws of the Islamic state, such that the woman possesses a divorce stronger than the man's divorce. For when she wants separation from her husband, she only has to request from the judge khul' from her husband, and the judge compels the dissolution between her and him, and she does not give him except her mahr, and she is not obligated to any financial or moral rights. Whereas if the husband wants to divorce her, he has to pay her deferred mahr along with maintenance during the 'iddah, custody, etc. Thus the divorce becomes in the woman's hand in this form of khul' much stronger than the man's divorce, and no reliable jurist has said this because it contradicts the clear Qur'an and Sunnah. And some contemporaries have been deluded by the apparent meaning of some hadith in support of these laws, and I have detailed that in a book on 'The Requirement of the Husband's Consent in Khul'' in which I quoted the Qur'anic and hadith texts and the consensus of all jurists on that. And I restrict myself here to some prophetic hadith due to the ambiguity that has occurred in them, hoping that Allah may benefit by them in removing this affliction. So I say:

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the nature of khul' (divorce by redemption). The author explains that the Qur'anic verse (2:229) implies that khul' is a type of talaq because the husband's action is necessarily required for dissolution, and the verse serves as an explanation of divorce with or without compensation. He criticizes those who consider khul' as faskh (annulment) separate from talaq, arguing that this interpretation disrupts the textual structure of the Qur'an. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this dispute is twofold: first, if khul' is talaq, it reduces the number of divorces the husband has (e.g., from three to two), whereas if it is faskh, it does not; second, the 'iddah (waiting period) for the woman differs—in faskh, the 'iddah is one menstrual cycle, while in talaq it is three. The author then expresses astonishment at some contemporary scholars who mistakenly believe khul' is a faskh that does not require the husband's consent, leading them to forcibly separate couples without the husband's agreement. He refutes this by stating that no reliable jurist has held such a view, as it contradicts the clear texts of the Qur'an and Sunnah, and he promises to present the hadith evidence to clarify the matter.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce by redemption where the wife pays compensation to the husband to obtain her release.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract without counting as a divorce.
طلاق (talaq): Divorce pronounced by the husband.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The number of divorces and the 'iddah period differ.
C) The wife must return the dower.
D) The husband cannot remarry her.

Key Takeaway
Khul' in the Hanafi school is a valid type of talaq that requires the husband's consent and reduces the number of available divorces.

Hadith Evidence for Khul': The Story of Thabit ibn Qays
Presenting multiple narrations of the first khul' in Islam and their explanations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith evidence for khul' and explain how it proves that khul' is a talaq requiring the husband's consent.

Core Idea
Khul' is a talaq with the husband's consent, executed by his pronouncement of divorce.

The previous lesson established the definition of khul'. Now we turn to the primary textual evidence: the hadith of Thabit ibn Qays, widely regarded as the first instance of khul' in Islam. Multiple narrations appear in the major hadith collections, each providing slightly different context but all confirming the same legal structure. This lesson walks through these narrations and the commentators' explanations to extract the Hanafi ruling on khul'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal elements
In each narration, identify the wife's request, the husband's mahr (garden), the Prophet's role, and the outcome (divorce).
Focus on the common thread: return of mahr, one divorce pronounced by the husband.
2
Analyze the Prophet's command
The Prophet said to Thabit: 'Accept the garden and divorce her with one divorce' (طلقها تطليقة). This indicates that the husband must consent and pronounce the divorce; it is not a judicial annulment.
The phrase 'طلقها' is an imperative directed at the husband.
3
Understand the wife's justification
The wife feared falling into disbelief due to her intense dislike. The Prophet did not investigate the claim but proceeded with khul' immediately, showing that the wife's serious aversion suffices.
The hadith does not require proving harm or fault; the wife's fear of kufr is sufficient.
4
Note the variations and their significance
Different narrations mention physical ugliness, broken hand, or fear of disbelief. These variations do not change the ruling but confirm that khul' is permissible for any valid reason that makes marital life unbearable.
The Hanafi position does not restrict khul' to specific causes.
5
Derive the Hanafi ruling
From this hadith, the Hanafi school concludes that khul' is a talaq (not faskh), requires the husband's consent, and the compensation is typically the return of the mahr. The Prophet's command to 'divorce her with one divorce' shows that the husband executes the divorce.
This distinguishes khul' from faskh by a judge, which is a different procedure.

And hadith came regarding khul', especially concerning the story of Thabit ibn Qays with some of his wives. They asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for khul' from Thabit in exchange for each of them returning to him the mahr which he had given to her, which was a garden. And the reason for each one's khul' differed from the other, except that they shared in that he was ugly in appearance. And this story is narrated in most hadith books, but some have summary while others have detail. So whoever wants to know all its events should look at all its narrations. And here it is presented with its wordings and differences along with the words of the commentators in explaining its vocabulary, so that any confusion in understanding it may be removed: On the authority of Ibn Abbas that the wife of Thabit ibn Qays came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, Thabit ibn Qays, I do not blame him for character or religion, but I hate disbelief in Islam.' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Will you return his garden to him?' She said: 'Yes.' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Accept the garden and divorce her with one divorce' in Sahih al-Bukhari (5:2020) and others. And the meaning of 'I do not blame him for character or religion' is that I do not want to leave him due to his bad character or deficiency in his religion. But in some narrations, he broke her hand, so it is interpreted that she meant that... the creation, but it was bad. She did not blame him for that but for something else, as in Fath al-Bari (3:311) and Irshad al-Sari (8:150), which is that he was ugly in appearance. So on the authority of Ibn Amr and Sahl ibn Abi Hathma, they said: 'Habibah was under Thabit ibn Qays ibn Shammas al-Ansari, and she disliked him, and he was an ugly man. So she came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, I see him, and were it not for fear of Allah, I would spit in his face. The Messenger of Allah said: Will you return to him his garden which he gave you as dower? She said: Yes. So he sent to him, and she returned his garden to him, and he separated them, and that was the first khul' in Islam' in Musnad Ahmad (4:3) and al-Mu'jam al-Kabir (6:103) and others. And that is clearly evident in the narration of Ibn Abbas: 'The first khul' in Islam was the wife of Thabit ibn Qays. She came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, my head and Thabit's head will never come together. I lifted the side of the tent and saw him coming among a group, and he was the darkest of them, the shortest in stature, and the ugliest in face. He said: Will you return his garden to him? She said: Yes, and if he wishes, I will add to it. So he separated them' in Fath al-Bari (9:311) and Sharh al-Zurqani (3:238) and others. And the meaning of 'I hate disbelief in Islam' is: I hate that if I stay with him, I would fall into what necessitates disbelief, as in Irshad al-Sari (8:150). And in a narration: 'Except that I fear disbelief' in Sahih al-Bukhari (5:2022). Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari (9:311): 'As if she indicated that her intense dislike of him might lead her to show disbelief so that her marriage would be annulled from him, and she knew that...'

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of hadith evidence (dalil naqli) for the ruling on khul'. The author, after criticizing a mistaken contemporary view, now provides the hadith narrations of the first khul' in Islam, the story of Thabit ibn Qays and his wife. Multiple versions are given: in one, the wife says she does not blame him for character or religion but fears disbelief; in another, she mentions his ugly appearance; in a third, she says she would spit in his face. In all versions, the Prophet asks if she will return the garden (the mahr), and when she agrees, he instructs the husband to accept it and divorce her with one divorce. The key points are: (1) khul' requires the husband's consent (the Prophet commands the husband to divorce), (2) it is a talaq (one divorce is pronounced), (3) the compensation is the return of the mahr. The author also explains the meaning of 'I hate disbelief in Islam' as fear of falling into kufr due to intense dislike, as interpreted by Ibn Hajar.

Key Terms
حديقة (hadiqah): Garden; in the hadith, it was the mahr (dower) given by the husband.
دميم (dhamim): Ugly, of unpleasant appearance.
تطليقة (tatliqah): One pronouncement of divorce.

Khul' of Thabit ibn Qays and the Command of Guidance (Amr Irshad)
Hadith analysis with refutation of a modern misinterpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Prophet's command to Thabit was a command of guidance (irshad) and state the Hanafi ruling that khul' requires the husband's consent.

Core Idea
The Prophet's command was advice, not obligation—khul' requires husband's consent.

The hadith of Thabit ibn Qays is often cited in discussions of khul'. In this lesson, we examine the detailed narrations and the interpretations of major Hadith commentators. We will see how the Prophet's command to 'accept the garden and divorce her' was a command of guidance (amr irshad), not a binding order. This understanding is crucial to avoid a modern misinterpretation that eliminates the husband's role in khul'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core event
Recognize that the wife asked for khul', offering to return the dower because she could not bear her husband's appearance. The Prophet asked if she would return the garden, and she agreed.
2
Locate the Prophetic command
The command 'Accept the garden and divorce her' is the key. Determine whether it is an order of obligation or guidance.
The imperative verb 'اقبل' (accept) can indicate either wujub or irshad depending on context.
3
Distinguish between command types
In Hanafi usul, a command can be amr wujub (obligatory) or amr irshad (advisory). The context of the hadith indicates advice because the wife was unwilling and the Prophet knew Thabit's situation.
Classical commentators explicitly state the command was irshad wa islah.
4
Examine the commentators' explanations
Read the quotes from Ibn Hajar, al-Qastallani, and al-Ayni: all say the command was for guidance and improvement, not obligation.
Ibn Hajar: 'Amr irshad wa islah la ijab'. Al-Ayni: 'Amr lil irshad wal istislah'.
5
Refute the modern misinterpretation
The modern claim that the husband's role is eliminated contradicts the Quran (which gives divorce to the husband) and the consensus of scholars. The command was advisory, so khul' remains valid only with the husband's consent and pronouncement.
The passage provides two proofs: Quranic texts and commentators' statements.

ورد أحاديث في الخلع لا سيما في قصة ثابت بن قيس مع بعض نسائه، كن طلبن من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المخالعة من ثابت مقابل أن تردّ كلّ واحدة منهنّ له المهر الذي أعطاها إياه وهي حديقة، وكان سبب خلع كلّ واحدة منهما مختلف عن الأخرى إلا أن بينهما اشتراك في أنه دميم الخلقة.
وهذه القصة رويت في أكثر كتب الحديث إلا أن في بعضها إجمالاً، الأخرى تفصيل، فمن أراد الاطلاع على تمام أحداثها فعليه أن ينظر في كافة رواياتها، وهاهي معروضة بألفاظها واختلافاتها مع كلام الشراح في بيان مفرداتها؛ ليزول أي إشكال في فهمها: فعن ابن عباس أن امرأة ثابت بن قيس أتت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: يا رسول الله ثابت بن قيس ما أعتب عليه في خلق ولا دين ولكنّي أكره الكفر في الإسلام، فقال رسول الله: أتردين عليه حديقته، قالت: نعم، قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «اقبل الحديقة وطلقها تطليقة» في صحيح البخاري (5: 2020)، وغيره. ومعنى: (وما أعتب عليه في خلق ولا دين) أي لا أريد مفارقته لسوء خلقه ولا لنقصان دينه، لكن في بعض الروايات أنه كسر يدها، فيحمل على أنها أرادت أنه . ء الخلق، لكنها سيء. ما تعيبه بذلك بل بشيء آخر، كما في فتح الباري (3: 311)، وإرشاد الساري (8: 150)، وهو أنه كان دميم الخلقة، فعن ابن عمرو وسهل بن أبي حثمة، قال: «كانت حبيبة تحت ثابت بن قيس بن شماس الأنصاري فكرهته وكان رجلاً دميماً فجاءت إلى النبي، فقالت يا رسول الله إني لأراه، فلولا مخافة الله عزّ وجل لبزقت في وجهه، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: أتردين عليه حديقته التي أصدقك؟ قالت: نعم فأرسل إليه، فردت عليه حديقته، وفرق بينهما، فكان ذلك أول خلع كان في الإسلام» في مسند أحمد (4: 3)، والمعجم الكبير (6: 103)، وغيرها. ويتجلى ذلك بوضوح في رواية ابن عباس: «أول خلع كان في الإسلام امرأة ثابت بن قيس أتت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يا رسول الله لا يجتمع رأسي ورأس ثابت أبداً، إني رفعت جانب الخباء فرأيته أقبل في عدة، فإذا هو أشدّهم سواداً، وأقصرهم قامة، وأقبحهم وجهاً، فقال: أتردين عليه حديقته؟ قالت: نعم وإن شاء زدته، ففرق بينهما» في فتح الباري (9: 311)، وشرح الزرقاني (3: 238)، وغيرهما.
ومعنى: «أكره الكفر في الإسلام»: أي أكره إن أقمت عنده أن أقع فيما يقتضي الكفر، كما في إرشاد الساري (8): (150)، وفي رواية: «إلا أني أخاف الكفر» في صحيح البخاري (5: 2022)، قال ابن حجر في فتح الباري (9): (311): وكأنها أشارت إلى أنها قد تحملها شدة كراهتها له على إظهار الكفر لينفسخ نكاحها منه، وهي كانت تعرف أن ذلك حرام، لكن خشيت أن تحملها شدة البغض على الوقوع فيه. ويحتمل أن تريد بالكفر كفران العشير؛ إذ هو تقصير المرأة في حق الزوج. وقال الطيبي: المعنى أخاف على نفسي في الإسلام ما ينافي حكمه من نشوز وترك وغيرها مما يتوقع من الشابة الجميلة المبغضة لزوجها إذا كان بالضد منها، فأطلقت على ما ينافي مقتضى الإسلام الكفر، ويحتمل أن يكون في كلامها إضمار أي أكره لوازم الكفر من المعاداة والشقاق والخصومة. ويتوافق مع هذا المعنى رواية: «ولكني لا أطيقه» في صحيح البخاري (5: 2021).
ومعنى: «اقبل حديقتها وطلقها تطليقة»، وفي رواية: «فردتها وأمره يطلقها» في صحيح البخاري (5: 2021)، وفي رواية: «فردَّت عليه وأمره ففارقها» في صحيح البخاري (5: 2022)، وفي رواية: «خذ منها، فأخذ منها» في صحيح ابن حبان (10: 110)، وسنن أبي داود (2: 268)، والموطأ (2): 465: أن الأمر فيه من باب النصح من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لثابت بن قيس؛ لأنه لَمَّا علم أن امرأته لا تطيقه ولا يمكنها العيش معه، وقد وافقت على أن توفيه حقه من المال فالأفضل له أن يقبل ذلك، ويطلقها، وهذا ما نصح به الرسول. وليس المعنى كما تأوّله بعض أهل زماننا بأن النبي ألغى دور الرجل في الخلع، واكتفى بموافقة المرأة على دفع البدل؛ لأن هذا الفهم مستشنع وبشع للغاية لم يقله أحد يعتد به لا من السلف ولا من الخلف.
ويمكن بيان بطلان هذا الفهم من وجوه منها:
الأول: أنه يتعارض تعارضاً تاماً مع نصوص القرآن الكريم الواردة في الطلاق؛ إذ أنها ملكت الرجل الحق في الطلاق، ولم تملكه لغيره إلا إذا الرجل ملكه لغيره.
الثاني: أن شراح الحديث المعتمدين نصوا على أن أمره لثابت إنما هو لإرشاده للأفضل والأصلح له، لا أنه يجب عليه طلاقها. فقال ابن حجر العسقلاني في «فتح الباري (9): (312): هو أمر إرشاد وإصلاح لا إيجاب». وقال القسطلاني في إرشاد الساري (8): 150: هو أمر إرشاد وإصلاح لا إيجاب». وقال أيضاً: ولم يكن أمره بفراقها أمر إيجاب وإلزام بالطلاق، بل أمر إرشاد إلى ما هو الأصوب». وقال بدر الدين العيني في عمدة القاري (20): (260): «الأمر فيه للإرشاد والاستصلاح لا للإيجاب والإلزام.
Hadiths have been reported about khul', especially the story of Thabit ibn Qays with some of his wives. They asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for khul' from Thabit in exchange for each one returning to him the dower he had given her, which was a garden. The reason for each one's khul' differed from the other, except that they shared that he was ugly in appearance. This story is narrated in most hadith books, but some are brief and others detailed. Whoever wishes to know all its events should look at all its narrations. Here it is presented with its exact wordings and differences along with the commentators' speech explaining its vocabulary, so that any confusion in understanding it is removed. From Ibn Abbas that the wife of Thabit ibn Qays came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, Thabit ibn Qays, I do not criticize him in character or religion, but I dislike [؟] disbelief in Islam. The Messenger of Allah said: Will you return to him his garden? She said: Yes. The Messenger of Allah said: Accept the garden and divorce her once. [Sahih al-Bukhari (5:2020) and others]. The meaning of 'I do not criticize him in character or religion' is that I do not want to separate from him due to bad character or deficiency in religion, but in some narrations he broke her hand, so it is interpreted that she meant he was [؟] character, but she did not find fault with him in that but in something else, as in Fath al-Bari (3:311) and Irshad al-Sari (8:150), which is that he was ugly in appearance. From Ibn Amr and Sahl ibn Abi Hathma, they said: Habiba was under Thabit ibn Qays ibn Shammas al-Ansari and she disliked him and he was an ugly man. She came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, I see him, and if not for the fear of Allah, I would have spat in his face. The Messenger of Allah said: Will you return to him his garden that he gave as dower? She said: Yes. So he sent to him, and she returned his garden to him, and he separated them. That was the first khul' in Islam. [Musnad Ahmad (4:3), al-Mu'jam al-Kabir (6:103), etc.]. This is clearly seen in the narration of Ibn Abbas: The first khul' in Islam was the wife of Thabit ibn Qays. She came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, my head and Thabit's head will never come together. I lifted the side of the tent and saw him approaching among a group, and he was the darkest, shortest, and ugliest of them. He said: Will you return his garden to him? She said: Yes, and if he wishes, I will add more. So he separated them. [Fath al-Bari (9:311), Sharh al-Zarqani (3:238), etc.]. The meaning of 'I dislike disbelief in Islam' is: I dislike that if I stay with him, I will fall into what necessitates disbelief, as in Irshad al-Sari (8:150). In one narration: 'Except that I fear disbelief' (Sahih al-Bukhari 5:2022). Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari (9:311): It is as if she indicated that her intense dislike for him might cause her to manifest disbelief in order to dissolve her marriage from him, and she knew that was forbidden, but she feared that intense hatred would cause her to fall into it. It is also possible that she meant by 'disbelief' ingratitude towards her spouse, as that is a woman's shortcoming towards her husband's rights. Al-Tibi said: The meaning is that I fear for myself in Islam what contradicts its ruling, such as nushuz, abandonment, etc., which is expected from a beautiful young woman who hates her husband if he is the opposite. So she called what contradicts the requirements of Islam 'disbelief'. It is possible that there is an implicit clause in her speech: I dislike the necessary consequences of disbelief, such as enmity, discord, and dispute. This meaning is consistent with the narration: 'But I cannot bear him' (Sahih al-Bukhari 5:2021). The meaning of 'Accept her garden and divorce her once', and in a narration: 'She returned it and he ordered him to divorce her' (Sahih al-Bukhari 5:2021), and in a narration: 'She returned it to him and he ordered him and he separated from her' (Sahih al-Bukhari 5:2022), and in a narration: 'Take from her, so he took from her' (Sahih Ibn Hibban 10:110, Sunan Abi Dawud 2:268, al-Muwatta 2:465) that the command in it is from the type of advice from the Messenger of Allah to Thabit ibn Qays, because when he knew that his wife could not bear him and could not live with him, and she agreed to give him his due of wealth, the better for him is to accept that and divorce her. This is what the Prophet advised. It is not as some of our contemporaries interpret that the Prophet eliminated the role of the husband in khul' and was satisfied with the woman's agreement to pay the compensation, because this understanding is extremely objectionable and ugly, not said by anyone reliable among the predecessors nor the successors. The invalidity of this understanding can be shown from several aspects: First: It completely contradicts the texts of the Holy Quran regarding divorce, for they gave the man the right to divorce and gave it to no one else unless the man gave it to someone else. Second: The relied-upon hadith commentators stated that his command to Thabit is only to guide him to what is better and more appropriate for him, not that he must divorce her. Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani said in Fath al-Bari (9:312): 'It is a command of guidance and reform, not obligation.' Al-Qastallani said in Irshad al-Sari (8:150): 'It is a command of guidance and reform, not obligation.' He also said: 'His command to separate from her was not a command of obligation and imposition of divorce, but a command of guidance to what is most correct.' Badr al-Din al-Ayni said in Umdat al-Qari (20:260): 'The command in it is for guidance and seeking reform, not for obligation and imposition.'
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a detailed examination of the hadith of khul' involving Thabit ibn Qays and his wife, along with a refutation of a modern misinterpretation. The author first presents the various narrations of the incident, noting differences in wording and detail. The core story is that the wife disliked Thabit due to his ugliness and sought khul', agreeing to return the garden (dower). The Prophet ordered Thabit to accept the garden and divorce her. The author then explains the meanings of key phrases: 'I dislike disbelief in Islam' is interpreted as fear of falling into sin due to intense hatred, or ungratefulness to husband, or actions contrary to Islam. The command 'accept the garden and divorce her' is then clarified: it was a command of guidance (irshad) and advice, not obligation. The author strongly rejects the modern view that the Prophet eliminated the husband's role in khul'. Two proofs are given: (1) the Quran gives the right of divorce to the husband; (2) major hadith commentators explicitly state the command was advisory. Thus, in Hanafi fiqh, khul' requires the husband's consent and pronouncement of divorce; the wife's payment of compensation is accepted, but the husband must agree and divorce.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
أمر إرشاد (amr irshad): A command given as advice or guidance, not as an obligation or legal requirement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith commentators quoted in the passage, what type of command was the Prophet's statement 'Accept the garden and divorce her'?
A) A command of obligation (amr wujub)
B) A command of prohibition (amr nahy)
C) A command of guidance and reform (amr irshad wa islah)
D) A command of permission (amr ibaha)

Key Takeaway
The Prophetic command in the hadith of Thabit ibn Qays was one of guidance, not obligation, so khul' remains valid only with the husband's consent and pronouncement of divorce.

Obligation of the Substitute in Khul'
Proof that the wife must pay the substitute in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the substitute in khul' and prove it using the Quranic verse.

Core Idea
The substitute in khul' is wajib on the wife, and it may be any amount – equal to, more, or less than the mahr.

This lesson examines the obligation of the substitute (badal) in khul' – the compensation the wife pays to obtain her freedom from marriage. The Hanafi school holds that this substitute is wajib (obligatory) upon the wife, and its amount is not restricted to the mahr. The proof is drawn from the generality of the Quranic verse in Surah al-Baqarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm (legal classification) is. Here, the act is the wife paying the substitute in khul', and the ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory).
The passage explicitly says 'ويلزم بدله' – 'and its substitute is obligatory'.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The commentator cites the Quranic verse from Al-Baqarah 2:229: 'فَإِنْ خِفْتُمْ أَلَّا يُقِيمَا حُدُودَ اللَّهِ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا فِيمَا افْتَدَتْ بِهِ'.
This verse is the primary textual evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (aspect of evidence)
Analyze how the verse proves the ruling. The word 'افْتَدَتْ' (ransoms herself) indicates that she must give something in exchange. The generality of 'فِيمَا' (in whatever) implies that any amount is permissible, not restricted to the mahr.
The Hanafi school relies on the general language of the verse.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) restrict the substitute to the amount of the mahr. The Hanafi school disagrees based on the general wording.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is that any amount is valid.

Source Text

كتاب الطلاق باب الخلع
ويلزم بدله
[1]
ويلزم بدله
[1] قوله : ويلزم ؛ أي يجب على المرأة بدل الخلع، سواء كان مقدار المهر أو أزيد منه أو أقل لإطلاق قوله : فيها افْتَدَتْ به (1)

(1) البقرة : من الآية ٢٢٩
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Khul'. And its substitute is obligatory. [1] And its substitute is obligatory. [1] His saying: 'and it is obligatory' means that the substitute in khul' is obligatory upon the woman, whether it is equal to the mahr, more than it, or less than it, due to the generality of His statement: 'in what she ransoms herself with' (1). (1) Al-Baqarah: part of verse 229.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran. The commentator explains the concise ruling from the matn: 'And its substitute is obligatory'. The word 'its' refers to khul'. The ruling is that the substitute (badal) is wajib upon the wife when she initiates khul'. The amount of the substitute is not fixed to the mahr; it may be equal, more, or less. The proof is the general implication of the Quranic verse (2:229) which says 'there is no sin upon them concerning that by which she ransoms herself'. The word 'taftadi' (ransoms) indicates that she must give something, and the verse does not restrict it to the mahr amount. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid by her to the husband.
بدل (badal): The compensation paid by the wife in khul' as the substitute for the husband's right to divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is optional for the wife.
B) It is wajib (obligatory) upon the wife.
C) It is haram (prohibited).
D) It is sunnah (recommended).

Key Takeaway
The substitute in khul' is wajib on the wife and may be any amount, as per the generality of Quran 2:229.

The Obligation of Compensation in Khul'
Ruling that the wife owes compensation in khul' with proof from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of compensation in khul', cite the Quranic and hadith proofs, and explain that the compensation may be equal to, more than, or less than the mahr.

Core Idea
In khul', the wife must pay compensation, which may be more or less than the mahr, as proven by the Quran and Sunnah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the obligation of the wife to pay a compensation (badal) in khul'. It demonstrates that this compensation is wajib, regardless of amount, citing the Quranic verse and the hadith of Thabit ibn Qays.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine what is ruled wajib: the compensation (badal) in khul'. Note that it applies whether the compensation equals, exceeds, or is less than the mahr.
The ruling is general, not restricted to a specific amount.
2
Examine the primary Quranic proof
Locate the verse cited: 'Fala junaha 'alayhima fima iftadat bih' (2:229). Understand that 'iftidā' implies ransom, indicating that the wife gives something to free herself.
The verse uses the term 'iftadat', which shows that compensation is given.
3
Examine the secondary hadith proof
Analyze the hadith of Thabit ibn Qays where the Prophet ordered the husband to accept a garden as compensation and separate from his wife. This establishes the practice and obligation.
The hadith is narrated by Bukhari, indicating its authenticity.
4
Understand the generality of the compensation amount
From the verse and hadith, the compensation is not limited to the mahr. The Prophet did not require equality, so it can be any agreed amount.
This refutes the misconception that compensation must equal the mahr.
5
Note the necessity of the husband's consent
The passage also discusses that khul' requires the husband's consent, as seen in the actions of the Companions. This is a condition for the effectiveness of khul'.
Consent is necessary, but once given, the compensation becomes wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلزم بدله

قوله: ويلزم؛ أي يجب على المرأة بدل الخلع، سواء كان مقدار المهر أو أزيد منه أو أقل لإطلاق قوله تعالى: {فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به} [البقرة:229]. ويدل عليه ما روي عن ثابت بن قيس: أن امرأته اختلعت منه على حديقة، فأمره النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يأخذ الحديقة ويفارقها. وفي رواية: أن امرأة ثابت بن قيس أتت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: يا رسول الله، إني لا أعيب في دين ولا خلق، ولكني أكره الكفر في الإسلام، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: أتردين عليه حديقته؟ قالت: نعم، فأمره النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يأخذ الحديقة ويخلي سبيلها. أخرجه البخاري. وعن سعيد بن المسيب: أن امرأة كانت تحت ثابت بن قيس بن شماس وكان أصدقها حديقة، وكان غيوراً فضربها فكسر يدها، فجاءت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فاشتكت إليه، فقالت: أنا أرد إليه حديقته، قال: أو تفعلين؟ قالت: نعم، فدعا زوجها، فقال: إنها ترد عليك حديقتك، قال: أو ذلك لي؟ قال: نعم، قال: فقد قبلت يا رسول الله، فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: اذهبا فهي واحدة. ثم نكحت بعده رفاعة العابدي فضربها، فجاءت عثمان، فقالت: أنا أرد إليه صداقه، فدعاه عثمان فقبل، فقال عثمان: اذهبي فهي واحدة. أخرجه عبد الرزاق.
الرابع: إن كبار الصحابة ولو كانوا إذ خلعوا امرأة من زوجها جعلوا الأمر إليه إن وافق، كان بها، وإلا فلا، ويؤيد ذلك الرواية السابقة. وفي آخرها: ثم نكحت بعده رفاعة العابدي فضربها فجاءت عثمان فقالت: أنا أرد إليه صداقه فدعاه عثمان فقبل فقال عثمان: اذهبي فهي واحدة.
وأيضا: عن الربيع بنت معوذ بن عفراء، قالت: تزوجت ابن عم لي فشقى بي وشقيت به، وعني بي وعنيت به، وإني استأديت عليه عثمان فظلمني وظلمته، وكثر علي وكثرت عليه، وإنها انفلتت مني كلمة أنا أفتدي بمالي كله، قال: قد قبلت، فقال عثمان: خذ منها، قالت: فانطلقت فدفعت إليه متاعي كله إلا ثيابي وفراشي، وإنه قال لي: لا أرضى، وإنه استاداني على عثمان، فلما دنونا منه، قال: يا أمير المؤمنين الشرط أملك، قال: أجل فخذ منها متاعها حتى عقاصها، قالت: فانطلقت فدفعت إليه كل شيء حتى أجفت بيني وبينه. فهاتان الروايتان واضحتان في الدلالة على أنه لا بد من موافقة الرجل على الخلع؛ لأن الأمر ملكه، ملكه إياه الشارع، فلا يملك أحد نزعه منه كما ورد في الأحاديث والآثار.
And its compensation is required. He said: 'and it is required' meaning it is obligatory upon the woman the compensation of khul', whether it is the amount of the mahr, or more than it, or less, due to the generality of His statement: {Then there is no sin upon either of them concerning that by which she ransoms herself} [al-Baqarah 2:229]. And it is indicated by what is narrated from Thabit ibn Qays: that his wife divorced him in exchange for a garden, and the Prophet ordered him to take the garden and separate from her. In another narration: that the wife of Thabit ibn Qays came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, I do not fault him in religion or character, but I dislike ingratitude in Islam. So the Messenger of Allah said: Will you return to him his garden? She said: Yes, so the Prophet ordered him to take the garden and let her go. Narrated by al-Bukhari. And from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab: that a woman was under Thabit ibn Qays ibn Shammas, and he had given her a garden as dower, and he was jealous and struck her and broke her hand. She came to the Prophet and complained to him, saying: I will return to him his garden. He said: Will you do that? She said: Yes. So he called her husband and said: She returns to you your garden. He said: Is that for me? He said: Yes. He said: Then I have accepted, O Messenger of Allah. So the Prophet said: Go, for it is one divorce. Then she married after him Rifa'ah al-Abidi, who struck her, so she came to Uthman and said: I will return to him his dower. So Uthman called him and he accepted, and Uthman said: Go, for it is one divorce. Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. The fourth: That the senior Companions, when they divorced a woman from her husband, they made the matter up to him: if he agreed, it was effective; otherwise not. This is supported by the previous narration. And also from al-Rabi' bint Mu'awwidh ibn Afra: She said: I married a cousin of mine, and he was miserable with me and I with him, and he was harsh with me and I with him. I sought justice against him with Uthman, and he oppressed me and I oppressed him. And the matter escalated between us. Then a word slipped from me: I will ransom myself with all my wealth. He said: I accept. Then Uthman said: Take from her. So I went and gave him all my belongings except my clothes and bed. He said: I am not satisfied. And he sought justice against me with Uthman. When we approached him, he said: O Commander of the Faithful, the condition is mine. He said: Yes, then take from her her belongings, even her headband. She said: So I went and gave him everything until I was separated from him. These two narrations are clear in indicating that the man's consent is necessary for khul'; because the matter is his property, given to him by the Lawgiver, so no one can remove it from him, as is reported in the hadiths and athar.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the classical Hanafi work 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. The author states the ruling that the wife is obligated to pay the compensation (badal) in khul', regardless of whether it equals the mahr, is more, or less. The proof is the Quranic verse 2:229 which permits khul' with mutual agreement and indicates that compensation is given. Then the author cites hadith of Thabit ibn Qays and others to show the Prophet's approval of khul' in exchange for property, establishing the obligation of payment. The passage also includes a discussion about the necessity of the husband's consent, citing actions of the Companions, particularly Uthman, showing that khul' requires mutual agreement. However, the primary ruling is the obligatory nature of the compensation upon acceptance by the husband.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife with payment of compensation to the husband to free herself from the marriage.
بدل (badal): The compensation paid by the wife to the husband in khul', which may be equal to, more than, or less than the mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, is it permissible for the wife to pay more than the mahr as compensation in khul'?
A) No, it must be exactly the mahr
B) Yes, it is permissible
C) Only if the husband agrees
D) Only if the wife is nashiz

Key Takeaway
Compensation in khul' is mandatory for the wife upon acceptance by the husband, and its amount is unrestricted.

Rulings on Compensation in Nushuz and Divorce for Property
Rulings on khul' compensation and nature of divorce for property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking compensation in khul' when the husband is nashiz versus when the wife is nashiz, and classify divorce for property as ba'in upon acceptance.

Core Idea
Khul' compensation: haram if husband is nashiz, excess over mahr makruh if wife is nashiz, and divorce for property is ba'in.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses the ethics of khul' compensation. It distinguishes between nushuz from the husband or wife, and clarifies the nature of divorce for property. Understanding these rulings is crucial for applying khul' correctly in marital disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three distinct rulings in the passage.
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the rulings on (1) taking compensation when husband is nashiz, (2) taking excess when wife is nashiz, (3) divorce for property.
2
For each ruling, identify the hukm level.
Determine whether it is haram, makruh, wajib, etc. For the first, the text says 'disliked with prohibition'; for the second, 'disliked'; for the third, ruling on nature of divorce.
3
Locate the dalil for each ruling.
Find the evidence cited: Quran 4:20 for husband nashiz, hadith of Thabit's wife for excess, and logical reasoning for ba'in.
4
Determine the legal effect and how the rulings differ based on the source of nushuz.
Understand that the ruling changes depending on which spouse is at fault. Also note that divorce for property is ba'in, not raj'i.
The key is the context of exchange (mu'awada) which makes the divorce contingent on acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره أخذه إن نَشَر، وأخذ الفضل إن نَشَزت، ولو طلقها بمال، أو على مال وقع بائن إن قبلت، ولزمها المال.

[قال:] إن نشز؛ النشوزُ الكراهة والإعراض والتخالف، وحاصله: إن موجب خُلعها إن كان من جانب الزوج يكره له تحريماً أخذ شيء منها، كيف فإنه أرحشها فلا يزيد وحشته بأخذ المال، وعليه يحمل قوله: {وَإِنْ أَرَدْتُمُ اسْتِبْدَالَ زَوْجٍ مَكَانَ زَوْجٍ وَآتَيْتُمْ إِحْدَاهُنَّ قِنطَارًا} [النساء:20] الآية. وإن كان من جانب الزوجة يكره له أخذ الزيادة، لقوله لامرأة ثابت بن قيس التي اختلعت منه: أتردين إليه حديقته التي أعطاك؟ قالت: نعم وزيادة، فقال النبي: أما الزيادة فلا، ولكن حديقته. أخرجه أبو داود والدارقطني. [قوله:] وقع بائن؛ لأن الزوج يستبد بإيقاع الطلاق تنجيزاً وتعليقاً، وقد علقه بقبولها بدلالة مقام المعاوضة، فإن الحكم يتعلق فيه بالقبول، والمرأة تملك التزام المال لولايتها على نفسها، فيلزم عليها المال إن قبلت، ويقع طلاق المعوض به. وإنما كان بائناً لأنها لا تسلم المال لتسلم لها نفسها، وهو في البائن.
And it is disliked to take from her if he is nashiz, and to take the excess if she is nashiz. And if he divorces her for property, or upon property, it occurs as ba'in if she accepts, and the property is owed by her.

He said: 'if he is nashiz' – nushuz is dislike, aversion, and opposition. The summary: if the cause of the khul' is from the husband's side, it is disliked for him, with prohibition, to take anything from her; because he has driven her away so he should not increase her aversion by taking property. Accordingly, His statement is interpreted: {And if you want to replace a wife with another and you have given one of them a heap of wealth} [an-Nisa 4:20] the verse. And if it is from the wife's side, it is disliked for him to take the excess, due to his statement to the wife of Thabit ibn Qays who divorced him: 'Will you return to him his garden which he gave you?' She said: 'Yes, and more.' The Prophet said: 'As for the extra, no, but his garden.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Daraqutni. He said: 'it occurs as ba'in' – because the husband has sole authority to affect divorce, immediately or conditionally, and he has conditioned it upon her acceptance as indicated by the context of exchange; for the ruling is linked to acceptance, and the woman has the capacity to bind herself to pay the property due to her legal capacity over herself, so the property becomes obligatory upon her if she accepts, and the divorce subject to compensation occurs. It is ba'in because she does not hand over the property to secure herself; this is the case in ba'in.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah covers three related rulings. First, if the husband is the one causing discord (nushuz), it is prohibited (haram) for him to take any compensation from the wife in khul', based on Quran 4:20 which forbids taking back what was given. Second, if the wife is nashiz, it is disliked (makruh) for the husband to take more than the mahr, as shown by the hadith where the Prophet refused the extra. Third, if the husband says 'You are divorced for such and such property' or 'upon such property', it is a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce upon the wife's acceptance, and she owes the property. The commentary explains that this is ba'in because the divorce is contingent on acceptance in the context of exchange, and the wife's acceptance obligates the property. The divorce is ba'in because the wife pays the property to free herself, not to retain the marriage.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushuz): The wife's aversion, disobedience, or opposition to the husband, or the husband's harshness and aversion towards the wife.
بائن (ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately, but allows the possibility of remarriage with a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced for 1000 dirhams' and she accepts, what type of divorce occurs?
A) Raj'i (revocable) divorce
B) Ba'in (irrevocable) divorce
C) It is not a valid divorce
D) It depends on the husband's intent

Key Takeaway
Compensation in khul' is restricted: haram from a nashiz husband, only up to mahr from a nashiz wife, and divorce for property is ba'in upon acceptance.

Ruling on Taking Compensation in Khul' When One Spouse is Nashiz
Ruling with proofs on compensation in khul' based on fault.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking compensation in khul' when the husband is nashiz and when the wife is nashiz, and cite the evidence (Quran and Hadith) for each ruling.

Core Idea
When the husband is nashiz, taking any compensation is prohibited; when the wife is nashiz, only the mahr may be taken.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah addresses a critical nuance in khul': who is at fault? The Hanafi school distinguishes between two scenarios based on whether the husband or the wife is nashiz (the one causing marital discord). The ruling is grounded in clear textual evidence—a Quranic verse and a prophetic hadith. Understanding this distinction prevents the common error of assuming that any compensation in khul' is permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: first, when the husband is nashiz (the cause of discord), and second, when the wife is nashiz. Nushuz is defined as hatred, aversion, and discord.
2
Extract the ruling for each scenario
For husband nashiz: it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) for him to take anything as compensation. For wife nashiz: it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) for him to take more than the mahr he gave.
The text uses 'karaha tahriman' for the first and 'yukrahu' without qualification for the second, indicating different levels of prohibition.
3
Locate the dalil for the husband nashiz case
The Quranic verse 4:20 prohibits taking back any gift when divorcing a wife to marry another. By analogy (qiyas), when the husband is nashiz in khul', he is the one causing the breakdown, so he cannot take anything.
The verse is general, but the Hanafi school extends it to khul' through the underlying rationale (illah): fault.
4
Locate the dalil for the wife nashiz case
The hadith of the wife of Thabit ibn Qais (narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Daraqutni) shows that the Prophet ﷺ permitted taking only the garden (the mahr) and prohibited taking extra when the wife sought khul'.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning (dalalah) is clear in prohibiting extra.
5
Understand the rationale
If the husband is at fault, taking money would compound the wife's hardship. If the wife is at fault, returning the mahr is fair compensation for the husband's loss, but demanding more is exploitative.
The ruling protects both parties from injustice, balancing the interests of justice and harmony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره أخذه إن نشز، وأخذ الفضل إن نشزت. قال الشارح: أي أخذ الفضل على ما دفع إليها من المهر. [١] قوله: إن نشز؛ النشوز الكراهة والإعراض والتخالف، وحاصله: إن موجب خلعها إن كان من جانب الزوج يكره له تحريماً أخذ شيء منها، كيف فإنه أرحشها فلا يزيد وحشته بأخذ المال، وعليه يحمل قوله تعالى: {وَإِنْ أَرَدْتُمُ اسْتِبْدَالَ زَوْجٍ مَكَانَ زَوْجٍ وَآتَيْتُمْ إِحْدَاهُنَّ قِنْطَارًا فَلَا تَأْخُذُوا مِنْهُ شَيْئًا} [النساء: 20]. وإن كان من جانب الزوجة يكره له أخذ الزيادة، لقوله ﷺ لامرأة ثابت بن قيس التي اختلعت منه: 'أتردين إليه حديقته التي أعطاك؟' قالت: نعم وزيادة، فقال النبي ﷺ: 'أما الزيادة فلا، ولكن حديقته'. أخرجه أبو داود في المراسيل والدارقطني.
And it is disliked that he takes [anything] if he is nashiz, and [it is disliked that he] takes extra if she is nashiz. The commentator said: meaning taking extra over what he paid to her as mahr. [1] His statement: 'if he is nashiz': nushuz is hatred, aversion, and discord. The summary: if the cause of the khul' is from the husband's side, it is prohibitively disliked for him to take anything from her, because he is the one who drove her away, so he should not increase her aversion by taking money. And upon this is interpreted the statement of Allah the Exalted: {And if you wish to exchange a wife in place of another and you have given one of them a heap [of wealth], take not from it anything} [An-Nisa 4:20]. And if it is from the wife's side, it is disliked for him to take extra, because of his statement to the wife of Thabit ibn Qais who sought khul' from him: 'Would you return to him his garden that he gave you?' She said: 'Yes, and more.' The Prophet ﷺ said: 'As for the extra, no, but [take] his garden.' Narrated by Abu Dawud in al-Marasil and al-Daraqutni.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with its proofs. It addresses the issue of taking compensation in khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with payment) when one spouse is nashiz (disobedient/defaulting). The text identifies two scenarios: first, if the husband is nashiz (he is the cause of the discord), it is makruh tahrimi for him to take any compensation from the wife. The proof is the Quranic verse 4:20, which prohibits taking back any gift given to a wife when divorcing her to marry another, implying that when the husband is at fault, he should not take anything. Second, if the wife is nashiz (she is the cause), it is makruh (tanzihi) for the husband to take more than the mahr he gave her. The proof is the hadith concerning the wife of Thabit ibn Qais: she offered to return the garden (the mahr) plus extra, but the Prophet ﷺ prohibited the extra, allowing only the garden. Thus, taking extra is disliked but not prohibited. The commentary clarifies that 'nushuz' means hatred and aversion, and the ruling is based on who is responsible for the breakdown.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushūz): In this text, nushuz means hatred, aversion, and discord (كراهة وإعراض وتخالف) that leads to marital breakdown; it is attributed to either the husband or the wife.
خلع (khul‘): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband; the passage discusses rulings on what compensation can be taken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling if a husband who is nashiz takes compensation from his wife in khul'?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked but not prohibited (makruh tanzihi)
C) Prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi)
D) Obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of compensation in khul' depends on who is at fault: the husband cannot take anything if he is the cause of discord, and the wife cannot give more than the mahr if she is the cause.

Divorce for Compensation Results in Baiyin Talaq
Explains the ruling and reason for bain in divorce for compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a divorce pronounced for compensation and explain why it becomes bain (irrevocable) in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A divorce for compensation is bain because the wife pays to end the marriage, not to remain in a revocable state.

In this passage, the commentator explains the legal effect when a husband offers a divorce in exchange for a payment (maal). The key point is that the divorce is conditional upon the wife's acceptance, and once accepted, it becomes an irrevocable (bain) divorce. This is analogous to khul', where the wife gives compensation to obtain her freedom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a pronouncement of talaq by the husband with an offer of compensation (e.g., 'You are divorced for a thousand dirhams'). The ruling: it occurs as bain (irrevocable) if the wife accepts, and the compensation becomes wajib (binding) on her.
The compensation is a type of mal (property), not necessarily money.
2
Understand the conditional nature
The divorce is not immediate; it is conditional upon the wife's acceptance. The context of exchange (mu'awada) indicates that the husband's statement is an offer, not an irrevocable pronouncement.
This differs from a regular talaq which is effective immediately.
3
Recognize why it becomes bain
The reasoning: in a raj'i divorce, the husband can take the wife back during iddah, so the marriage is not fully severed. But here, the wife pays compensation to end the marriage completely. Therefore, it must be bain, analogous to khul'.
Thus, the type of divorce is determined by the context and the wife's payment.
4
Note the consequence: compensation is binding
Once the wife accepts, the specified compensation becomes wajib upon her. She must pay it, and the divorce takes effect as bain.
If she does not accept, no divorce occurs and no payment is due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو طلقها بمال، أو على مال وقع بائن إن قبلت، ولزمها المال. [٢] قوله: وقع بائن؛ لأنّ الزوج يستبد بإيقاع الطلاق تنجيزاً وتعليقاً، وقد علقه بقبولها بدلالة مقام المعاوضة، فإنّ الحكم يتعلّق فيه بالقبول، والمرأة تملك التزام المال لولايتها على نفسها فيلزم عليها المال إن قبلت، ويقع طلاق المعوّض به. وإنما كان بائناً؛ لأنها لا تسلّم المال لتسلم لها نفسها، وهو في البائن، فإنّ الرجعي لا يقطع النكاح، بل هو أحق بالرجعة، ولهذا يقع في الخلع البائن. كذا في «النهاية» و«العناية».
And if he divorces her for a property, or upon a property, it occurs as bain if she accepts, and the property is binding on her. [2] His statement: 'it occurs as bain' because the husband has the exclusive right to effect divorce immediately or conditionally, and he has conditioned it upon her acceptance by indication of the context of exchange (mu'awada), so the ruling depends on acceptance. The woman has the capacity to undertake the property obligation due to her authority over herself, so the property becomes binding on her if she accepts, and a divorce compensated thereby occurs. And it is bain because she does not hand over the property so that she may retain herself (i.e., the marriage), and that is in the case of bain divorce, for the raj'i divorce does not sever the marriage, but rather he has more right to take her back. Hence khul' results in bain. This is stated in al-Nihaya and al-Inaya.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage examines the ruling when a husband says 'You are divorced for a thousand dirhams' or similar. The text clarifies three points: (1) The divorce is conditional upon the wife's acceptance because the context of exchange (mu'awada) indicates that the pronouncement is not an immediate divorce but an offer. (2) If she accepts, the compensation (the specified property) becomes wajib (obligatory) on her. (3) The divorce that occurs is bain (irrevocable), not raj'i (revocable). The reasoning is: in a raj'i divorce, the husband retains the right to take back the wife during the iddah, so the marriage is not fully severed. But here, the wife pays compensation precisely to end the marriage fully; she pays to be free, not to remain in a revocable state. Therefore, the divorce is bain. This is the relied-upon position, as mentioned in al-Nihaya and al-Inaya.

Key Terms
بائن (bā’in): In this context, bain means a divorce that is irrevocable, where the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage and mahr.
رجعي (raj‘ī): A revocable divorce where the husband can take back the wife during the iddah without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced for 500 dirhams' and she accepts, what type of divorce occurs?
A) Raj'i (revocable) divorce because the word 'talaq' is used
B) Bain (irrevocable) divorce because it is an exchange
C) The divorce does not occur until she pays
D) The divorce occurs as bain only if she fails to pay

Key Takeaway
Divorce for compensation is irrevocable (bain) and the compensation is binding on the wife upon acceptance.

Khul' or Talaq with Invalid Compensation
Rulings on divorce with invalid or nonexistent compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling and explain the reasoning for khul' and talaq when the compensation is invalid, and for the scenario 'what is in my hand' when there is nothing.

Core Idea
When compensation is invalid, divorce is valid but payment is void; bain vs raj'i hinges on whether wording is kinaya or sarih.

This lesson examines two related scenarios where the compensation in a khul' or talaq agreement is legally invalid. The first involves items like wine or pork that cannot be valid consideration in a contract. The second involves an unspecified compensation that turns out to be nonexistent. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the effect of the wording used—khul' (a kinaya) and talaq (sarih)—and the validity of the divorce itself despite the void compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling for each scenario
First, note the two main scenarios: (1) khul' or talaq with inherently invalid compensation (e.g., wine, pork); (2) khul' on 'what is in my hand' when nothing exists. For each, state the hukm: the divorce occurs, but no compensation is due. In scenario (1), the type is bain for khul', raj'i for talaq. In scenario (2), the divorce is bain.
The compensation must be valid property (mal muttaqawwim). Wine and pork are not property in Islamic law.
2
Understand the reason for validity of divorce
The divorce is valid because the husband's offer was implicitly conditioned on the wife's acceptance. Once she accepts, the condition is fulfilled and the divorce takes effect. The invalidity of compensation does not nullify the divorce itself.
The ruling preserves the intention to dissolve the marriage despite the flawed exchange.
3
Analyze the difference between bain and raj'i in scenario (1)
When the compensation is void, the wording becomes the decisive factor. 'Khul'' is a kinaya (allusive) term; without valid compensation, it defaults to a bain divorce. In contrast, 'talaq' is sarih (explicit) and normally effects a raj'i divorce; it only becomes bain if paired with a valid compensation. Since the compensation is void, the default explicit meaning prevails, giving a raj'i divorce.
The linguistic nature of the words determines the post-divorce consequences.
4
Apply the same reasoning to the 'what is in my hand' scenario
Here the wife offers unspecified compensation. If nothing exists, the compensation is effectively nonexistent. The ruling follows the same logic: the khul' is valid (bain) but no payment is due. The compensation is void because the object never existed.
This case falls under the second facet: when the named item may or may not be property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو خلع أو طلق: بخمر أو خنزير لم يجب شيء، ووقع بائن في الخلع، ورجعي في الطلاق. وإن قالت: خالعني على ما في يدي، أو على ما في يدي من مال، أو من دراهم، ففعل ولا شيء في يدها. [١] قوله: بخمر أو خنزير؛ ذكرهما على سبيل التمثيل، والحاصل: أن العوض إن كان مما لا يصح جعله عوضاً كالخمر والخنزير والميتة وغيرها، فإن كان في الخلع لا يجب شيء، ويقع طلاق بائن، وإن كان في الطلاق لا يجب شيء، ويقع رجعي. أما عدم وجوب شيء عليها فلبطلان ما جعله عوضاً، ولم ترض بغيره، حتى يجب عليه، وأما وقوع الطلاق فيهما فلأنه كان معلّقاً معنى على قبول المرأة، وقد وجد، وأما الافتراق بالبينونة والرجعة فإنّه لما بطل العوض بقي العامل في صورة الخلع، لفظ: الخلع؛ وهو من الكنايات، فيقعُ به بائن، وفي صورة الطلاق لفظ: الطلاق؛ وهو صريح يقعُ به الرجعي، وإنّما يقعُ به البائن إذا كان بعوض، وقد بطل. كذا في «الهداية» وحواشيهما. (٢) قوله: وإن قالت... الخ؛ الأصل في هذا الباب أن الخلع إن كان على المهر فذاك، وإن كان على غيره فهو على أوجه: أحدها: أن يكون ذلك المسمّى غير متقوم كالخمر، فيقع فيه الطلاق من دون وجوب شيء. وثانيها: أن يحتمل كونه مالاً، وغيره، مثل ما في بيتها أو يدها من شيء، وكذا ما في يديها؟
And if he performs khul' or pronounces talaq with wine or a pig, nothing is incumbent, and it occurs as bain in khul' and as raj'i in talaq. And if she says: 'Divorce me (khul') on what is in my hand, or on what is in my hand of property, or of dirhams,' and he does so and there is nothing in her hand. [1] His statement: 'with wine or pig'; he mentions them as examples. The summary: if the compensation is something that cannot validly be made a compensation, like wine, pig, carrion, etc., then if it is in khul', nothing is incumbent and a bain talaq occurs; if it is in talaq, nothing is incumbent and a raj'i talaq occurs. As for nothing being incumbent on her, it is because what she made as compensation is null, and she did not consent to any other, such that it would be binding on him. As for the occurrence of divorce in both, it is because it was implicitly conditioned upon the woman's acceptance, and that has occurred. As for the difference between bain and raj'i, when the compensation is nullified, in the form of khul', the word 'khul'' remains; it is a kinaya (allusive expression), so it results in bain. In the form of talaq, the word 'talaq' is used; it is explicit (sarih), so it results in raj'i. It only results in bain if it is with valid compensation, and that is nullified. This is stated in al-Hidaya and its annotations. (2) His statement: 'And if she says...' the principle in this chapter is that if khul' is for the mahr, then it is that; if it is for something else, then it has several facets: one of them is that the named thing is not valuable (muttaqawwim) like wine, so the divorce occurs without anything being incumbent. Second: that it may be property or not, such as what is in her house or hand of something, and similarly what is in her hands?
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios involving invalid compensation in divorce: (1) When the compensation is inherently invalid (e.g., wine or pork), the ruling differs depending on the wording: if the wording is 'khul'', the divorce is bain but no compensation is due; if the wording is 'talaq', the divorce is raj'i and no compensation is due. The reason is that 'khul'' is a kinaya (allusive) term, and when the compensation is void, it still triggers a bain divorce by default. 'Talaq' is explicit and results in raj'i unless accompanied by valid compensation. (2) When the wife says 'Divorce me (khul') on what is in my hand' and there is nothing, the divorce is bain but no compensation is due because the compensation was unspecified and nonexistent. The commentary outlines a principle: khul' on the mahr is straightforward; on something else, there are facets: (a) if the named item is non-valuable (like wine), divorce occurs without compensation; (b) if the named item could be property or not (like 'something in the house'), the ruling depends on existence.

Key Terms
كناية (kināyah): An allusive expression that does not directly mention divorce but can imply it; 'khul'' is considered a kinaya in the context of divorce.
صريح (ṣarīḥ): An explicit expression that directly indicates divorce without need for intention; 'talaq' is explicit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'I divorce you (talaq) for this bottle of wine,' the divorce is:
A) Bain divorce, no compensation due
B) Raj'i divorce, no compensation due
C) Bain divorce, wife must pay value of wine
D) No divorce because consideration is invalid

Key Takeaway
When compensation in khul' or talaq is invalid (non-valuable or nonexistent), the divorce is valid but payment is void; the type depends on the wording's linguistic nature.
