Ruling on Khul' and Talaq with Invalid Consideration
Ruling on khul'/talaq with invalid consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce with invalid consideration and distinguish the effects on khul' versus talaq.

Core Idea
A divorce with invalid consideration is valid, but the type depends on the word: khul' = ba'in, talaq = raj'i.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we examine a scenario where a husband uses wine or pig as consideration for khul' or talaq. According to Hanafi fiqh, the divorce takes effect even though the consideration is invalid. However, the nature of the divorce differs: if the word 'khul'' was used, it becomes an irrevocable divorce (ba'in); if 'talaq' was used, it remains revocable (raj'i). This ruling highlights the Hanafi principle that the validity of the divorce is independent of the validity of the consideration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The acts are khul' and talaq with invalid consideration (wine, pig, carrion). The ruling: the divorce is valid (sahih) but no consideration is due. The type differs: khul' is ba'in, talaq is raj'i.
2
Understand the hukm level
The divorce is sahih but the type (raj'i or ba'in) depends on the word used. For khul', it becomes ba'in because the word is kinayah (allusive) and without valid consideration, it defaults to ba'in. For talaq, it remains raj'i because the word is sarih (explicit) and only becomes ba'in if a valid consideration is specified.
In Hanafi usul, kinayah forms of talaq result in ba'in unless specified otherwise.
3
Locate the dalil
The passage uses rational reasoning (dalil aqli): the divorce is suspended on the wife's acceptance, which has occurred. The invalidity of the consideration means the wife did not consent to any other obligation, so nothing is owed. The divorce occurs regardless.
No explicit Quran or Hadith is cited; instead, juristic reasoning (istidlal) is used.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that khul' with invalid consideration is itself invalid (batil) because khul' is a contract requiring valid consideration. Therefore, no divorce would occur. The Hanafi view differs by treating khul' primarily as a form of talaq.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is considered the relied-upon (mufta bihi) within the school. The practical consequence: the marriage ends irrevocably (ba'in) in khul', but the husband can take back the wife during iddah in talaq without a new contract.
The school's authority weight is zahir al-riwayah from the six core works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو خَلَع أو طلقَ : بخمر أو خنزير لم يجب شيء، ووقع بائن في الخلع، ورجعي في الطلاق. قوله : بخمر أو خنزير ؛ ذكرهما على سبيل التمثيل، والحاصل : أن العوض إن كان مما لا يصح جعله عوضاً كالخمر والخنزير والميتة وغيرها، فإن كان في الخلع لا يجب شيء، ويقع طلاق بائن، وإن كان في الطلاق لا يجب شيء، ويقع رجعي. أما عدم وجوب شيء عليها فلبطلان ما جعله عوضاً، ولم ترض بغيره، حتى يجب عليه، وأما وقوع الطلاق فيهما فلأنه كان معلّقاً معنى على قبول المرأة، وقد وجد، وأما الافتراق بالبينونة والرجعة فإنّه لَمَّا بطل العوض بقي العامل في صورة الخلع، لفظ : الخلع ؛ وهو من الكنايات، فيقعُ به بائن، وفي صورة الطلاق لفظ : الطلاق ؛ وهو صريح يقعُ به الرجعي، وإنّما يقعُ به البائن إذا كان بعوض، وقد بطل . كذا في «الهداية وحواشيهما.
And if he performed khul' or divorced with wine or pig, nothing is owed, and it occurs as ba'in in khul' and raj'i in divorce. [Commentary:] He said: 'with wine or pig' – he mentioned them as examples. The conclusion: if the consideration is something that cannot be validly made consideration, like wine, pig, carrion, etc., then if it is in khul', nothing is owed and it occurs as an irrevocable divorce; if it is in divorce, nothing is owed and it occurs as a revocable divorce. As for the fact that nothing is owed by her, it is because what was made consideration is invalid, and she did not consent to anything else that would obligate him. As for the occurrence of divorce in both cases, it is because it was effectively suspended on the woman's acceptance, and that has occurred. As for the difference between irrevocability and revocability: when the consideration is invalidated, the operative word remains. In the case of khul', the word 'khul'' is a kinayah, so it is an irrevocable divorce. In the case of divorce, the word 'talaq' is explicit (sarih), so it is a revocable divorce; it only becomes irrevocable if with consideration, and that has been invalidated. This is in Al-Hidayah and its glosses.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah on the consequences of khul' or talaq when the consideration (iwad) is something that is not legally valuable (ghayr mutaqawwim) like wine, pig, or carrion. The author states that in such a case, no consideration is due from the wife, but the divorce still takes effect. However, the type of divorce differs: in khul' it is ba'in (irrevocable), while in talaq it is raj'i (revocable). The commentary explains the reasoning: the invalidity of the consideration means it is as if no consideration was specified, so the wife is not obligated to pay anything. The divorce occurs because the husband's offer was conditional on her acceptance, and that acceptance happened. As for the difference in effect, it is due to the nature of the words used: 'khul'' is a kinayah (allusive) term for divorce, and when used without a valid consideration, it results in a ba'in divorce (since it is not revocable except with a new contract). In contrast, 'talaq' is a sarih (explicit) term, and when used without a valid consideration, it results in a raj'i divorce. The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle that a kinayah divorce is ba'in unless specified otherwise, while a sarih divorce is raj'i unless made ba'in by an accompanying condition (like a valid consideration).

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce by redemption where the wife gives consideration to the husband for divorce.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce; the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage contract.
رجعي (raj'i): Revocable divorce; the husband can take back the wife during the iddah without a new contract.
عوض (iwad): Consideration given by the wife in khul' in exchange for divorce.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a divorce with invalid consideration is valid; the type (ba'in/raj'i) depends on the word used.

Khul' with Unspecified Consideration: Cases and Rulings
Ruling on khul' with unspecified consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for each of the three cases of khul' with unspecified consideration and explain the principle of specification (tasmia) that governs the obligation.

Core Idea
The validity of khul' depends on whether the wife specified valuable property; if not, the divorce is free of compensation.

When a wife says 'khul' me on what is in my hand,' the ruling depends on how she describes that thing. The Hanafi school distinguishes three subcases, each with a different outcome, based on whether she mentioned 'property' or 'dirhams.' This lesson unpacks those rules and the broader principles from Al-Dhakhirah that guide the determination of consideration in khul'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases in the matn
The base text presents three scenarios: (1) 'what is in my hand' (unspecified), (2) 'what is in my hand of property', (3) 'of dirhams'. For each, determine what is owed if she has nothing.
The key is whether she specified property (mal) or a specific type (dirhams).
2
Understand the principle of specification (tasmia)
In the first case, no specification means the husband accepted a free divorce. In the second, she specified property, so the husband did not consent to free, but since the amount is unknown (jahalah), she returns any mahr she took. In the third, dirhams are a known category, so the minimum plural (three) is owed.
3
Map the six categories from Al-Dhakhirah
The commentary expands to six scenarios: invalid consideration (wine), ambiguous (house contents), future property (fruit), unknown amount (furniture), known category with minimum (dirhams), mislabeled (vinegar turns out wine). Each has a distinct ruling.
These categories help in practice when the wife’s description is ambiguous.
4
Recognize the role of jahalah (ignorance)
Hanafi school tolerates jahalah in khul' because the wife is buying her freedom, and the husband can waive precision. But when the consideration is impossible to value, the contract still valid but the husband can recover the mahr.
Compare with Shafi'i position that requires known consideration at the time of contract.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is consider khul' with unspecified consideration invalid. Hanafis uphold validity and adjust the obligation based on what was specified. The practical difference is whether the talaq takes effect at all.
The term 'mukhtalaf fih' applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قالت : خالعني على ما في يدي، أو على ما في يدي من مال ، أو من دراهم، ففعل ولا شيء في يدها لم يجب شيء في الأولى، وتردُّ ما قبضت في الثانية، وثلاثةُ دراهم في الثالثة. قوله : وإن قالت... الخ ؛ الأصل في هذا الباب أن الخلع إن كان على المهر فذاك، وإن كان على غيره فهو على أوجه: أحدها: أن يكون ذلك المُسَمَّى غير متقوم كالخمر، فيقع فيه الطلاق من دون العوض. وثانيها : أن يحتمل كونه مالاً ، وغيره، مثل ما في بيتها أو يدها من شيء، وكذا ما في بطن شاتها أو جاريتها ، فإن وُجد المسمّى وكان مالاً متقوماً وجب، وإلا وقع الطلاق من غير شيء. وثالثها : أن يكون مالاً سيوجد مثل ما تثمر نخيلها العام، فعليها ردّ ما قبضت من المهر، سواء وجد ذلك أو لا. ورابعها أن يكون مالاً لا يوقف على قدره ، مثل : ما في بيتها أو يدها من المتاع، فإن وجد منه شيء فهو الواجب، وإلا ردّت المهر. وخامسها : أن يكون مالاً له مقدار معلوم مثل ما في يدها من الدراهم، فإن أقله ثلاث، فله الثلاثة أو الأكثر. وسادسها : أن تسمّي مالاً وتشير إلى غير مال، كهذا الخل فإذا هو خمر، فإن علم بأنه خمر فلا شيء له، وإلا رجع بالمهر، هكذا في «الذخيرة». قوله : في الأولى؛ لعدم وجود التسمية، ويقع الطلاق مجاناً لقبوله ورضاه. قوله : في الثانية ؛ أي فيما إذا قالت : علي ما في يدي من مال ؛ لأنها لَمَّا سمت مالاً لم يكن الزوج راضياً بوقوعه مجاناً، ولا سبيل إلى إيجاب المسمى أو قيمته للجهالة، فتعين ردّ ما قبضت منه من المهر ، فإن لم تكن قبضت شيئاً منه لا شيء عليها. كذا في «البحر». قوله : وثلاثة ؛ وكذا إذا قالت : على ما في هذا المكان من الشياه أو البغال أو الحمير ونحو ذلك ، فيجب ثلاثة منها. قوله : في الثالثة ؛ لأنها ذكرت الدراهم بلفظ الجمع، ولا حد لأكثره، فوجب الأقل المتيقن.
And if she says: 'Divorce me by khul' in exchange for what is in my hand,' or 'for what is in my hand of property,' or 'of dirhams,' and he does so and there is nothing in her hand, then nothing is owed in the first case, and she returns whatever she had received (of the mahr) in the second case, and three dirhams in the third case. [Commentary:] He said: 'And if she says...' The principle in this chapter is that if khul' is on the mahr, that is one thing; if on other than the mahr, it has several aspects: First: that the specified thing is not valuable, like wine, then divorce occurs without consideration. Second: that it could be property or not, like 'what is in her house or hand' and similarly 'what is in the belly of her sheep or her slave-girl'; if the specified thing is found and is valuable, it is obligated; otherwise divorce occurs without anything. Third: that it is property that will exist, like the fruit of her palm trees this year; she must return whatever she took of the mahr, whether that exists or not. Fourth: that it is property whose amount is unknown, like furniture in her house or hand; if something of it is found, it is obligated; otherwise she returns the mahr. Fifth: that it is property with a known amount, like dirhams in her hand; the minimum is three, so he gets three or more. Sixth: that she specifies property and points to something that is not property, like 'this vinegar' but it is wine; if he knew it was wine, he gets nothing; otherwise he takes back the mahr. This is in Al-Dhakhirah. He said: 'In the first case' – because of the absence of specification, and the divorce occurs for free due to his acceptance and consent. He said: 'In the second case' – that is, when she says 'on what is in my hand of property'; since she specified property, the husband was not content with it occurring for free, and there is no way to obligate the specified thing or its value due to ignorance; so he takes back whatever she had received of the mahr; if she had received nothing, then nothing is owed by her. This is in Al-Bahr. He said: 'And three' – similarly if she says 'on what is in this place of sheep, mules, donkeys, etc.', then three of them are obligated. He said: 'In the third case' – because she mentioned dirhams in the plural, and there is no limit for the most, so the least that is certain is obligated.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage deals with khul' where the wife offers an unspecified consideration that is conditional on finding something in her possession. Three subcases are given: (1) She says 'on what is in my hand' without specifying property; nothing is owed because there was no specification of valuable property, and the husband accepted with that understanding. (2) She says 'on what is in my hand of property'; here she specified property, so the husband would not have intended a free divorce. Since it is unknown what exactly is in her hand, the consideration is void, and she must return any mahr she had received (if any). (3) She says 'of dirhams'; since dirhams are a specific type of property, but she used the plural (dirhams) without specifying number, the minimum obligatory is three (the smallest plural). The commentary expands with six categories from Al-Dhakhirah: (a) invalid consideration (wine), (b) ambiguous whether property or not (e.g., what is in house/hand), (c) future property (fruit), (d) unknown amount (furniture), (e) known category with minimum (dirhams), (f) mislabeled property (vinegar turned out wine). These categories are guidelines for determining whether the consideration is valid and what is owed.

Key Terms
مُسَمَّى (musamma): The specified thing named as consideration in the khul' contract.
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Legally valuable property that can be owned and traded.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about the exact amount or nature of the consideration.
الثلاثة (ath-thalatha): Three dirhams; the minimum plural considered for dirhams in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where the wife says 'Khul' me on what is in my hand of dirhams' and she has nothing, what is owed according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Nothing, because she has nothing.
B) She must return any mahr received.
C) Three dirhams.
D) The value of three dirhams.

Key Takeaway
Three dirhams are owed when the wife offers khul' in exchange for 'dirhams' without a number, even if she has none in hand.

10 min
Six Cases of Khul' with Unknown Dower
Commentary enumerating and explaining six khul' dower cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six distinct cases of khul' with unknown dower and apply the Hanafi ruling to determine what the wife must pay in each scenario.

Core Idea
Unknown khul' dower leads to specific default rulings: nothing, return of dower, or minimum of three dirhams.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah presents six distinct scenarios in khul' (divorce initiated by the wife) where the dower amount or existence is uncertain. Each case has a specific ruling based on the principle that the husband's consent to a gratuitous divorce is not presumed, but the precise payment is determined by what is known. We will walk through each case systematically, building from the simplest to the most complex.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first two cases
Case 1: Wife specifies no dower → divorce is gratuitous, she owes nothing. Case 2: Wife says 'upon me is what is in my hand of wealth' but no wealth is found → she must return any dower she received from the husband.
Key distinction: absence of specification vs. presence of vague specification.
2
Analyze the third case: plurality of dirhams or animals
If wife says 'upon me is what is in this place of sheep, mules, etc.', or 'dirhams' in plural, the minimum (three dirhams or three animals) is due because the plural in Arabic indicates at least three, and the minimum is the assured amount.
Hanafi principle: al-jam' yufidu al-adnā (the plural gives the minimum).
3
Examine cases four and five: known vs. unknown quantity
Case 4: Dower is goods whose amount is unknown (e.g., furniture in house) → if any found, that is due; otherwise, she returns the dower. Case 5: Dower is of a known type with a known minimum (e.g., dirhams) → the minimum (three) is due, or more if found.
The goal is to give effect to the husband's consent as much as possible.
4
Study case six: mistaken identity
Wife names 'vinegar' but it turns out to be wine (not valuable property). If husband knew it was wine, nothing is due (he accepted the risk). If he was unaware, he recovers the dower because the named item is non-existent as valuable property.
Wine is ghayr mutaqawwim (non-valuable), so cannot be dower.
5
Derive the underlying principle
In all cases, the khul' is valid. The payment is determined by: (a) what the wife named if it exists and is valuable, (b) the minimum of the named category, (c) return of received dower if named item absent, or (d) nothing if no specification or if husband knowingly accepted a non-valuable item.
The husband's consent to a gratuitous divorce is not presumed unless explicitly stated or implied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) أي لعدم وجود التسمية ويقع الطلاق مجاناً لقبوله ورضاه. ينظر: ((الدر المختار»(٢: ٥٦١). (۲) «البحر الرائق» (٤: ٩٦).
Nothing is due in the first case; she returns what she received in the second; and three dirhams in the third. Fourth: that it be wealth whose amount is unknown, like goods in her house or in her hand; if any of it is found, that is due; otherwise she returns the dower. Fifth: that it be wealth of a known amount, like dirhams in her hand; its minimum is three, so he gets three or more. Sixth: that she name wealth but point to something that is not wealth, like this vinegar when it is wine; if he knew it was wine, nothing is due; otherwise he recovers the dower. Thus in al-Dhakhira. Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the rules of khul' when the dower is unknown or conditional. It enumerates six distinct cases from legal works. In the first case, if the wife specifies no dower at all, the divorce is gratuitous and she owes nothing. In the second case, if she says 'upon me is what is in my hand of wealth,' but no specific items are found, she must return any dower she already received because the husband did not agree to a gratuitous divorce and the specified dower is impossible to enforce. In the third case, if she promises dirhams, the minimum known (three) is due. Similar rules apply for sheep, mules, etc. The fourth case involves goods in her possession—if any are found, she gives those; otherwise, she returns the dower. The fifth case is like dirhams: the minimum of three is due. The sixth case is when she mistakenly names vinegar but it turns out to be wine (wine is not valuable); if the husband knew it was wine, nothing is due; otherwise he gets the dower. The commentary clarifies that the divorce in the first case is gratuitous (no payment) because the husband accepted it with no dower. In the second, because the wife named wealth but it was unknown, she must return the dower she received. In the third, the plural form 'dirhams' requires at least three—the assured minimum—as per Hanafi principles.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for payment (usually the dower or some compensation). It becomes a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce.
المسمى (al-musamma): The specifically named or designated dower in the khul' agreement.
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Property that is legally valuable and permissible to trade in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where the wife says 'upon me is what is in my hand of wealth' but no wealth is found, what must she do?
A) She owes nothing because the dower is unknown.
B) She must return any dower she already received from the husband.
C) She must pay the minimum amount of three dirhams.
D) The khul' is invalid and she must return all dower and remarry.

Key Takeaway
When the khul' dower is unknown, the wife's obligation is determined by a set of default rules that aim to honor the husband's consent while dealing with uncertainty.

Khul' with a Slave Whose Safety Unknown: Corrupt Condition Does Not Invalidate
Ruling on khul' with a runaway slave and a condition of no liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when khul' dower is a runaway slave with a condition of no liability, and explain why the condition is corrupt yet the khul' remains valid.

Core Idea
In khul', a corrupt condition does not invalidate the contract; the wife must deliver the dower or its value.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in khul' (divorce by redemption) where the wife offers a runaway slave as dower and stipulates she is not liable if the slave cannot be found. The key legal question is whether this condition affects the validity of the khul' and what the wife must do. Understanding this ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that corrupt conditions in compensatory contracts are void but the contract itself stands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its core elements
The act is khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation). The dower is a slave that is 'abiq' (runaway, location unknown). The wife stipulates that she is free from liability if the slave is not found.
2
Determine the ruling on the condition
The condition of immunity from liability is considered 'shart fasid' (corrupt condition) in Hanafi law for compensatory transactions like khul'. It is invalid because it contradicts the nature of the exchange—the wife must deliver the dower or its equivalent.
The text states: 'فإنّ شرط البراء في المعاوضات فاسد' (the condition of immunity in compensations is corrupt).
3
Analyze the effect on the contract
Despite the corrupt condition, the khul' itself remains valid. In Hanafi law, corrupt conditions in mu'amalat do not invalidate the core contract; they are simply voided. The wife must fulfill the essence of the contract.
The text: 'وإنما يصح الخلع؛ لأنه مما لا يبطلُ بالشروط الفاسدة بل تفسد هي' (khul' is valid because it is not invalidated by corrupt conditions; rather, they become void).
4
Identify the obligation of the wife
The wife is obligated (wajib) to hand over the slave if she can locate and deliver it. If she is unable (e.g., the slave remains lost), she must pay the slave's value. This ensures the husband receives compensation equivalent to what was promised.
The text: 'تُسلَّمُهُ إِن قَدَرَت، وقيمته إن عجزت' (she hands him over if she can, and if unable, its value).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن اختلعت على عبد لها آيق على براءتها من ضمانه، تُسلَّمُهُ إِن قَدَرَت، وقيمته إن عجزت [١]قوله: على براءتها؛ يعني بشرط أنها بريئة منه، بمعنى أنها لا تطالب بتحصيله وتسليمه، بل إن وجدَ تُسَلِّمهُ إليه وإلا شيء عليها. [٢]قوله: تسلّمه؛ أي وجب عليها أن تُسَلَّمَ العبد إلى الزوج إن قدرت عليه، وإن عجزت وجبت عليها أداء قيمته، ولا يعتبر بشرطهما الفاسد، فإنّ شرط البراء في المعاوضات فاسد، وإنما يصح الخلع؛ لأنه مما لا يبطلُ بالشروط الفاسدة بل تفسد هي.
And if she took khul' for a slave of hers that is 'abiq' (runaway/fugitive) on condition of her being free from liability for it, she hands him over if she can, and if she is unable, she pays its value. [1] His statement: on her being free; meaning on condition that she is free from it, i.e., she is not required to procure it and hand it over; rather, if it is found, she hands it over to him, otherwise nothing is upon her. [2] His statement: she hands him over; meaning it is obligatory upon her to hand over the slave to the husband if she is able; if she is unable, she must pay its value. Their corrupt condition is not considered, for the condition of immunity in compensations is corrupt. The khul' is valid because it is not invalidated by corrupt conditions; rather, they become void.

Commentary
This passage discusses a khul' where the dower is a slave of the wife that has run away ('abiq). The condition is that she is not liable if the slave cannot be found. The ruling is that if she can find and hand over the slave, she must do so. If she cannot, she must pay the value of the slave. The condition of her being free from liability is corrupt (fasid) because it contradicts the nature of a compensatory transaction; however, the khul' itself remains valid. In Hanafi law, a valid contract is not invalidated by a corrupt condition; rather, the condition is nullified. This is an important principle in mu'amalat.

Key Terms
آبق (abiq): A slave who has run away and whose whereabouts are unknown.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is legally invalid (corrupt) but does not invalidate the core contract if it is part of a compensatory transaction like khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) She must pay the value of the slave.
C) The khul' is invalid and she must return the dower.
D) She must give the husband a different slave.

Key Takeaway
In khul', a corrupt condition (like no liability for delivery) does not invalidate the contract; the wife must deliver the dower or pay its value.

Khul' for Three Divorces: Divisibility of Compensation
Inter-madhab dispute on divisibility of compensation in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the divisibility of compensation in khul' and evaluate the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In a khul' offer for three divorces, only the first divorce triggers payment; subsequent divorces are raj'iy without compensation per Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines a common scenario in khul': the wife offers a lump sum for three divorces, but the husband divorces only once. The key dispute is whether the compensation is divisible per divorce. Abu Hanifa treats the offer as a package, while the Sahibayn treat each divorce independently. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how subsequent divorces are classified and the financial obligations involved.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa when the wife offers a sum for three divorces and the husband divorces once.
The first divorce is ba'in with one-third of the sum; the second divorce (if later) is raj'iy with no payment.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
State the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on the same scenario.
They hold that each subsequent divorce is also ba'in with its one-third share.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the reasoning of the Sahibayn: parts of the compensation are divisible on parts of the compensated.
They analogize to the sale of two slaves: if one is lost, half the price is due.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain Abu Hanifa's counter-argument: parts of the condition (three divorces) are not divisible on parts of the conditioned.
The offer was a single package; once partially executed, the remaining divorce is without consideration.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of the disagreement for a second divorce.
Under Abu Hanifa, the wife owes nothing and the divorce is raj'iy; under Sahibayn, she owes another one-third and it is ba'in.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن طلبت ثلاثاً بألف أو على ألف درهم فطلقها واحدة تقع في الأولى بائنة بثلث الألف وفي الثانية رجعية بلا شيء عند أبي حنيفة عندهما فيقع بائنُ بثُلث الألف. فإنها إذا قالت: طلقني ثلاثاً بألف جعلت الألف عوضاً للثلاث، فإذا طلقها واحدة يجب ثلث الألف؛ لأنَّ أجزاء العوض منقسمة على أجزاء المعوض. [٤] قوله: تقع؛ أي إن طلقها في مجلسه فلو قامَ فطلقها لم يجب شيء عليها؛ لأنه معاوضة من جانبها، فيشترط في قبوله المجلس. [0] قوله: بائنة ... الخ؛ أما كونها بائنة فلكونها بمقابلة المال، والطلاق بعوض يكون بائناً كالخلع، وأما وجوب ثلث الألف عليها؛ فلأنها جعلت الألف بمقابلة ثلاث تطليقات، وقد طلقها واحدة والواحد ثلث الثلاث، فيجب عليها ثلث الألف. And if she asks for three [divorces] for a thousand or upon a thousand dirhams, and he divorces her [with] one, the first falls as ba'in with one-third of the thousand, and the second as raj'iy without anything according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it falls as ba'in with one-third of the thousand. For if she says: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand,' she makes the thousand compensation for the three. [4] His statement: it falls; i.e., if he divorces her in his session; if he stood up and then divorced her, nothing is due upon her because it is a compensation from her side, so the session is required for acceptance. Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The scenario: the wife says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand dirhams' or 'upon a thousand dirhams,' implying the sum is for all three. The husband divorces her only once. All agree that the first divorce is ba'in (irrevocable) and she owes one-third of the thousand, because the compensation is divisible proportionally—the divorce in exchange for money is like khul'. However, according to Abu Hanifa, if he later divorces her a second time (in a different session), that second divorce is raj'iy (revocable) and she owes nothing, because the original offer was for three as a package; the parts of the condition (three divorces) are not divisible in his view. The Sahibayn hold that any subsequent divorce also becomes ba'in with one-third each, because each divorce is considered separately. The commentary clarifies that the session requirement applies: if the husband does not divorce in the same session, the offer lapses and no compensation is due. The example of selling two slaves illustrates divisibility: if one is lost, half the price is due.

Key Terms
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce where husband cannot take back wife without new marriage contract and dower.
رجعي (raj'iy): Revocable divorce where husband can take back wife during waiting period without new contract.
مجلس (majlis): Session of offer and acceptance; offer must be accepted in same session to be binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is ba'in and she owes another one-third.
B) It is raj'iy and she owes nothing.
C) It is ba'in and she owes the full remaining two-thirds.
D) It is invalid and the husband must remarry her.

Key Takeaway
In a khul' offer for multiple divorces, the divisibility of the condition determines whether subsequent divorces carry compensation; Abu Hanifa treats the condition as indivisible, the Sahibayn as divisible.

The Meaning of 'على' in Conditional Khul': An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'على'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the interpretation of 'على' in a wife's khul' request, explain the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view, and evaluate the counter-argument of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When a wife says 'Divorce me thrice for a thousand,' the word 'على' makes it a condition: no condition fulfilled, no money owed.

This passage explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the meaning of the word 'على' when a wife offers money for a divorce. The central question is whether partial fulfillment of the condition (one divorce instead of three) creates a partial financial obligation. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it does not, because a condition is indivisible. His two companions disagree. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi approach to conditional contracts and the importance of precise language in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the disputed word
The wife says 'طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف' and the husband divorces only once. The word 'على' is the key term in dispute: does it indicate a condition (shart) or an exchange (mu'awada)?
2
Contrast the positions
Abu Hanifa says 'على' indicates a condition; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) say it indicates exchange.
3
Examine the reasoning for condition
A condition does not divide into parts corresponding to parts of the conditioned. Example: half sunrise does not create half daytime. Similarly, wudu is a condition for prayer; half wudu does not enable half prayer.
4
Examine the reasoning for exchange
The Sahibayn argue that 'على' can be used like 'باء' for exchange, as in sale ('بعت على ألف'). Thus, partial fulfillment should trigger proportional compensation.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and the thamarah
Divorce can be conditioned (unlike sale), so there is no need to reinterpret 'على'. The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, nothing is owed; under Sahibayn, one-third is owed. The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما إذا قالت : طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف فكلمة على للشرط، والطلاق يصح تعليقه بالشرط، فأبو حنيفة له يحملها عليه ، وأجزاء الشَّرط لا تنقسم على أجزاء المشروط
والسر فيه : أن المعاوضة والمقابلة تكون بجعل المجموع عوضاً للمجموع ، فبالضرورة تنقسم أجزاؤه على أجزائه، بخلاف الشرط، فإنّه ما يتوقف عليه وجود المشروط، وهو الجزاء، وليس مقابلاً به ولا عوضاً . عنه ، فلا ينقسم بانقسامه.
ألا ترى أنّ قولنا : إذا كانت الشمس طالعة فالنهارُ موجود يدلّ على لزوم وجود النهار لطلوع الشمس، ولا يمكن أن يوجد نصف النهار بنصف الطلوع، وكذا الوضوء شرط لصحة الصلاة، ولا يمكن تحقق نصف الصلاة بنصف الوضوء.
[١]قوله : فكلمة على للشرط أي قد تستعمل في معنى يفهم منه كون ما بعدها شرطاً لما قبلها ، كقوله : يُبا يعنَكَ عَلَى أَن لا يُشْرِكُن بِاللَّهِ شَيْئًا (١) أي بشرط عدم الإشراك ، وكونها للشرط بمنزلة الحقيقة عند الفقهاء لأنها في أصل الموضع للإلزام، والجزاء لازم للشرط. كذا في «التلويح".
[٢] قوله : يحملها أي يحملُ كلمة «على» في باب الطلاق على معناه الأصلي، وهو الشرط لاستقامته.
[۳] قوله : لا تنقسم قال التفتازاني في «التلويح»: تحقيق ذلك أن ثبوت العوض مع المعوّض من باب المقابلة، حتى يثبت كلّ جزء من هذا في مقابلة كلّ جزء من ذلك ، ويمتنع تقدم أحدهما على الآخر، بمنزلة المتضايفين.
وثبوت المشروط والشرط بطريق المعاقبة ضرورة توقف المشروط على الشرط من غير عكس، فلو انقسم أجزاء الشرط على أجزاء المشروط لزم تقدم جزء من المشروط على الشرط ، فلا تتحقق المعاقبة.
وأما إذا قالت : طلقني ثلاثاً بألف فطلقها واحدة، يجب ثلث الألف لأنَّ الباءَ للمعاوضة والمقابلة، فيثبت التوزيع. (الممتحنة : من الآية ١٢). (التلويح ١ : 219).
As for when she says: 'Divorce me thrice for one thousand,' the word 'ala (upon) indicates a condition, and divorce can be suspended on a condition. Abu Hanifa - may Allah have mercy on him - interprets it as such, and the parts of the condition do not divide over the parts of the conditioned. The reason is that exchange and counter-exchange involve making the whole a substitute for the whole, so necessarily its parts divide over its parts, unlike the condition, which is that upon which the existence of the conditioned (i.e., the result) depends, and is not in exchange for it nor a substitute for it, so it does not divide by its division. Do you not see that our saying: 'If the sun has risen, then daytime exists' indicates the necessary existence of daytime upon sunrise, and half of daytime cannot exist by half of sunrise. Similarly, wudu is a condition for the validity of prayer, and half of prayer cannot be realized by half of wudu. [1] His saying: 'The word 'ala indicates a condition' means it is sometimes used in a sense that implies that what follows it is a condition for what precedes it, as in His saying: 'They pledge allegiance to you upon [the condition] that they do not associate anything with Allah' (Quran 60:12), i.e., on the condition of not associating partners. And it being for a condition is like a literal meaning according to the jurists because in its original context it is for obligation, and the result is necessary for the condition. So it is in 'al-Talwih'. [2] His saying: 'He interprets it' means he interprets the word 'ala in the chapter of divorce according to its original meaning, which is condition, for its correctness. [3] His saying: 'does not divide' - al-Taftazani said in 'al-Talwih': The reality of this is that the establishment of a compensation with the compensated is a matter of exchange, such that every part of this is established in exchange for every part of that, and it is impossible for one to precede the other, similar to correlatives. The establishment of the conditioned and the condition is by way of consequentiality, due to the necessity of the conditioned depending on the condition without the reverse. So if the parts of the condition divided over the parts of the conditioned, it would necessitate a part of the conditioned preceding the condition, so consequentiality would not be realized. And as for when she says: 'Divorce me thrice for one thousand' (using the letter ba), and he divorces her once, one-third of the thousand is obligatory, because the ba indicates exchange and counter-exchange, so distribution is established. (Quran 60:12) (al-Talwih 1:219).
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of the word 'على' (upon/on) when a wife says to her husband: 'طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف' (Divorce me thrice for a thousand). The ruling is that if the husband divorces her once, she owes nothing of the thousand according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the word 'على' establishes a condition, not an exchange. The condition—that the full thousand be given for three divorces—is not fulfilled by a single divorce, so no financial obligation arises. Imam Abu Hanifa reasons that a condition does not divide into parts corresponding to the parts of the conditioned thing (the divorce). He contrasts this with exchange ('معاوضة'), where the whole consideration is divided proportionally; for example, if she says 'بألف' (with the letter ba), the ba indicates exchange, so if he divorces once, she owes one-third of the thousand. The commentary from 'al-Talwih' supports this by citing Quranic usage (60:12) where 'على' indicates a condition. Al-Taftazani's explanation emphasizes that in exchange, parts are reciprocal, but in a condition, the conditioned depends entirely on the condition, so partial fulfillment does not obligate partial compensation. The passage also distinguishes between sale (which does not accept suspension on a condition) and divorce (which does). Thus, Abu Hanifa's position is that no money is due for one divorce under 'على'. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that 'على' here also implies exchange, similar to 'باء', so she would owe one-third. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, as the text indicates.

Key Terms
على (ala): In this passage, 'على' is interpreted as indicating a condition (shart) for the occurrence of divorce, not as an exchange (mu'awada).
شرط (shart): A condition upon which the existence of the divorce depends; the divorce is suspended until the condition is fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife says to her husband 'طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف' and he divorces her once, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa?
A) She owes one-third of the thousand.
B) She owes nothing.
C) She owes the full thousand.
D) The divorce is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The preposition 'على' in a wife's conditional divorce request establishes a condition, not an exchange, so partial fulfillment does not require partial payment.

Ruling on Delegating Three Divorces for a Full Thousand: Partial Divorce
Explaining the consequence of delegating three divorces for a thousand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa holds that no divorce occurs when the wife divorces once under a delegation of three for a full thousand, and contrast this with the Sahibayn's view regarding the interpretation of 'على'.

Core Idea
Delegation for a full amount is conditional: partial performance does not constitute consent.

When a husband delegates three divorces for a full thousand dirhams, his consent is tied to receiving the entire amount. If the wife divorces only once, the condition is not met. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling and the counter-argument from the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), focusing on the linguistic and contractual interpretation of 'على'.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa: when the husband says 'Divorce yourself three times for a thousand' and she divorces once, no divorce occurs. Understand the basis: the husband's delegation is conditional on the full amount.
The key is that the husband did not consent to separation unless he receives the entire thousand.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's view
Recognize that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that one divorce does occur and she owes one-third of the thousand. Their reasoning interprets 'على' as meaning exchange (like 'باء') based on context, similar to a sale.
They treat the delegation as an exchange (mu'awada) that can be split proportionally.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
Trace their argument: in sale contracts, 'على' is used as 'باء' meaning exchange, and since divorce for money is also an exchange, 'على' should be interpreted similarly. Thus, one divorce is valid and she owes a proportional part.
They rely on the context of compensation to override the literal conditional meaning.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine Abu Hanifa's rebuttal: sale does not accept being suspended on a condition, so interpreting 'على' as exchange is necessary there to validate the contract. Divorce, however, does accept conditions (ta'liq), so there is no necessity to reinterpret 'على'. The literal meaning (condition) is retained, and the husband's condition of the full thousand is not fulfilled by one divorce.
This distinction between sale (mu'awada mahda) and divorce (isqat) is central.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the wife remains married and owes nothing; under the Sahibayn, she is divorced once and must pay one-third of the thousand. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
This difference affects financial obligations and marital status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قال : طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً بألف أو على ألف فطلقت واحدة لم يقع شيء
[1] وأبو يوسف ومحمد الله حملاه على العوض، بمعنى الباء، كما في بعتُ عبداً بألف ، أو على ألف. فالجواب : أن البيع لا أن البيع لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط، فيحمل على العوض
[2] ضرورة، ولا ضرورة في الطلاق لصحة تعليقه بالشرط. (وإن قال : طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً بألف ، أو على ألف فطلقت واحدةً لم يقع شيء) لأن الزوج لم يرضَ بالبينونة إلا أن تسلّم له الألف كلها ولو قالت : طلقني وضرتها على ألف، فطلقها واحداً يجب ما يَخُصها من الألف لأنها للمقابلة بدلالة الحال إذ لو حمل على الشرط كان البدل كله عليها). [ ] قوله : حملاه ... الخ قال في «التلويح»: لأنَّ الطلاق على المال معاوضةٌ من جانب المرأة ، ولهذا كان لها الرجوع قبل كلام الزوج، وكلمة على تحتمل معنى «الباء»، فيحمل عليها بدلالة الحال، وعنده للشرط على الحقيقة.
[2] قوله : فالجواب أي من قبل أبي حنيفة له ، وحاصله : أن حمل كلمة «على» في صورة البيع على «الباء» للضرورة، وهي أنّ البيع من المعاوضات المحضة الخالية عن معنى الإسقاط ، كالإجارة والنكاح وغيرهما، وهي لا تقبل التعليق بالشرط، فتحمل هناك كلمة «على» على معنى «الباء»، وهو المعاوضة صحيحاً للعقد، فإنّ المعاوضات تفسدُ بالتعليق بالشرط ، ولا كذلك الطلاق ، فإنّه مسن الإسقاطات، وهي تقبلُ التعليق بالشرط ، فلا ضرورة فيه إلى حمل على على غير معناه الحقيقي.
[3] قوله : لأن ... الخ حاصله : أنّ الزوج فوَّض إليها الطلقات الثلاث لا بل بعوض الألف أو بشرط أداء الألف بتمامه ، فلم يرض بالبينونة إلا أن يحصل له الألف كلّه، ولا يحصل ذلك إذا طلقت واحدة، بل يجب عليها حينئذ ثلث الألف فقط في الصورتين أو في الأولى فقط، فكان تطليقها الواحدة من غير تفويضه فلا يقع شيء. (انتهى من «التلويح» ١ : 219-220).
And if he says: 'Divorce yourself thrice for a thousand (bā') or upon a thousand (alā),' and she divorces once, nothing occurs. [1] Abu Yusuf and Muhammad - may Allah have mercy on them - interpret it as an exchange, in the sense of the letter bā', as in 'I sold a slave for a thousand (bi-alf) or upon a thousand (alā alf).' The response is that sale [2] cannot be suspended on a condition, so it is necessarily interpreted as an exchange, and there is no necessity in divorce because it can be suspended on a condition. (And if he says: 'Divorce yourself thrice for a thousand (bā') or upon a thousand (alā),' and she divorces once, nothing occurs) because the husband did not consent to separation unless she hands over the entire thousand to him. And if she says: 'Divorce me and my co-wife for a thousand,' and he divorces one of them, what is specific to her from the thousand is obligatory because it is for exchange by indication of the context; for if it were interpreted as a condition, the entire consideration would be upon her. [ ] His saying: 'They interpret it ...' etc. He said in 'al-Talwih': Because divorce for money is an exchange from the woman's side, therefore she has the right to withdraw before the husband's speech, and the word 'alā can carry the meaning of 'bā',' so it is interpreted as such by context. According to him (Abu Hanifa), it is a condition literally. [2] His saying: 'The response' is from Abu Hanifa, and its summary is that interpreting the word 'alā in the case of sale as 'bā' is due to necessity, because sale is a pure exchange devoid of the meaning of rescission, like leasing, marriage, etc., and it does not accept suspension on a condition. So there, the word 'alā is interpreted as 'bā' meaning exchange, to validate the contract, because exchanges are invalidated by suspension on a condition. Divorce is different because it is from the category of rescissions, which accept suspension on a condition, so there is no necessity to interpret 'alā away from its literal meaning. [3] His saying: 'Because ...' etc. Its summary is that the husband delegated to her the three divorces only in exchange for the full thousand or on condition of paying the entire thousand. So he did not consent to separation unless he gets the entire thousand, and that does not happen if she divorces once. Rather, in that case only one-third of the thousand would be due in both scenarios or only in the first, so her single divorce was not within his delegation, so nothing occurs. (End from 'al-Talwih' 1:219-220).
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where the husband says to his wife: 'طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً بألف أو على ألف' (Divorce yourself three times for a thousand or upon a thousand). If she then divorces herself once, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no divorce occurs. The reason is that the husband authorized only three divorces in exchange for the full thousand or on condition of paying the full thousand. He did not agree to separation unless he receives the entire amount. A single divorce would not give him the full thousand, so it is not within the scope of his delegation; thus the divorce is ineffective. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree: they interpret the word 'على' here as meaning exchange (like 'باء'), similar to a sale, so they hold that one divorce should occur and she owes one-third of the thousand. However, the text refutes them by distinguishing sale from divorce: sale cannot be suspended on a condition, so interpreting 'على' as exchange is necessary there, but divorce can be suspended on a condition, so no necessity to reinterpret it. Moreover, the context indicates that the husband specified three divorces for the full amount, so partial performance is not accepted. The commentary from 'al-Talwih' stresses that the wife can even withdraw before the husband's acceptance if it is an exchange, but here the husband's words are a delegation. The final ruling is that a single divorce does not take effect, and she owes nothing (or in some interpretations, only one-third but still the divorce is invalid because it was not authorized). The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, which is that no divorce occurs.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwid): Delegation by the husband to the wife to divorce herself, subject to specified conditions or exchange.
بدل (badal): The consideration (the thousand) given in exchange for the divorce; here it is a condition for the full three divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the ruling if a husband says 'Divorce yourself three times for a thousand' and she divorces once?
A) One divorce occurs and she owes one-third.
B) No divorce occurs.
C) Three divorces occur and she owes the full thousand.
D) The marriage becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband delegates three divorces for a full thousand, a single divorce is ineffective because the condition of full payment is not met; the mufta bihi is that no divorce occurs.

Interpretation of 'Ala in Khul' Delegation: Condition or Compensation?
Dispute over interpretation of 'on a thousand' in divorce delegation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the interpretation of 'ala in khul' delegation and explain why Abu Hanifa rejects the Sahibayn's analogy to sale.

Core Idea
In divorce, 'ala retains its literal condition meaning; no necessity to reinterpret as compensation.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the meaning of the word 'ala (upon) in a husband's delegation of divorce to his wife. When the husband says 'Divorce yourself three times upon a thousand,' and the wife divorces only once, does a divorce occur? Abu Hanifa says no, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes, with proportional compensation. The disagreement hinges on whether 'ala is interpreted literally as a condition or as compensation, and whether the analogy to sale is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband delegates divorce to the wife using the phrase 'upon a thousand' (على ألف). Determine the legal issue: whether the word 'ala indicates a condition or compensation.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
According to Abu Hanifa, no divorce occurs because the condition of paying the full thousand was not met. The word 'ala retains its literal meaning of condition.
The matn favors this view.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad interpret 'ala as compensation (like 'ba'), so one divorce occurs and the wife owes one-third of the thousand.
They analogize to sale.
4
Analyze the proof and rebuttal
Sahibayn argue that 'ala indicates compensation, as in sale. Abu Hanifa rebuts: sale cannot be conditioned, so the reinterpretation is forced; divorce can be conditioned, so no necessity.
The key distinction is whether the contract accepts conditions.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the wife remains married; under Sahibayn, she is divorced with a debt. This affects inheritance, remarriage, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قال : طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً بألف أو على ألف فطلقت واحدة لم يقع شيء، وأبو يوسف ومحمد الله حملاه على العوض، بمعنى الباء، كما في بعتُ عبداً بألف ، أو على ألف. فالجواب : أن البيع لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط، فيحمل على العوض ضرورة، ولا ضرورة في الطلاق لصحة تعليقه بالشرط. قوله : حملاه ... الخ ؛ قال في «التلويح»: لأنَّ الطلاق على المال معاوضةٌ من جانب المرأة ، ولهذا كان لها الرجوع قبل كلام الزوج، وكلمة على تحتمل معنى «الباء»، فيحمل عليها بدلالة الحال، وعنده للشرط على الحقيقة). قوله : فالجواب ؛ أي من قبل أبي حنيفة له ، وحاصله : أن حمل كلمة «على» في صورة البيع على «الباء» للضرورة، وهي أنّ البيع من المعاوضات المحضة الخالية عن معنى الإسقاط ، كالإجارة والنكاح وغيرهما، وهي لا تقبل التعليق بالشرط، فتحمل هناك كلمة «على» على معنى «الباء»، وهو المعاوضة صحيحاً للعقد، فإنّ المعاوضات تفسدُ بالتعليق بالشرط ، ولا كذلك الطلاق ، فإنّه مسن الإسقاطات، وهي تقبلُ التعليق بالشرط ، فلا ضرورة فيه إلى حمل على على غير معناه مطلقاً، الحقيقي. قوله : لأن ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أنّ الزوج فوَّض إليها الطلقات الثلاث لا بل بعوض الألف أو بشرط أداء الألف بتمامه ، فلم يرض بالبينونة إلا أن يحصل له الألف كلّه، ولا يحصل ذلك إذا طلقت واحدة، بل يجب عليها حينئذ ثلث الألف فقط في الصورتين أو في الأولى فقط، فكان تطليقها الواحدة من غير تفويضه فلا يقع شيء. بخلاف قولها " طلقني ثلاثاً بألف ؛ لأنَّها لما رضيت بالبينونة بألف ، فهي أرضى بالبينونة ببعضها. فإن قلت : قد يكون لها غرض في الثلاث حسماً لمادة رجوعه إليها لشدّة بغضه، فلا تكون راضية بالبينونة الحاصلة بما دون الثلاث. قلت : هذا لا اعتبار له بعد حصول أصل المقصود بملكها نفسها.
And if he said: 'Divorce yourself three times for a thousand or upon a thousand' and she divorced herself once, nothing occurs. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) interpreted it as compensation, meaning the letter 'ba', as in 'I sold a slave for a thousand' or 'upon a thousand'. The answer: that sale cannot be suspended on a condition, so it is interpreted as compensation out of necessity, and there is no necessity in divorce because it can be suspended on a condition. His statement: 'they interpreted it...' etc.; it is said in al-Talwih: because divorce for money is a transaction from the woman's side, therefore she can retract before the husband's speech, and the word 'ala' can mean 'ba', so it is interpreted accordingly by contextual indication, while according to him it is for the condition literally. His statement: 'the answer'; that is from Abu Hanifa to him, and its summary: that interpreting the word 'ala' in the case of sale as 'ba' is out of necessity, because sale is a pure transaction devoid of the meaning of relinquishment, like lease and marriage and others, and it does not accept suspension on a condition, so there the word 'ala' is interpreted as 'ba', which is valid compensation for the contract, for transactions are invalidated by suspension on a condition, but divorce is not so, for it is from the category of relinquishments, and they accept suspension on a condition, so there is no necessity to interpret 'ala' in other than its literal meaning at all. His statement: 'Because...' etc.; its summary: the husband delegated the three divorces to her only with compensation of a thousand or with the condition of paying the full thousand, so he did not consent to the separation unless he obtains the entire thousand, and that is not achieved if she divorces once; rather, she then owes only one-third of a thousand in both cases or only in the first case, so her divorcing once without his authorization results in nothing occurring. Contrary to her saying: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand', because when she consented to separation for a thousand, she is more consenting to separation for part of it. If you say: she might have an interest in three divorces to cut off the possibility of his return due to intense hatred, so she would not consent to separation obtained by less than three. I say: this is not considered after the attainment of the basic objective of possessing herself.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of the word 'ala (upon) in the context of khul' (divorce by compensation). The matn states that if a husband delegates divorce to his wife saying 'divorce yourself three times for a thousand' (with 'ba) or 'upon a thousand' (with 'ala), and she divorces herself only once, no divorce occurs according to the author (Abu Hanifa). The two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, interpret 'ala as meaning 'ba' (with), similar to the phrase 'I sold a slave for a thousand' or 'upon a thousand', implying compensation. The commentary explains Abu Hanifa's position: in sales, the word 'ala is interpreted as 'ba out of necessity because sales cannot be conditioned, but divorce can be conditioned, so no necessity to reinterpret. The husband's intent was to obtain the full thousand in exchange for all three divorces; a single divorce does not satisfy that, so it is as if she acted without permission and no divorce falls. The passage then addresses an objection: why not contrast this with the case where the wife asks for three divorces for a thousand and the husband gives one? There, she is deemed consenting to separation for a third, so one divorce would occur. The answer is that her request for three shows she is willing to accept separation for any portion.

Key Terms
على (‘alā): In this passage, it is a preposition that can mean either 'upon' (condition) or 'with' (compensation), depending on context.
الخلع (al-khul‘): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does no divorce occur when the husband says 'Divorce yourself three times upon a thousand' and the wife divorces once?
A) Because the wife did not pay the full thousand.
B) Because the word 'ala means condition, and the condition of three divorces was not met.
C) Because the husband intended compensation, not condition.
D) Because the wife did not consent to the divorce.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the word 'ala in a husband's delegation of khul' is interpreted as a condition, not compensation, because divorce accepts conditions, unlike sale.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Divorce or Manumission Conditional on a Debt: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Waw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the phrase 'You are divorced and you owe one thousand,' and explain the linguistic basis for their disagreement.

Core Idea
The conjunctive 'waw' does not create a condition; only a circumstantial interpretation does.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over a single phrase. At stake is whether a husband's statement 'You are divorced, and you owe one thousand' constitutes an unconditional divorce or a conditional offer. The disagreement turns on the grammatical role of the letter waw (و).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
State the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the legal effect of the husband's statement. Note that according to Abu Hanifa the divorce/manumission occurs immediately without any payment; according to the Sahibayn it occurs only if the wife/slave accepts the debt.
2
Locate the contested phrase
Identify the exact Arabic phrase being discussed: 'أنت طالق وعليك ألف' (You are divorced, and you owe one thousand). The key is the conjunction 'wa' (و) connecting the two clauses.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's argument
Explain that the Sahibayn interpret the waw as a circumstantial clause (hal) or as standing for the 'ba' of exchange, making the second clause a condition. Therefore, the divorce is contingent upon the wife's acceptance and payment.
The text mentions two reasons: hal acts like a condition, and such phrasing is used in exchange transactions.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's argument
Explain that Abu Hanifa takes the waw in its primary conjunctive sense (atf). The second clause is an independent statement of fact; the husband simply informs her of a debt. There is no condition, so the divorce takes effect immediately regardless of acceptance.
Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that conjunction is the original meaning of waw and deviation requires necessity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Identify the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa the wife gets divorced immediately and owes nothing; under the Sahibayn she must accept and pay for the divorce to occur. Note that the later fatwa (mufta bihi) follows the Sahibayn.
The tarjih authority (e.g., Al-Hawi) states that bihima yufta—fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn.

ولم تسلم بخلاف قولها " طلقني ثلاثاً بألف ؛ لأنَّها لما رضيت بالبينونة بألف ، فهي أرضى بالبينونة ببعضها. [٢]قوله : جعلا ... الخ ؛ وجه مذهبهما بوجهين : أحدهما : ما ذكره الشارح، وحاصله : إنّ «الواو» قد تجيء للحال، والحال بمنزلة الشرط في مقارنته مع ذي الحال، وتوقفه عليه بوجه ما ، فكان معنى قوله لزوجته: أنت طالق وعليك ألف ، أنت طالق حال كون الألف لازماً عليك، فإن قبلت وقع الطلاق، ولزم المال، وإن لم تقبل فلا وقوع ولا لزوم، وقس عليه قوله لأمته : «أنت حرّة ، وعليك ألف»، أو لعبده : «أنت حر وعليك ألف». وثانيهما : إنّ مثل هذا الكلام يستعمل في المعاوضة ، يقال : احمل هذا المتاع ولك درهم بمنزلة قوله بدرهم، فتحملُ (الواو) هاهنا على معنى «الباء» بدلالة حال المعاوضة، فكان كقوله : أنت طالق وأنت حرّة بألف.
[٣]قوله : جعل الواو للعطف ; فكان قوله : وعليك ألف» جملة مستقلة معطوفة وتناسب الجملتين في كونهما اسميتين يدلُّ على العطف ، فيكون إخباراً بأن عليهما الألف، فيقع بلا شيء. (والخلعُ: معاوضة" في حقها على قوله : أنت طالق أو أنت حرّة، فلا يفيد الكلام تعليق الطلاق بالألف، ولا تعويضه به، فيقع الطلاق مجاناً قبلته أو لم تقبله ، واتفقوا على أنها للحال في : «أد إليّ ألفاً وأنت حرّ ; لتعذر عطف الخبر على الإنشاء، وعلى أنّها بمعنى «باء» المعاوضة في : احمل هذا ولك درهم ; لأنَّ المعاوضة في الإجارة أصلية. وعلى تعين العطف في قول المضارب : خذ هذا المال واعمـل بـه في البز، للإنشائية، فلا تتقيّد المضاربه به وعلى احتمال الأمرين في : أنت طالق وأنت مريضة أو مصلية، إذ لا مانع ولا معيّن فتنجيز الطلاق قضاء ويتعلق ديانة إن نواه. كذا في «البحر»(1). [١]قوله : على العطف ; أشار به إلى أنّ العطف معناه الأصلي، فلا يعدل عنه إلا لضرورة، كعدم تناسب الجملتين، فلا يصح العطف أو لا يستحسن، وهاهنا وُجِدَ التناسب، فيرجح ذلك العطف. (٢) قوله : فيكون ; أي يكون قوله : وعليك ألف إخباراً بكون الألف عليها، وبإخباره سواء كان صادقاً أو كاذباً لا يلزمُ شيء عليها ، والقبول إنما يفيد في اللزوم إذا كان جواباً للإنشاء. [٣]قوله : معاوضة ; ولهذا لا يصح الخلع إذا لقنها بالعربية: اختلعت منك بكذا، وهي لا تعلم معناه، فإنّ العلم بالمعنى شرط في صحة المعاوضات(٢). كذا في «الفتح». [٤]قوله : في حقها ; أي هو معاوضة من جانب المرأة ; لأنها تملكه المال بعوض الطلاق، ويدل عليه قوله الله في بحث الخلع فيما أفندت به (۳) حيث أسند الافتداء إليها.
And if he said: 'You are divorced, and you owe one thousand,' or 'You are free, and you owe one thousand,' whether they accept or not, she is divorced and she is freed without anything. And she is not liable, contrary to her saying 'Divorce me three times for one thousand'; because when she consented to separation for one thousand, she is more consenting to separation for part of it. (And if he said: 'You are divorced, and you owe one thousand,' or 'You are free, and you owe one thousand,' whether they accept or not, she is divorced and she is freed without anything): This is according to Abu Hanifa. As for according to them (the two Sahibayn), if the woman accepts, she is divorced for one thousand; and if the slave-girl accepts, she is freed for one thousand; but if they do not accept, nothing occurs. They made the 'waw' in his saying 'and you owe' as for the circumstantial clause (hal), and the circumstantial clause is like a condition. Abu Hanifa made the 'waw' for conjunction (atf). [1] His saying: 'contrary to her saying...' is a rebuttal of an implied objection. The explanation of the objection: that just as nothing occurs if he divorces less than three here, similarly nothing should occur when she asks for three divorces for one thousand and he divorces one. The gist of the answer: that there she consented to separation for the compensation of one thousand, so she consents to it for one-third by priority. If you say: she might have an interest in three to cut off the possibility of his return due to intense hatred, so she is not content with the separation obtained by less than three. I say: this is not considered after the attainment of the original objective of her ownership of herself. [2] His saying: 'they made...': there are two aspects to their school: First, what the commentator mentioned, and its gist: that the 'waw' may come for the circumstantial clause, and the circumstantial clause is like a condition in its concomitance with the owner of the circumstance and its dependence on it in some way. So the meaning of his saying to his wife 'you are divorced and you owe one thousand' is 'you are divorced while the one thousand is obligatory upon you'; if she accepts, divorce occurs and the money is due; if she does not accept, neither occurrence nor obligation. And analogize to his saying to his slave-girl 'you are free and you owe one thousand' or to his slave 'you are free and you owe one thousand'. Second, that such speech is used in exchange; it is said 'carry this merchandise and you have a dirham' similar to saying 'with a dirham', so the 'waw' here is interpreted in the meaning of the 'ba'' (for compensation) by indication of the context of exchange, so it is as if he said 'you are divorced and you are free for one thousand'. [3] His saying: 'he made the waw for conjunction': so his saying 'and you owe one thousand' is an independent clause conjoined, and the suitability of the two clauses in both being nominal indicates conjunction, so it is informing that she owes one thousand, so divorce occurs without anything. (And khul' is an exchange from her side) on his saying 'you are divorced' or 'you are free', so the speech does not effect the suspension of divorce upon the thousand, nor compensation with it, so divorce occurs gratuitously whether she accepts or not. And they agree that it (the waw) is for the circumstantial clause in 'give me a thousand and you are free' because it is impossible to conjoin a predicate to a command; and that it is in the meaning of the 'ba'' of exchange in 'carry this and you have a dirham' because exchange in hiring is primary. And on the definite conjunction in the saying of the mudarib 'take this capital and trade with it in cloth' due to the imperative nature, so the mudaraba is not restricted. And on the possibility of both in 'you are divorced and you are sick or praying' since there is no impediment nor determinant, so divorce takes effect judicially and is subject to intention regarding religion. As in 'al-Bahr'. [1] His saying: 'on conjunction' indicates that conjunction is the primary meaning, so one does not deviate from it except for necessity, like lack of suitability of the two clauses, so conjunction is invalid or not commendable, and here suitability is found, so conjunction is preferred. (2) His saying: 'so it is' means his saying 'and you owe one thousand' is informing that the thousand is upon her, and by his informing, whether truthful or false, nothing is due upon her, and acceptance only benefits in liability if it is a response to a creative speech. [3] His saying: 'exchange' — for this reason khul' is not valid if he dictates to her in Arabic: 'I have khul'ed myself from you for such-and-such' and she does not know its meaning, for knowledge of the meaning is a condition for the validity of exchanges. As in 'al-Fath'. [4] His saying: 'from her side' means it is an exchange from the woman's side because she gives him money in exchange for divorce, and evidence for it is Allah's saying in the verse on khul' regarding what she ransoms herself with, where He attributed the ransom to her.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific statement: a husband saying to his wife 'You are divorced, and you owe one thousand,' or to his slave-girl 'You are free, and you owe one thousand.' The basic ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa is that the divorce or manumission occurs immediately without any payment, whether the wife or slave-girl accepts or not. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ: if the woman accepts, the divorce occurs and she owes the thousand; if she does not accept, nothing occurs. The disagreement hinges on the interpretation of the conjunctive 'waw' (and). The Sahibayn view the waw as introducing a circumstantial clause (hal), which functions like a condition: the divorce is contingent upon the debt being accepted. They also argue that such phrasing is commonly used in exchange transactions, so it is as if he said 'for one thousand.' Abu Hanifa, however, takes the waw in its primary conjunctive sense, making the second clause an independent statement of fact: the husband merely informs her that she owes one thousand, and the divorce is unconditional. The commentary defends Abu Hanifa's view by noting that conjunction is the original meaning of the waw, and one should not deviate from it without necessity. The suitability of the two nominal clauses supports conjunction. The passage also distinguishes this case from the scenario where a wife asks for three divorces for one thousand and the husband divorces her once. There, the wife's consent to separation for the full amount implies she consents to it for part, so the divorce is valid with a proportional payment. The commentary further refines the rule by indicating that according to later fatwa (mufta bihi), the position of the Sahibayn is followed in practice, though the text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the primary one. Finally, the commentary defines khul' as an exchange from the woman's side, emphasizing that knowledge of the terms is required for validity.

Key Terms
الواو (al-waw): The letter waw used as a conjunction; its interpretation as conjunctive (عطف) or circumstantial (حال) determines the legal effect.
الحال (al-hal): A circumstantial clause that describes the state of the subject; here, the Sahibayn interpret 'and you owe' as a circumstantial clause making the payment a condition.
العطف (al-atf): Grammatical conjunction; here, Abu Hanifa interprets the waw as simply connecting two independent statements.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation; the passage defines it as an exchange from the woman's side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling when a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced, and you owe one thousand'?
A) The divorce occurs only if the wife accepts the debt.
B) The divorce occurs immediately without any payment, regardless of acceptance.
C) The divorce occurs only if she pays one thousand first.
D) The divorce is invalid because the amount is uncertain.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of the word 'wa' (and) as conjunctive or circumstantial determines whether divorce is immediate or conditional, and the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn making it conditional.

The Conjunctive Waw in Khul': When Talaq Falls Freely
Linguistic analysis of the conjunctive waw in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the conjunctive waw in nominal sentences preserves the unconditional nature of talaq and identify the practical consequence when the wife declines payment.

Core Idea
The default conjunction of nominal sentences keeps talaq unconditional; khul's compensation requires a clear exchange wording.

When a husband says 'You are divorced and you are free' (intending khul'), does the talaq depend on the wife's acceptance or payment? This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the Hanafi position: the conjunction 'waw' between two nominal sentences indicates a simple informing, not a condition. Therefore, talaq falls freely even if the wife refuses to pay. We will examine the linguistic reasoning and its practical outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous wording
The husband says 'أنت طالق وعليك ألف' (You are divorced and upon you a thousand). Does the waw make the talaq conditional on the payment?
The two parts are both nominal sentences: 'You are divorced' and 'upon you a thousand'.
2
Apply the Hanafi default rule for waw
Hanafis hold that the original meaning of waw is conjunction (عطف), and one does not deviate from it without necessity. Necessity arises when the two sentences are not suitable for conjunction (e.g., one is a command, the other a report). Here both are nominal, so conjunction is retained.
This rule is explicitly stated in the passage: 'conjunction is the original meaning, so one does not deviate from it except for necessity'.
3
Derive the ruling for khul'
Since the waw is conjunctive, the statement is an informing (إخبار) that talaq has occurred and that a thousand is owed. But informing does not condition talaq on payment. Therefore, talaq falls instantly regardless of whether she accepts to pay.
The phrase 'يقع بلا شيء' (it occurs without anything) summarizes the practical outcome.
4
Distinguish other uses of waw
The passage contrasts four other scenarios: (a) 'Pay me a thousand and you are free' – waw is for immediate execution (li al-hal) because you cannot conjoin a report with a construction; (b) 'Carry this and for you a dirham' – waw is like ba of exchange; (c) mudarib's instruction – waw is purely imperative; (d) 'You are divorced and you are sick' – waw is ambiguous, so talaq is executed judicially but religiously depends on intention.
These distinctions help identify when the default conjunction does not apply.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and thamarah
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'is) may interpret the waw as conditional or as implying compensation. The practical difference: according to Hanafis, talaq falls without compensation; according to others, it does not fall if she refuses to pay.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and supported by the principle that conjunction is the original state.

(والخلعُ: معاوضة" في حقها (4) على قوله : أنت طالق أو أنت حرّة، فلا يفيد الكلام تعليق الطلاق بالألف، ولا تعويضه به، فيقع الطلاق مجاناً قبلته أو لم تقبله ، واتفقوا على أنها للحال في : «أد إليّ ألفاً وأنت حرّ ؛ لتعذر عطف الخبر على الإنشاء، وعلى أنّها بمعنى «باء» المعاوضة في : احمل هذا ولك درهم ؛ لأنَّ المعاوضة في الإجارة أصلية. وعلى تعين العطف في قول المضارب : خذ هذا المال واعمـل بـه في البز، للإنشائية، فلا تتقيّد المضاربه به وعلى احتمال الأمرين في : أنت طالق وأنت مريضة أو مصلية، إذ لا مانع ولا معيّن فتنجيز الطلاق قضاء ويتعلق ديانة إن نواه. كذا في «البحر»(1). [٤]قوله : في حقها ؛ أي هو معاوضة من جانب المرأة ؛ لأنها تملكه المال بعوض الطلاق، ويدل عليه قوله الله في بحث الخلع فيما أفندت به (۳) حيث أسند الافتداء إليها. (۱) «البحر الرائق (٣: ٢٨٥ - ٢٨٦). And the suitability of the two sentences in both being nominal indicates conjunction, so it becomes informing that upon her is the thousand, so it (talaq) occurs without anything. And (khul' is an exchange) on his statement: 'You are divorced or you are free', so the speech does not make talaq conditional upon the thousand, nor compensation with it, so talaq occurs gratis whether she accepts or not. And they agreed that it (the waw) is for the present tense in 'Pay me a thousand and you are free' because it is impossible to conjoin a report with a construction; and that it is in the sense of 'ba' of exchange in 'Carry this and for you a dirham' because exchange in hire is essential. (2) His statement: 'so it becomes' meaning his statement 'and upon you a thousand' is informing that the thousand is upon her, and by his informing, whether truthful or false, nothing is incumbent upon her, and acceptance only benefits in obligation if it is a response to a construction. [3] His statement: 'exchange' therefore khul' is not valid if he dictates to her in Arabic: 'I khul' from you for such-and-such' and she does not know its meaning, for knowledge of the meaning is a condition for the validity of exchanges. Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the nature of the conjunction 'waw' in the wording of khul'. The author explains that when a husband says 'You are divorced and you are free' (intending to make talaq conditional on payment), the conjunction indicates that the two clauses are joined as an informing statement. Thus, it does not condition talaq upon payment nor compensate with it; talaq falls freely regardless of acceptance. The author contrasts this with other uses of 'waw': in 'Pay me a thousand and you are free', it signifies immediate execution (li al-hal); in 'Carry this and for you a dirham', it is equivalent to 'ba' of exchange (as in hire); in the mudarib's instruction, it is purely imperative. For ambiguous cases like 'You are divorced and you are sick', both interpretations are possible, so talaq is executed judicially but relates religiously only if intended. The commentary then refines: conjunction is the original meaning, not deviated from without necessity. The phrase 'معاوضة' (exchange) confirms that khul' is a financial exchange from the woman's side, as she gives wealth for talaq. This is supported by Quran 2:229 where ransoming is attributed to her.

Key Terms
عطف (atf): Grammatical conjunction; joining one clause to another using a conjunctive particle like waw.
معاوضة (mu'awadah): An exchange or commutative contract where each party gives something in return.
إنشاء (insha'): Performative utterance that brings about a legal effect, such as pronouncing talaq or making a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband says 'أنت طالق وعليك ألف' (You are divorced and upon you a thousand), and the wife does not accept any payment, what is the ruling?
A) Talaq does not fall because it was conditional upon payment.
B) Talaq falls validly without any compensation.
C) Talaq falls but the wife must pay something.
D) The statement is invalid and no talaq occurs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: the conjunctive waw in nominal sentences does not make talaq conditional on payment; talaq falls immediately without compensation.
